A future applied result may be described only by a sequence-neutral spec, body recipe, or assigned scalar order, never by its not-yet-computable ObjectId/digest. Self IDs, mutually strong cycles, and an input command that names its own applied result are invalid.

Stored digest fields are never defined by naming convention. Every `durable_fields.toml` digest row declares exactly one semantic class: `TargetDigest` of separately identified bytes, `TranscriptDigest` with a registered transcript recipe, `WeakIdentityDigest`, or `BodyDigest`. A `BodyDigest<T>` row fixes `{domain_separator,schema_major,included_field_tags,excluded_field_tags}`; its default recipe is `BLAKE3(domain_separator || canonical(schema_major, T excluding exactly the one BodyDigest field))`. Signatures, MACs, or other fields are excluded only when the row explicitly lists their stable tags. Unknown exclusions, two body-digest fields, an implicit zero placeholder, or computing over bytes that include the digest itself are G0 errors. Encoder, decoder, field-table, golden-vector, mutation, and cross-version tests all use the same generated recipe. In particular `RaftSnapshot.body_digest`, `ShardHistoryInventory.body_digest`, and `GlobalKeyEnvelopeManifest.body_digest` use registered body transcripts excluding only their own field; `BackupManifest` instead follows its acyclic Body -> SignatureSet -> Manifest construction and contains no self digest.

To avoid the state-root/command-head cycle, canonical state is layered. `LogicalStatePayload` contains the complete semantic state at `{ applied_logical_command_seq, applied_commit_seq }` but no logical-command-head wrapper. `LocalCommandOrigin` is the closed union `Prior{predecessor:ConditionalCommandRef}|RecoveryBridge{bridge_spec_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryBridgeSpec>,source_manifest_identity:WeakDigest,transform_and_projection_digest}`. After deterministic apply has constructed every result object and the payload, it creates `LogicalCommandRecord { logical_command_seq, origin:LocalCommandOrigin, command:StrongRef<CommitCommand|ControlCommand>, transaction_marker:StrongMarkerRef?, logical_command_hlc, resulting_state_payload_digest:WeakDigest }`. Normal work requires `Prior`; only the first guarded restore command may use `RecoveryBridge`. It then creates `LogicalStateRoot { payload_ref:StrongRef<LogicalStatePayload>, logical_command_head:StrongCommandRef? }`; fresh genesis alone has no head. The payload digest cross-checks the sibling object; it is not a reachability edge. Thus the final root commits both the complete state and its transition record without either object naming a future ObjectId. Checkpoint cuts are the only normal predecessor-reclamation boundary. Each canonical `CommitMarker` is independently encoded and hashed before packing. `MarkerRef { marker_oid, commit_seq }` is the transaction-history identity used by branch heads, version origins/retirements, checkpoints, MMR leaves, and merges. A `MarkerBatch` merely packs length-delimited marker bytes; the object-location index maps each marker OID to its authenticated `(batch_encoding, offset, length)` subobject locator. Objects are assembled in uniquely named staging files, fsynced, sealed with an immutable trailer, renamed to final segment identity, and made directory-durable before publication. Staging files are unreachable state and are cleaned only by a recovery procedure that proves it.

`manifest.root` is a fixed two-slot bootstrap file; these are the only published durable bytes updated in place. Each 4 KiB `RootSlot` contains `{ magic, format, slot_generation, local_writer_fence_epoch, database_id, database_security_namespace_id, cluster_incarnation, incarnation_continuity_profile_id, cluster_incarnation_continuity_digest, continuity_cas_version, service_visibility_epoch, root_manifest_oid[32], RootBootstrap, tear_checksum }`. `IncarnationContinuityProfile` is `DirectoryBound` (ordinary embedded/local writes rely on the exact inode lease, and same-identity restore to another directory is forbidden—clone only) or `ExternalCas` (the Appendix A continuity record and live member lease are mandatory); W12 requires `ExternalCas`. `RootBootstrap` supplies everything needed **before** the object-location index exists: the complete canonical `CipherDescriptorWithoutDigest` for this root; its complete `EncodingDescriptorWithoutId` (including transfer length, both OTI fields, symbol size/count, and symbol-auth profile); `CiphertextId`, `EncodingId`, and ciphertext digest; a complete specialized `ContiguousSpan` placement descriptor containing placement epoch, failure-domain policy and domain ID, segment/offset/length, and symbol-inventory digest; and a noncircular opener bundle for both the root DEK and `K_oid` (inline wrapped keys or authenticated KMS/HSM locators plus wrap digests). Recovery locates the span, scans and authenticates its exact symbol inventory, verifies the inventory digest and reconstructed `PlacementId`, reconstructs the exact object AAD and encoding transcript, decodes the root, verifies its keyed ObjectId, and only then consults its indexes. No descriptor or identity-key field comes from the object being opened. `ObjectId` is already the full logical digest; there is no redundant `root_full_digest`. Recovery rejects a root whose authenticated namespace/database/incarnation/continuity/profile/visibility tuple disagrees with the slot.

Every slot publication is serialized by one per-open-inode `RootPublicationSequencer`; the whole-inode writer lease excludes other processes, while this sequencer excludes stale same-process tasks. It is an asupersync actor/obligation, not a conventional mutex held across `await`, and it grants at most one linear nonserializable `RootPublicationPermit`. Permit acquisition rereads and structurally authenticates both slots and binds `{inode_identity,filesystem_profile,publication_class,expected_winning_slot,expected_winning_generation,expected_winning_slot_digest,expected_manifest_identity,expected_writer_fence_epoch,expected_continuity_profile_digest_and_cas_version,expected_service_visibility_epoch,target_inactive_slot,next_generation,target_manifest_identity,target_bootstrap_digest,incarnation_lease_action_digest}`. `next_generation=checked_add(expected_winning_generation,1)`; exhaustion fail-closes all further publication and requires a fenced clone/migration rather than wrap or saturation. Two structurally credible equal-highest generations are accepted for read recovery only when their complete authenticated slot bytes are identical; any difference is ambiguity and fail-closes. Write mode first normalizes an identical-equal pair through a specialized takeover/convergence permit or remains read-only.

Immediately before `pwrite`, the permit re-reads the expected winner and live inode/fence/continuity/lease tuple. Any slot, generation, digest, manifest, epoch, CAS, service, path, mount, or lease drift consumes the permit as `AbortedStale` without writing; the caller rebuilds/rebases from the new winner. A successful permit writes exactly one complete inactive slot, performs the registered file and parent-directory durability actions, rereads/authenticates the new winner and its mandatory closure, and returns `RootPublicationReceipt {publication_class,prior_slot_and_generation,new_slot_and_generation,prior_and_new_manifest_identities,writer_continuity_service_tuple,bootstrap_digest,durability_profile,reread_digest}`. Cancellation after write begins must drive the obligation to durable reread or poison write mode; it cannot free the sequencer early. Ordinary semantic apply, prepared-root/Raft-only publication, audit candidate/mirror, checkpoint/cut, compaction, restore, role transition, fence-only takeover, creation, retirement, and slot convergence each have a generated legal `publication_class`/guard/manifest-transition row and all use this boundary. No code path may call the slot writer directly.

Publication alternates slots through that permit and never precomputes a generation outside it. Recovery first discards slots whose fixed record fails structural/tear validation, then selects the highest remaining generation. Once a slot is structurally credible, authentication or mandatory-closure failure triggers symbol/replica repair and then **fails closed**; it never silently rolls back to an older authenticated state that may precede an acknowledged commit. Using an older generation requires the explicit restore/rollback protocol in §16, with fencing, incarnation advancement, and an audit/transparency record.

Replicated semantics and replica-local recovery metadata are distinct. Local, Meta, and Shard payload/root schemas are the exact Appendix A role-tagged contracts, including every security/retention/trust/derived/key/delivery/backup/GC field and the fresh bootstrap plus restore-only `RecoveryReconciling` rules. Semantic sequences/HLC advance on every owning-state mutation; commit sequence advances only on graph commit. Replicas at one role/prefix agree on the canonical semantic root.

`RootManifest` is likewise the exact four-posture role-tagged union: common database/security-namespace/incarnation/replica/role/group/filesystem/fence/metadata-tree fields plus one of `Local{LogicalStateRoot,LocalPreparedPayloadRoot,RaftStateRoot,positions,AuditVisibilityFenceRef?}`, `Meta{GlobalStateRoot,MetaPreparedPayloadRoot,RaftStateRoot,positions,AuditVisibilityFenceRef?}`, `Shard{ShardLogicalStateRoot,ShardPreparedPayloadRoot,RaftStateRoot,positions}`, or the compact nonsemantic `RetiredLocal{CertifiedRoleTransitionRef,retirement certificate leaf,catalog receipt,terminal weak identities and seal digest,compact physical inventory,retirement audit evidence}` defined in Appendix A. Role/database/config/prepared/fence tuples are checked, including the narrowly defined takeover and prepared-transfer exceptions; RetiredLocal instead rejects every semantic, prepared, Raft, fence, and service root and can be opened only by the retirement/reclamation tools. An audit fence owns its unpublished candidate until the exact mirror permits visibility. Metadata-tree entries remain nonretaining locators: semantic/prepared/Raft/retirement-proof roots decide liveness, then GC resolves physical realizations. Each tree edge carries complete child descriptor/locator and authenticated child-DEK opener under the exact domain-separated AAD; no parent identity is needed before construction, and predecessor root digest is audit-only. Snapshots retain an active role's canonical and physical recovery roots; replay pins `ReplayLogicalStateEvidence::Local|Sharded`, never a locator map, and RetiredLocal admits neither snapshots nor replay execution.

The current `RootManifest` is deliberately absent from every metadata-tree generation that it bootstraps: its slot's `RootBootstrap` is its sole opener, and a tree `closure_digest` covers only that already-constructed tree closure, excluding the slot, the current manifest, and the bootstrap bytes. A later generation may index an older manifest only as nonretaining history after that older identity is known. This exclusion prevents a future-root identity from entering the tree whose identity the root must already name.

Exactly one process per replica directory may hold the publication lease, and exactly one task within it may hold the root-publication permit. Durable write mode requires a versioned `FilesystemDurabilityProfile`, not a filesystem-name guess. The initial `FGFS-LINUX-LOCAL-V1` profile admits only regular files on checked-in, kernel/mount-option-pinned local ext4 (`data=ordered|journal`, barriers enabled) or XFS (barriers and log-force flushes enabled), with staging and final paths on the same mounted filesystem. DAX, network/cluster filesystems, FUSE/overlay layers, disabled barriers, an unidentifiable mount/device, and every unregistered combination are read-only. `filesystem_profiles.toml` records the allowed kernel/filesystem/mount/device assumptions and probe-suite version; `fgdb doctor --write-profile` performs a scratch-directory conformance probe, while open repeats the mount, stable-inode, and option checks. A future platform profile must prove the same contract before it can enable writes: a nonblocking process-death-released exclusive whole-inode lease linearizable among FrankenGraphDB writers; one cancel-correct in-process publication sequencer; `pwrite` confined to the permit-selected inactive slot even if that slot tears arbitrarily; no collateral damage to the other slot; durable file-data/metadata after its declared sync; durable create/no-replace same-directory rename after parent-directory sync; and no acknowledged volatile-cache state after a successful flush. The profile is an explicit storage assumption—doctor cannot transmute lying hardware into a proof.

Writer acquisition for an existing database is the normative `WriterTakeoverProtocol`. It (1) opens the database directory and `manifest.root` without symlink traversal, records mount/device/inode identity, and acquires the nonblocking exclusive lease on that exact open inode; (2) creates the sole `RootPublicationSequencer` for that leased inode, re-resolves the path, and rejects replacement or identity drift; (3) under the lease, authenticates the highest structurally credible slot and mandatory closure, recovers Raft/audit-fence/restore state, and reconciles every prepared owner; (4) validates the slot's `IncarnationContinuityProfile`: `DirectoryBound` requires the original directory/inode continuity and forbids a restore bridge, while `ExternalCas` fetches the exact current continuity head, byte-matches namespace/incarnation/CAS/visibility state, and acquires a member-bound lease with `OrdinaryWrite` or narrowly `RecoveryOnly` scope; (5) computes `new_epoch = 1 + max(epoch values in the selected slot and its authenticated reachable RootManifest/seals/prepared records)` with checked overflow—unrooted staging cannot raise the fence; (6) mints a linear, nonexportable `PendingFenceGuard { lease,publication_sequencer,stable_identity,old_epoch,new_epoch,exact_recovered_root,continuity_head_and_incarnation_guard }` whose sole effects are building/sealing this fence-only successor and requesting the exact `FenceTakeover` publication permit; (7) uses that permit to persist a successor `RootManifest` that preserves the same canonical logical root and every receipted/ordered obligation, publishes/syncs the inactive slot at `new_epoch`, then rereads/authenticates that exact slot and revalidates continuity; and only then (8) consumes it into the ordinary nonconstructible combined writer/incarnation token in `CommitCx` (or recovery-only token) and enables only the effects allowed by that scope. The pending guard cannot create user data, issue a receipt, acknowledge/propose ordinary Raft, alter canonical state, or publish any other root. There is no timeout or administrative force path around either lease or sequencer. A stale/later/unavailable external continuity head makes the database read-only; a crashed old owner may leave immutable staging bytes, but its already receipted/ordered ownership remains live and is adopted by recovery, while it may not issue a new receipt or publish after either epoch changes.

Brand-new creation is the sole separate initialization transition. Under an accepted filesystem profile, `CreateNew` opens the directory without symlinks, creates a uniquely named staging root inode with `O_CREAT|O_EXCL`, acquires its whole-inode lease, and receives a `PendingCreationGuard` limited to constructing the complete Genesis closure and valid epoch-1 root slot. It fully writes and syncs that staging inode, verifies it in place, then atomically promotes it with same-directory `renameat2(RENAME_NOREPLACE)` (or the registered equivalent), syncs the parent directory, re-resolves and verifies that `manifest.root` is the same leased inode, rereads/authenticates the slot, and only then consumes the guard into the ordinary writer token. A racing loser never truncates or adopts the winner's file; its staging inode remains unreachable and is eligible only for generation/name-scoped recovery cleanup. A crash before promotion leaves no canonical `manifest.root`; a crash after the directory sync leaves a complete valid one. There is no empty/partial canonical tomb and no “empty file means ours” state.

Every ordinary segment/object/root seal, immutable-root build, prepared-root publication, `PayloadReceipt`, Raft proposal or follower acknowledgement, checkpoint/certificate publication, and `RootSlot` write compares the local `FenceToken` against the live inode lease and published epoch immediately before its irreversible step. Under `ExternalCas` it also revalidates the exact external continuity head/CAS version and a live member-bound `ClusterIncarnationLease` with the required scope; under `DirectoryBound`, the guard proves the unchanged creation directory/inode and cannot authorize cross-directory same-identity recovery. `CommitCx` contains the nonconstructible combined local/incarnation guard. The only pre-token writes are the type-restricted fence-only/Genesis/role-transition/restore operations of their named pending guards; their encoders reject every other object/root kind and consume the guard on promotion. Losing a lease, seeing a higher epoch/incarnation/CAS version, expired external authority, or observing path/inode/profile/visibility drift poisons the guard and fails closed. Local fence epoch is excluded from canonical capsule/marker/state-root bytes, while cluster incarnation and service visibility are canonical domain fields, so replicas agree. Read-only multi-process opens remain supported.

### 5.2 Commit protocol

Single-node and replicated commits use the same state machine; single-node mode is the quorum-one specialization. The durable unit is **not** the user's unresolved intent log. It is a post-rebase, post-constraint, post-SSI canonical effect capsule.

No caller can submit bare mutation intents. `fgdb-authz-types` defines a nonconstructible `AuthorizedMutationPermit` produced only by the trusted policy verifier. It binds database security namespace/incarnation, tenant/principal/issuer, authority digest and non-widenable operation ceiling, policy-semantics ObjectId, policy and revocation indices, root/snapshot and branch scope, exact read `GraphReferenceBinding[]` and write `CoordinateSchemaBinding[]`, topology epoch, expiry, channel/session binding where applicable, and a unique nonce. The coordinator verifies the permit's provenance and scope, recomputes authorization over the **final** effects and any `CoordinateSchemaTransition[]`, and orders the authorization decision against revocation/policy changes. Warden administers issuance later, but the verifier, permit type, and fail-closed revocation interface are W1/W2 dependencies—not optional server middleware.

Re-evaluable intents bind `IntentSemanticsOid`, the content digest of intent-schema version, `language_contract_oid`, semantic/scalar profiles, binder/normalizer version, and every procedure/UDF/module artifact that influenced intent construction. The merge ladder evaluates canonical typed intents under this object, never reparses source text under a new corrigendum or server default; if an artifact is unavailable, rebase fails closed.

1. **Propose.** A writer submits `TxnProposal { snapshot, expected_write_coordinates[], intent_semantics_oid, intents, predicate_witnesses, authorized_mutation_permit, ephemeral_reservation, requested_durable_charge_effects, txn_token }`. It may precompute physical candidates, but no candidate capsule is publishable truth. `txn_token` and every server handle are scoped as §13/App. D require.
2. **Order and validate.** The WriteCoordinator deterministically orders a group, verifies permit provenance/scope, live writer lease/fence, schema/topology/policy/revocation epochs, branch write/envelope-key epochs, resource reservation, and expected branch heads; then it performs FCW/SSI validation and the merge ladder when necessary. Each accepted transaction is evaluated against the committed basis plus earlier accepted effects in that group. A rebase produces new reads, writes, constraints, effects, and key-epoch bindings; it never blesses an old capsule.
3. **Canonicalize final effects.** Verify and preserve every previously ordered escaping allocation, then resolve only still-confined temporary IDs and generated keys; evaluate CAS/upsert/no-op behavior; expand cascades; compute explicit logical retractions and insertions with `BirthOrdinal`s only for genuinely new identities; preserve source origin and assign sequence-neutral `BranchAdmissionOrdinal {merge_ordinal,element_id}` for imports; recompute final authorization including hidden-state cascades; validate constraints and the authoritative durable-quota ledger; materialize canonical `ResourceChargeEffect`/release effects; and rerun SSI over the final footprint. Rebase may preserve an escaping binding or reject the attempt; it may never remap an identity already returned, referenced by a later statement, or otherwise durably exposed. The result is a sequence-neutral `CommittedEffectSet` plus `LogicalDeltaTemplate` (§9.1), independent of block/run layout. The later canonical `MarkerRef` supplies `CommitSeq`, so apply derives `OriginBirthOrder`, `BranchAdmissionOrder {commit_seq,merge_ordinal,element_id}`, effect order, and ordered delta time without changing the approved capsule digest.
4. **Finalize capsules.** Persist one canonical `LogicalDeltaTemplate`, then construct `CommittedEffectCapsule { read_snapshot_basis, validated_apply_basis, intent_semantics_oid, read_graph_reference_bindings, validated_write_coordinate_bindings, validated_write_key_epoch_bindings, coordinate_schema_transitions, topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index, committed_effects, final_read_witnesses, final_write_summary, constraint_evidence, authorization_decision_ref: StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>, authorization_decision_digest, resource_transition_refs: StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>[], resource_charge_effects, txn_outcome_preparation_ref: StrongRef<TxnOutcomePreparationRecord>, logical_delta_template_ref: StrongRef<LogicalDeltaTemplate>, logical_delta_template_digest, optional_physical_accelerators, txn_token, final_effect_digest }`. A repeated digest is an integrity cross-check, never a replacement for the typed strong edge. The template digest must match the referenced bytes and the template must match the final effect set; neither field may appear without the other. Each write-key binding fixes the branch envelope/write epoch under which every referenced new ciphertext DEK is wrapped. Physical patches carry an apply-basis digest and may be ignored; unresolved or conditional commands are forbidden. Capsule builders return bytes and a digest to the coordinator, which verifies them against its approved final effects.
5. **Payload durability barrier D1 and stable prepared ownership.** Seal and make directory-durable the final semantic capsule **and its entire mandatory strong closure**: coordinate effect payloads, `LogicalDeltaTemplate`, schema/constraint/resource transitions, authorization decision, merge record, outcome-preparation record, active final-certification reservation when terminal, optional accelerator bytes actually referenced by the command, and every newly introduced semantics/module/profile object. HLC observation and expected order are intentionally excluded from this stable semantic base and live only in the repeatable order-attempt supplement below. Its immutable base inventory defines `PreparedOwnershipId = H("fgdb:prepared-owner:v1", storage_member, replica_namespace_or_incarnation, prepare_id, configuration_state_oid, payload_predicate_digest, base_closure_inventory_digest)`; a scalar configuration epoch is insufficient because same-epoch candidates/joint states can differ. On every replica or availability donor issuing a receipt, create an immutable replica-local `PreparedCommitRecord { prepared_ownership_id, prepare_id, record_generation, predecessor_ref, database/incarnation/configuration-ref/predicate/fence tuple, txn_token, capsule_ref, command_ref?, base_closure_inventory_digest, current_closure_inventory_digest, strong_logical_refs[], exact_realizations[{ object_or_subobject_id, encoding_id, placement_id, key_opener_ref }], status, receipt_nonce }`; its typed references and predecessor are strong. Every successor repeats the stable ownership ID and identical base closure, while its current closure is identical or a strict authenticated superset—for example after adding the completed command. `PreparedPayloadRoot` maps stable ownership ID to the latest record; no record is mutated in place. Insert the record, publish authenticated nonretaining locator entries, persist the updated `RootManifest`, and durably publish a `RootSlot` **before** D1 is complete or a payload receipt may be emitted. Pre-existing objects are revalidated and promoted into the prepared closure; a digest or locator without reachable authenticated bytes is insufficient. A `PayloadAvailabilityCertificate` covers this exact **pre-command semantic base closure** under the exact configuration ObjectId/predicate, including the quorum-one local predicate. Each receipt binds that config OID, predicate digest, stable ownership ID, and base-closure digest; an observed record OID/root generation is diagnostic freshness, never the sole ownership identity. Bytes not yet admitted to a prepared root remain staging data and are unreachable after a crash.
6. **Authorize, command, order, and publish barrier D2.** For each proposal/reproposal, the coordinator builds and D1-certifies a fresh `LocalOrderAttemptInput` over the stable semantic owner, Active final-certification reservation, expected next order, and `LocalHlcProposalEvidence`. Immediately before ordering, voters verify the supplement/certificate, reservation, prepared ownership/configuration and writer fence, selected terminal, and HLC observation age/source policy. They do **not** revalidate mutable heads, key/policy/revocation/conflict/resource bases outside the reservation: those were atomically validated and held before signing, and later changes cannot reinterpret them. The normative immutable `CommitCommand` is `{command_version,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,txn_token,final_certification_reservation_ref:StrongRef<LocalFinalCertificationReservation>,required_reservation_state:Active,order_attempt_input_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptInput>,order_attempt_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptAvailabilityCertificate>,capsule_ref:StrongRef<CommittedEffectCapsule>,logical_delta_template_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaTemplate>,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>],txn_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<TxnOutcomePreparationRecord>,payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_branch_heads,expected_branch_key_epochs,topology_epoch,policy_epoch,revocation_index,final_effect_digest}`. The expected basis fields are redundant integrity projections that must byte-match the reservation, never fresh CAS gates. The semantic availability certificate covers the stable base; the order-attempt certificate separately covers only the repeatable order/HLC supplement. The coordinator publishes a semantic prepared-record successor that adds and strongly owns the completed command and marks the supplement Ordered in the same accepted transition. **Every durable database, including embedded and server single-node posture, orders through the same internal Raft log; single node is a one-member/quorum-one configuration.** Only `:memory:` runs the same state machine without a durability claim. After log acceptance, the Raft closure and certificate donors retain the command/base/supplement closures through apply and compaction. A semantic prepared owner may abandon only an unreceipted, provably unordered attempt under a current writer/configuration fence, or a receipted attempt after consensus proves it cannot be ordered and every certificate/configuration retention floor has expired. Once any terminal audit lock exists, neither semantic prepared ownership nor final certification may be abandoned; only a provably unordered stale supplement may be retired/replaced. Timeout or process death alone is never abandonment proof.

   Normatively, the inline `HlcProposalEvidence` union below is only a role-shape shorthand. Its two durable object kinds are `LocalHlcProposalEvidence {database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,role:Local,configured_source_id,source_profile_oid,signed_observation,observation_uncertainty,normalization_policy_oid,observation_body_digest}` and `MetaHlcProposalEvidence {database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,role:Meta,configured_source_set_and_epoch,canonically_sorted_signed_observations,required_quorum,observation_uncertainties,normalization_policy_oid,observation_body_digest}`; each registered transcript covers every field except the repeated body digest. The evidence is prebuilt, included in the separately D1-certified `OrderAttemptInput`, and reached by the ordered Local or Meta command only through that exact supplement. No command carries a parallel scalar or observation list, and apply derives its HLC solely from the previous persisted HLC plus the supplement's referenced object. Signature domain, source eligibility, and role are verified from ordered bytes; shards have no such object or semantic-HLC field.

   Local transaction apply also materializes the exact self-contained `LogicalDeltaBatch<LocalCommitted>` before constructing the candidate payload, verifies it against the committed capsule/template/marker, inserts `(next_commit_seq -> batch_ref)` into `LocalDeltaBatchIndex`, and advances `local_delta_frontier` to that same commit sequence in the **same** state transition. The batch is therefore reachable from the candidate root at the first crash point at which the commit exists; there is no separate Local delta-publish command or unrooted interval. Under a required audit fence the candidate index/frontier remain hidden with the candidate root until the exact mirror publishes it, but recovery still owns the batch through `RaftStateRoot`. `LocalTerminalCompletionSpec` accepts its delta postcondition only when the visible payload's index contains that exact marker/batch and its frontier is at least the commit sequence. Rematerialization and retry must reproduce identical bytes; a missing, duplicate, gapped, wrong-marker, or wrong-frontier insertion fails apply.

   `HlcProposalEvidence` is the closed role union `Local{configured_source_id,source_profile_oid,signed_observation,observation_uncertainty,normalization_policy_oid}|Meta{configured_source_set_and_epoch,canonically_sorted_signed_observations,required_quorum,observation_uncertainties,normalization_policy_oid}`. The registered policy fixes source eligibility, quorum, interval-to-candidate rule, maximum accepted age, and `maximum_forward_jump` relative to the previous logical HLC; missing, duplicated, untrusted, stale, future-skewed, or arithmetically invalid observations reject the proposal. Shards never propose semantic HLC. Deterministic apply verifies the command, closure, and evidence, assigns the next `LogicalCommandSeq`, computes `checked_increment(previous_logical_hlc)`, derives the one normalized candidate from the evidence, rejects a candidate beyond the checked forward-jump bound, and advances `logical_hlc_state=max(checked_increment,normalized_candidate)`. Any sequence/HLC overflow rejects the not-yet-ordered command before state mutation and permanently fail-closes further mutation in the live process against the already persisted maximum counter; recovery reaches the same refusal from that counter, and operator-directed clone/migration is the only continuation. No nonexistent terminal command or extra sequence value is fabricated, and arithmetic never wraps or saturates. Logical-HLC proposal evidence is ordering input only and cannot validate expiry. Transaction apply additionally assigns the next transaction-only `CommitSeq`, copies that command HLC into `CommitMarker.commit_hlc`, and canonically builds the standalone marker/`MarkerRef`, terminal outcome and other applied records, the new `LogicalStatePayload`, then the `LogicalCommandRecord`, and finally the outer `LogicalStateRoot` in that acyclic order. Semantic ownership transfers into those objects before the prepared record may become terminal. Every other canonical schema/policy/revocation/delivery/accounting/key/audit/configuration/GC operation is a typed `ControlCommand` and follows the same HLC and payload→record→root construction, incrementing `LogicalCommandSeq` but not `CommitSeq`. `ControlCommand.typed_payload_ref` always names a registered sequence-neutral pre-order spec—Local transaction lifecycle uses `LocalBeginReservationSpec`, `LocalBeginTerminalSpec`, `LocalAttemptRegistrationSpec`, `LocalStatementRegistrationSpec`, `LocalStatementPublicationSpec`, `LocalResultDeliveryTransitionSpec`, `LocalStatementAbortSpec`, `LocalPrepareAdmissionSpec`, `LocalReadCloseSpec`, `LocalTerminalCompletionSpec`, `LocalOutcomeCompactionSpec`, and `TxnAbortSpec`; other families include `CheckpointInstallSpec`, `IdRangeGrantSpec`, `MergePrepareSpec`, `DpTransitionSpec`, `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec`, `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec`, `AuditTerminalSpec`, `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec`, `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec`, `KeyDestroyProposal`, `KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec`, `GcProposal`, and `ConfigurationTransitionSpec`—never an applied record or resulting state. Every root/head CAS in such a spec or command is an explicit nonretaining `WeakStateIdentity`, `WeakMarkerIdentity`, or scalar epoch; retaining a prior state requires a separately typed temporary pin that cannot enter the installed result. Applied records may name the already identified `ControlCommand` plus their assigned logical-command sequence; they may not use `StrongCommandRef` to name their own future `LogicalCommandRecord`. Actual Raft configuration entries are the same typed configuration control-command entries—not an unsequenced second mutation—and advance logical-command time; heartbeat/read-index/no-op bookkeeping advances neither sequence nor HLC. Without an audit visibility fence, the local manifest points to the new logical root and the alternate slot publishes it. With a fence, the slot publishes a local manifest that still points to the prior visible logical root while `RaftStateRoot` strongly owns the new candidate; only the exact external-resolution mirror command may replace it with the final visible root (§12.8). The client receives `Committed(seq)` only after one-member or multi-member consensus, local D2 apply, configured acknowledgement durability, durable outcome record, completed protected-audit transition, and final root publication. A later revocation cannot retroactively undo a committed transaction; it fences subsequent work.

`txn_token` is the opaque durable idempotency identity inside §13's MACed `TxnOutcomeCapability`, scoped to database security namespace/incarnation/service-visibility epoch, tenant/principal, authority ceiling, and an issuance/expiry interval. Local 1.0 has the same durable BEGIN, explicit multi-statement, autocommit, result-replay, COMMIT/ROLLBACK, and status semantics later used by W12, but uses the closed Local object family in Appendix A rather than pretending the W12 Meta/shard family exists. A BEGIN first orders `LocalBeginReservationSpec` and exposes `BEGIN_ACCEPTED` only after `Reserved` plus `TxnOutcomeRecord::BeginStaging` are visible; registration atomically binds that reservation, operation-audit owner, workspace generation zero, and `TxnOutcomeRecord::Registered`. Autocommit uses `LocalAttemptRegistrationSpec::Autocommit` and the same lifecycle without emitting BEGIN frames. Every statement is durably Open before execution and terminally Published, Failed, or Abandoned; successful statements advance one predecessor-linked workspace generation, while result bytes remain spill-backed and audit-fenced until publication. Read-write commit first orders `LocalPrepareAdmissionSpec`, then builds the ordinary final capsule and unchanged `CommitCommand`; read-only completion uses `LocalReadCloseSpec`. Cancellation/rollback uses strengthened `TxnAbortSpec`, never an out-of-band coordinator flag.

`TxnOutcomeIndex` is therefore the sole Local token/capability lookup and attempt-lifecycle authority, mapping each scoped token to `Detailed{outcome_ref:StrongRef<TxnOutcomeRecord>}|Compacted{summary_root_ref:StrongRef<LocalTxnOutcomeSummaryRoot>,leaf_key_digest}|ExpiredTombstone{token_digest}`. `TxnOutcomeRecord` is predecessor-linked and moves only through `BeginStaging -> Registered/StatementOpen -> PrepareAdmitted -> CommittedPendingPostconditions -> Committed`, or the typed `Aborted`, `ReadClosed`, and `NeverRegistered` terminals described in Appendix A. An identical retry joins and returns the original durable state; a mismatched request, authority, epoch, token, idempotency key, statement, or expected predecessor fails closed. Before any terminal result is returned, the exact semantic outcome and required durability/delta/result/audit/resource postconditions reach `TerminalReady`. Records, compact summaries, permanent token tombstones, and verifier keys remain through the advertised lookup/retry/retention floor. After expiry a valid-MAC matching-domain capability returns `TokenExpired`; it is never treated as a new transaction. Cancellation after terminal ordering may return `Unknown(txn_token)` only when the caller lacks enough evidence to distinguish the already durable state, and resolves solely through scoped status lookup—it never promises rollback of a possibly committed transaction.

The protocol has two **durability barriers**, not literally two syscalls: each barrier includes every file and parent-directory sync required by the platform. Group commit amortizes both. Recovery starts from the highest valid root slot, reconciles `PreparedPayloadRoot` with the one-member or multi-member Raft log, completes every committed-but-unapplied command, and only then considers fenced abandonment/collection of prepared records. An active audit fence is recovered from the local Raft closure; its candidate remains retained and invisible while recovery reconciles the external terminal record and orders the mirror command. Recovery verifies the authoritative checkpoint and contiguous logical-command suffix; for transaction records it additionally verifies the contiguous transaction-marker subsequence, authenticates and decodes every referenced final capsule, and applies canonical effects. RaptorQ may repair damaged compatible symbols within the configured erasure model; it does not replace root redundancy, payload replication, or fail-closed recovery beyond that model.

### 5.3 Snapshots

A read snapshot is `{ database_id, database_security_namespace_id, cluster_incarnation, logical_state_root_oid, local_root_manifest_oid, local_root_generation, logical_command_seq, high_seq, graph_reference_bindings[], topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index, retention_lease }`, captured by following one validated slot through its local root to one immutable `LogicalStateRoot`. `logical_command_seq` fixes the complete canonical state-machine prefix; transaction-only `high_seq` fixes graph system time. Bindings are unique by `binding_role_id` (not by graph/branch), and every selected head is at or below the same `high_seq`; all repeated historical roles acquire their own ancestry/schema/authorization evidence under the snapshot's closure lease. Certificates/replay use the logical root and role-bearing bindings; the retention lease pins the local realization plus its logical closure. A version is visible only when its commit sequence is at or below `high_seq`, its creation marker belongs to that reference role's selected branch ancestry, and no visible retirement/supersession marker follows it. Integer-only visibility is legal solely inside a branch-filtered physical projection carrying a verified `(binding_role_id, graph, branch, head, lineage_digest)` token; global sequence interleaving alone never proves ancestry.

Snapshot acquisition uses `ReadSlotAndRoots -> RegisterLease(local_root_manifest_oid, logical_state_root_oid, gc_epoch) -> RevalidateSlotRootsAndEpoch`; if publication or GC races, it drops the tentative lease and retries. This closes the read-root/reclaim gap and is lock-free only if the lease-registry implementation proves that progress property—there is no blanket wait-free claim. A retention lease pins the **meaning and disk reachability** of its checkpoint/marker/index/object closure; it does not pin all potentially readable buffer frames. Only an active cursor/borrow pins a resident frame. Long-running analytics, backups, and replay manifests expose attributable lease cost, expiry policy, and cancellation requests, and nothing silently slides a snapshot or view watermark forward.

Each committed marker carries the deterministic `commit_hlc` copied from §5.2's ordered `logical_command_hlc`; the current logical HLC state is part of `LogicalStatePayload` and every checkpoint. `AS OF TIMESTAMP t` resolves through a versioned `(commit_hlc, commit_seq)` index to the greatest visible marker in the selected branch ancestry whose HLC is at most `t`; intervening control-command HLCs have no graph marker and therefore cannot become graph system-time answers. Local clock regression cannot change replicated bytes or order. The result certificate returns the effective marker/sequence.

### 5.4 One Version Universe: retention tiers = temporal database

The authoritative recovery equation for complete canonical state makes checkpoint installation itself explicit:

`state(L, C) = reconstruct_and_verify_install(RecoveryCheckpointProjection(B₀ at L₀,C₀), retained CheckpointInstall input+record at L₀+1) + apply contiguous LogicalCommandRecord suffix (L₀+1, L]`,

where `L` is `LogicalCommandSeq` and `C` is transaction-only `CommitSeq`. The interval `(L₀+1,L]` deliberately begins at `L₀+2`; the install record at `L₀+1` is reconstructed/verified exactly once, never replayed twice. A checkpoint is built **from** an already identified basis; it never claims that basis already points back to the new checkpoint. It records a nonretaining weak basis-command identity, covered marker identity, chain hashes, basis payload digest, HLC and partition projections plus the generated role-tagged `CheckpointStateVector`. The weak command boundary plus chain/payload/projection commitments authenticates the cut without keeping the prior command—and therefore a prior checkpoint-install spec—alive. Every Local/Meta/Shard vector has exactly one recipe for every field in its matching versioned payload schema. The common legal tags are `CopiedStrong`, `ProjectedSnapshot`, `ResetByCheckpointInstall`, and `SelfExcluded`; operational replacement additionally requires exactly one `InstallProvisionalCut` for the retention map, and Local-activation Meta/Shard bases use `ApplyActivationProjection` only for fields covered by the certified projection recipe. The generated role/basis matrix rejects either special tag anywhere else. Coverage includes bootstrap/restore/migration phase; graph partitions; catalog/schema/topology/security; allocator/external continuities; constraints/resources/privacy/DP/outcomes; branches/merge; retained-stream floor/retention map; derived, delivery, replay and backup registries; keys/signing/verifiers; audit/transparency; GC; remote trust/retention; prepared/certificate/decision directories; and configuration-floor state. `recovery_checkpoint_ref` uses `SelfExcluded{InstallThisCheckpoint}`. For an `Operational` basis, `config_payload_floor_ref` uses `SelfExcluded{InstallPairedConfigFloor}`; copying the old floor would recreate an unbounded `floor -> checkpoint -> prior floor` retention chain. Genesis copies the absent floor as `None`; the later initial-floor bootstrap remains separate. A domain-separated `basis_projection_digest` commits the canonical reconstruction with exact literals and checkpoint-free cut recipe, never future ObjectIds; `basis_payload_digest` records the exact pre-install payload observed while pinned.

`CheckpointInstallSpec { basis:WeakStateIdentity, basis_logical_command_seq:L₀, basis_commit_seq:C₀, basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest, basis_projection_digest, checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>, checkpoint_state_vector_digest, paired_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>?, retention_cut_body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>?, reset_field_tags[] }` is the exact first retained command at `L₀+1`. Its acyclic construction order is basis/projection plus checkpoint-free command/marker/effect cut recipes → `RetentionCutBody` → generated `CheckpointStateVector` → `RecoveryCheckpoint` →, for `Operational`, paired floor whose checkpoint observation is weak → install spec. The cut body names no checkpoint identity or reference; the apply-built `ProvisionalRetentionCutSet` attaches the actual enclosing checkpoint and install record. Genesis requires both optional refs `None` and no `InstallProvisionalCut` vector entry. An operational basis requires both `Some`; body, vector, checkpoint, and floor must cover the same prefix/current-prospective configuration, and the vector's registered retention-map entry is `InstallProvisionalCut{body_ref,checkpoint_binding=InstallThisCheckpoint}`. Apply verifies the current basis and projection, replaces `recovery_checkpoint_ref` with `checkpoint_ref`, atomically replaces `config_payload_floor_ref` with the paired floor, constructs/installs the exact provisional cut when required, performs only the listed `ResetByCheckpointInstall` values, advances bootstrap phase when applicable, and changes no other field. A reset entry is legal only in this first command and only with its registered equivalence/semantic-transition proof; no earlier suffix command can observe omitted state. The install record's conditional predecessor identifies the same weak covered-basis boundary (or genesis when `L₀=0`); after authority transfer, the verified `CommandCut` may stop there without retaining the old command bytes. Later retained records are contiguous. Transaction records form a subsequence whose markers advance contiguously from `C₀`; control commands do not advance `CommitSeq`. A non-genesis authoritative checkpoint therefore always has its install command—there is no empty-suffix special case and no self-referential post-install digest. A predecessor-checkpoint digest is weak audit metadata unless a retention root explicitly promotes it. The checkpoint/floor/cut trio becomes authoritative only after projection/equivalence/floor verification, install-command and payload durability, root publication, and the configured replica-durability gate; physical reclamation needs the later cut-activation command. This is an explicit transfer of recovery and configuration-payload authority, not a derived cache silently becoming primary.

Retired versions then cool through three query-retention tiers:

- **Tier 0 — live MVCC:** current version chains and unsealed deltas.
- **Tier 1 — warm logical history:** columnar logical effects sorted by `(element_id, commit_seq)`, directly queryable for recent `AS OF`/`BETWEEN` predicates.
- **Tier 2 — historical checkpoints:** full compressed partition snapshots plus a bounded logical-effect suffix. Optional inter-object delta compression names an explicit base ObjectId, forms an acyclic bounded-depth dependency graph, and is applied **before** each resulting payload is independently RaptorQ encoded. RaptorQ itself is never described as a delta codec.

Retention is configured per graph as `KEEP ALL`, `KEEP <duration|seqs>`, or `KEEP NONE`, but physical collection is governed by the conservative union of all roots. Every durable edge is explicitly strong, conditional, or a non-followed weak identity/digest. A capsule's sequence-neutral effect directory and its `LogicalDeltaTemplate` entries use `ConditionalCoordinateRef{oid,graph,branch}`; after commit, the enclosing marker supplies the coordinate's retention sequence. While a capsule is pending or otherwise has no committed marker context, traversal from `PreparedPayloadRoot` treats every such conditional edge as strong. Once committed, an authenticated installed-checkpoint/`RetentionMap` cut may stop only the matching coordinate at or below its verified boundary. Logical-command and marker predecessor links use `ConditionalCommandRef` and `ConditionalMarkerRef`; their corresponding checkpoint cuts may stop only the matching predecessor axis. Branch/fork/merge bases and all other strong roots still win. Missing bytes without a matching cut are corruption; a proved cut returns `HistoryUnavailable`, not a partial result. A baseline- or delta-resume promise roots its exact `DeliveredBaselinePayload` or `DeliveredDeltaPayload`/`DeltaDeliveryEnvelope` through the outstanding cursor lease; atomic delta provenance additionally owns its source `LogicalDeltaBatch`, while coalesced provenance needs source history only when its advertised proof scope requires it. Otherwise a missing promised range produces a visible `GAP` and new baseline. Weak source-template/marker identities do not pull old capsule history back into reachability. Effective floors also include stable prepared owners and consensus commands, transaction outcomes, branch manifests/key epochs/envelope roots/recipient or advancing grants/merge idempotency state, identity/privacy/audit external continuity, DP request+seed+result, audit ticket/event/resolution/receipt/gap state, replay registry/manifests/archives, resume cursors and baseline/delta/snapshot leases, backup/legal holds, current/prospective configuration floors, keys, and transparency policy. A floor's checkpoint/vector observations are explicitly weak and validated against the separately strong current payload checkpoint; operational checkpoint installation pairs the replacement floor and excludes the prior floor from its projection. Overrides, cuts, and retained bytes are observable.

Point-in-time restore, temporal queries, raw CDC, and audit all reuse Chronicle ordering, but they are not identical retention products. PITR is bounded by retained checkpoints/effects; compliance audit has its separate signed retention chain (§12.8); replay requires its evidence closure (§8.6); and derived subscriptions consume canonical `LogicalDeltaBatch` objects (§9), not unresolved intents.

### 5.5 Compaction

Compaction follows `BUILD -> VERIFY_EQUIVALENCE -> D1_NEW_OBJECTS -> ROOT_PUBLISH -> SLOT_CONVERGE -> WAIT_SAFE_POINT -> RETIRE`. It marks from both valid root slots and explicitly traverses logical-command/generated-complete installed-checkpoint cuts, stable prepared-payload and consensus-log ownership, every branch/base, branch key-epoch/envelope/grant root and branch-merge ledger, transaction/DP outcome, all external continuity links, resume-cursor/delivery/replay registries and archives, delivered-output payloads, audit ticket/event/resolution/CAS-receipt/gap/audit roots, snapshot and delivery leases, backup/legal hold, key/key-wrap, and current/prospective configuration/floors. It then resolves marked logical/subobject identities through nonretaining physical locators, builds new immutable encodings, proves old/new canonical logical digests equal, and publishes the new `RootManifest` through a serialized `CompactionRootPublish` permit.

After rereading and fully validating that highest slot/closure, a linear `RootSlotConvergenceGuard` may request a `SlotConvergence` permit whose acquisition rechecks that the **current** winner is still the exact target manifest, writer/continuity/service tuple, and bootstrap. Only while holding that permit may it publish the other slot at checked `winner_generation+1` with byte-identical target fields. Any intervening ordinary, audit, checkpoint, restore, role-transition, retirement, or other convergence publication changes the winner and makes acquisition or the immediate pre-write recheck fail stale; convergence then restarts from the new winner and can never overwrite it with an older manifest at a higher generation. Success syncs and rereads both slots and produces `RootSlotConvergenceReceipt {manifest_identity,first_slot_generation,second_slot_generation,identical_bootstrap_digest,two_slot_reread_digest,durability_profile,root_publication_receipt}`. This physical-only convergence advances no logical/Raft/commit/HLC sequence and cannot select a different manifest. Recovery at every crash simply chooses the highest credible slot; retry converges the remaining slot. Old encodings retire only after both valid slots converge away from the old closure, the receipt is durable, and no independent lease can expose them. Active marker batches are never rewritten in place. Staging namespace creation, sealing, rename, convergence, and retirement include the required directory durability operations; crash/DPOR tests cut before/after each convergence write, sync, reread, cancellation, and generation allocation while racing ordinary, prepared/Raft-only, audit candidate/mirror, checkpoint, restore, role-transition, retirement, and another convergence publication. They also cover equal-generation ambiguity and checked generation exhaustion.

Replica positions and CRDT gossip are observations, not GC authority. The safe point is computed under a consensus-fenced membership epoch (§14); loss of quorum, uncertain membership, an unacknowledged root, or a missing key wrap stops reclamation. The actor is supervised and rate limited against foreground latency. Space amplification, checkpoint cadence, and controller settings are empirical/configuration gates with named workloads and model assumptions, not safety invariants.

### 5.6 Branches: git for graphs

A branch manifest is `{ graph, branch_id, fork_parent, fork_parent_head, fork_boundary_logical_command_seq, base_checkpoint?, key_envelope_root, current_envelope_epoch, current_write_key_epoch, policy }`. The boundary sequence is the already assigned `BranchEpochBoundaryReservation.boundary_logical_command_seq`, not the later bundle-install sequence; client-visible install provenance lives only in the applied control record/registry projection. Branch creation adds only metadata and key wraps, so its **data-copy complexity** is O(1); metadata is proportional to the bounded envelope-root fanout created by the fork, not falsely claimed O(1) for arbitrary recipient lists. A durable creation still pays ordered root-publication latency and is never promised below an fsync-independent microsecond constant. Reads select the branch head and follow explicit branch-parent links atop structurally shared objects.

Forking is one canonical `BranchForkSpec`, not an out-of-band KMS effect. Before ordering, a stable prepared owner builds the complete `BranchForkBundle` bottom-up: pre-minted descriptors/keys; closed old-parent epoch successors through boundary `L-1`; frozen path-copied parent root; disjoint parent-successor/child epochs at boundary `L`; narrowly scoped grants; successor roots/manifests; exact ciphertext/encoding/placement/openers; then one availability certificate over that closed inventory. Here `L` is the already ordered boundary reservation's logical-command sequence, never the future install order. The command can be formed only after all identities exist. Deterministic apply creates no key/ciphertext/node/record/grant/manifest; it byte-validates the bundle, held head/epochs, boundary-reservation identity/sequence, nonce, and isolation laws, then atomically installs the already-known manifests/registries. Parent writes admitted after the boundary use only the successor; the child opens frozen history but no successor/sibling epoch. A prepared old-epoch parent write must be revalidated and rewrapped/re-encoded or abort before order. Epoch material is never reused after crash, restore, or merge.

Branch merge uses one explicit **squash-merge visibility model**. Against declared merge bases, the evaluator computes the canonical logical difference contributed by each source and emits ordinary target-branch retractions/insertions at one new target `MarkerRef`; source heads are provenance/idempotency inputs, not additional visibility parents. The target head therefore follows exactly one target predecessor, and reads never need to guess whether imported source marker ranges became ancestors. A source-created element keeps its globally unique VId/EId and immutable `OriginBirthOrder`; the target version's `created_by` is the merge marker. Pre-order merge effects store only `BranchAdmissionOrdinal {merge_ordinal,element_id}`. Apply combines it with the assigned marker's CommitSeq to derive `BranchAdmissionOrder {commit_seq,merge_ordinal,element_id}`. If a query explicitly requests branch-arrival order it uses that distinct policy—`InsertionOrder` never silently rewrites an element's origin, and no pre-order/audit/D1 transcript names a future merge sequence.

`MergeRecord { merge_token, merge_request_commitment, target, target_basis, source_heads[], merge_bases[], imported_range_tokens[], imported_range_keys[], resolution_policy_oid, resolution_digest, final_effect_digest }` is hash-linked from both capsule and marker. Each range token binds source branch, inclusive weak marker identities, base, and source chain digest without pretending that the source range became target ancestry. Merge idempotency has two independent keys. Before ordering, the authorized coordinator uses production entropy to mint the unguessable token and construct a complete `MergeOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord`; deterministic apply invents neither. The graph-effect-free `MergePrepareSpec {client_request_nonce,request_commitment,candidate_merge_token,capability_replay_ref:StrongRef<MergeOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord>,expected_merge_index_absence_or_matching_retry,terminal_audit_gate}` durably maps the caller/target-scoped nonce to that preidentified stable token and exact canonical capability bytes. Replay header/body, target, token, request, idempotency-key digest, verifier key/profile/window, policy/revocation, and authority must byte-match the spec. Retrying preparation with the same scoped nonce and request returns the record's original bytes even if a retry proposed a different candidate; conflicting commitment reuse is rejected. Evaluation/charging cannot begin until that capability is acknowledged and resubmitted. `BranchMergeLedgerRoot` maps the token to the immutable original request and `capability_replay_ref` plus `InFlight|Committed{target_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity,final_effect_digest}|Rejected{stable_reason_digest}|Compacted{summary_ref}|ExpiredTombstone{token_digest,capability_commitment,expiry_evidence_digest}`. Detailed and compacted nonexpired states retain the replay record; only evidence-bound expiry drops it. Transaction apply validates the token/request/range keys and atomically installs `Committed` plus coverage with the merge marker; a deterministic pre-effect rejection uses a typed `MergeRejectSpec` control command to install `Rejected`. A retry with the capability returns the original outcome even if the target head has since advanced; an old-incarnation or old-service-epoch capability never resolves the new state.

Separately, every requested source interval derives `ImportedRangeKey = H("fgdb:imported-range:v1", database_namespace, target_graph_branch, source_branch, source_range_and_chain_digest, merge_semantics_oid, resolution_policy_oid)`, deliberately excluding `target_basis`. The ledger maintains canonical imported coverage by source chain. A new request that exactly or partially overlaps committed coverage returns `AlreadyImported` or, only under a declared subtract-previously-imported policy, evaluates the canonical uncovered remainder; it never reapplies the overlap. `target_basis` remains an FCW/head-CAS validation input, not an idempotency key. Token outcomes and imported coverage are ordered with the merge command and retained in a compact authenticated non-forgetting map across checkpoint/history cuts, backup/restore, reconfiguration, and GC. Weak terminal identities prevent duplicate application without retaining old marker/capsule bytes forever. Only intent families with proved associative, commutative, idempotent joins may claim order independence. All other eligible operations use the resolution policy's pinned total order; unresolved conflicts produce a capability-redacted conflict graph. A vague cocycle check is not a substitute for algebraic laws or explicit ordering.

Shared encrypted objects keep their existing ciphertext and object DEKs. `KeyEnvelopeRoot` is a constructively verified immutable DAG, not an opaque “closure”: its nodes grant the current envelope key access to closed ancestor envelope roots and to exactly the branch write epochs whose object-DEK wraps it may open. Every inherited edge carries a maximum logical-command/marker cut, and every object-DEK wrap binds source graph/branch, write epoch, object/ciphertext identities, and creation prefix in canonical AAD. The fork-time double rotation above is the isolation boundary: a child receives the now-closed parent envelope key, never a key under which post-fork parent grants or ciphertexts may be created. A squash merge that reuses source ciphertext adds only per-object DEK wraps under the target's current write epoch; it never grants the target the source branch's envelope/write epoch wholesale unless an independently authorized handoff says so.

`KeyEnvelopeGrant` wraps the exact root opener/envelope key to a recipient and declares `SnapshotAtHead` or `AdvancingBranch`. A snapshot/revocation `BranchGrantBundle` prebuilds the same close/freeze/double-rotation, grants only the frozen root through `L-1`, and provides the successor manifest before ordering; apply only validates/installs the bundle. An advancing bundle intentionally grants the exact current root/epoch, and every later epoch needs another ordered grant. Thus a snapshot/revoked recipient never retains a key under which later wraps are legal. Handoff wraps metadata/keys rather than graph data but reports metadata and recipient cost. GC, backup/restore, and key destruction follow every live edge. Revocation cannot erase plaintext/keys already received and claims only prevention of future access.

Use cases remain what-if analysis, agent isolation, schema experiments, and reproducible feature snapshots. The 10k-branch objective is an empirical gate parameterized by retained deltas, key wraps, subscriptions, and lease cost—not an assumption embedded in correctness.

### 5.7 Scrubbing and self-healing

A background scrubber verifies record framing, authenticated headers, ciphertext digests, full logical digests after decode, and decode proofs; repairs missing symbols only within one `EncodingId`; and escalates insufficient local symbols to replica or backup recovery. Twenty-percent local repair overhead is an erasure budget inside the declared source-block/failure-domain placement model, not a promise against whole-device or correlated loss.

Two complementary coverage mechanisms are mandatory:

1. **Deterministic exhaustive sweeps** eventually cover every reachable encoding and provide the non-statistical detection guarantee.
2. **Keyed random sampling without replacement**, stratified by device, segment age, object kind, source block, and encoding profile, provides earlier statistical evidence. Sampling keys are committed after each sample epoch so an adversarial placement cannot predict the next sample. Every e-process record names its population, sampling design, dependence assumptions, alpha, and effective sample size; it is a statistical claim (`FG-CAL-*`), never proof that no corruption exists.

A CTMC-based MTTDL report remains useful as `FG-CFG-01`, with fitted failure rates, confidence/sensitivity ranges, repair bandwidth, placement assumptions, and model version. `fgdb doctor` may reject a deployment profile below its modeled target, but the result is labeled a configuration-model gate rather than an invariant. Optional donor possession challenges may trigger full audit or reseed; they prove responses to sampled challenges, not Byzantine correctness of the donor or semantic correctness of an object.


### 5.8 Verifiable to outsiders: the accumulator and transparency layer

Content addressing, the marker chain hash, and decode proofs make the database auditable *by its operator*. This layer cashes the same architecture into proofs a party who does **not** trust the server can check — the missing half of the trust story for agent memory (B6), cross-organization branches, and regulated pipelines:

1. **Global MMR scope.** The MMR commits the globally ordered marker entries with explicit leaf indices and tree size. Inclusion proves that one marker belongs to that committed history; consistency proves append-only extension relative to a previously trusted root. Neither proof establishes the semantic correctness of the capsule nor completeness of a filtered query result.
2. **Three transparency claims without branch-name leakage.** `LocalRollbackDetection` lets one client cache a signed checkpoint and reject rollback relative to its own last root; it says nothing cross-client. `WitnessedEquivocationDetection` requires authenticated gossip or cross-log receipts and promises detection/evidence after inconsistent heads meet, not prevention. Only `WitnessedNonEquivocation { witness_policy_ref }` may claim split-view prevention. Its content-addressed `WitnessPolicy` fixes one log/security-domain identity, the exact ordered witness keys, `n`, threshold `t`, Byzantine bound `f`, signature/consistency protocol, state-persistence/anti-rollback rule, predecessor and joint rotation, activation log size, maximum checkpoint age, and optional cross-log authorities. It is valid only when `2t > n + f`, so any two signing quorums intersect in more than `f` witnesses, and every honest witness durably remembers one head per log/policy, verifies an append-only consistency proof from that head, and never signs two roots at one size or non-extending histories. A policy rotation checkpoint needs both old and new valid quorums before the new policy activates. Checkpoints strongly name the policy and exact keyed signatures/cross-log receipts. If intersection, durable witness state, consistency proofs, or freshness fails, the API downgrades to detection/local scope or fails closed—it never labels later gossip as preventive non-equivocation. Branch identities/heads remain visible only through capability-authorized proofs or explicit metadata declassification; witnesses sign opaque domain commitments without learning branch names.
3. **Feed proof scopes.** Raw CDC over the global log can prove continuity with contiguous leaf/range proofs. A `SUBSCRIBE MATCH` frame can prove membership of its source commits, but not that the server evaluated the predicate completely. Filtered completeness is claimed only if each commit carries an authenticated, capability-domain-specific delta commitment—including an empty commitment—and the client receives a complete range of those commitments. Otherwise the API labels the proof `membership_only`.
4. **Proof-carrying transfer.** Backup and replica transfer archives object inventories, full digests, `EncodingId`s, key wraps, and decode proofs. Those prove byte closure and successful decode; restore additionally verifies the canonical logical checkpoint digest before promotion (§16).
5. **Authenticated point reads.** A sealed authorized namespace may expose Merkleized index roots, but a proof covers only the specified key/value and root. Absence, range completeness, capability projection, and freshness each require their corresponding proof and watermark.

FG-INV-08 requires authenticated global-history continuity. Non-equivocation is conditional on satisfying the declared witnessed-transparency policy and is not claimed in local-only mode.

---

## 6. Strata: The Storage Engine (Bet B2)

Strata resolves the write/scan/space trilemma by refusing to pick one point on it. Authoritative incidence is partitioned by stable vertex identity and edge type, never by mutable labels. Each `(vertex, direction, edge_type)` adjacency exists across three tiers, migrating by temperature.

### 6.1 Topology of the store

```
                       VERTEX DIRECTORY (per stable partition)
       snapshot ordinal → { stable VId, label-set ref, prop locator, sparse descriptor-table ref }
       packed ordinal maps + membership indexes; canonical constraint map for external keys
                                        │
        ┌───────────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────┐
        ▼                               ▼                                     ▼
  TIER D: DELTA (immutable published  TIER R: SEALED RUNS (immutable)   TIER A: CHECKPOINTS (ECS, cold)
  versions; mutable staging only)
  sorted 256-edge blocks              per-(partition,type,dir) runs     full compressed partition
  per-block MVCC version chains       per-list codec tags +             snapshots + logical effects
  hub vertices: skip-list of blocks   delta-varint neighbor gaps        (time travel / restore /
  hot-burst overflow log (bounded)    stable-EId-keyed property         replica seeding)
  volatile latch-free staging,        chunks; zone maps;
  immutable roots at publication      optional per-run bitmap ("holes")
        │            ▲                          ▲
        └─ seal ─────┘── compact (k-way merge, generational) ──┘
```

- **Tier I (inline micro-adjacency)**: below the diagram's three tiers sits a zeroth one. A small bounded vector in the vertex row stores the first few active `(direction, edge_type, descriptor)` entries; the descriptor may inline up to eight `(dst_VId, EId, prop_locator)` incidences. Mutable tiers never store a bare snapshot ordinal. Additional edge types live in a sparse immutable descriptor table, so schema cardinality cannot bloat every row. Overflow promotes to Tier D; demotion is a verified representation transition.
- **A logical adjacency list = merge(inline slot, delta blocks, [newest…oldest] sealed runs)**, exactly an LSM, except runs are graph-shaped and sorted by `(src_snapshot_ordinal, dst_snapshot_ordinal, EId)`. Tombstones and run holes carry creation/retirement marker references or a lineage-pinned effective-interval sidecar; a branch-agnostic scalar retire sequence or current hole bitmap may never hide an edge from a sibling branch or older snapshot. Compression-ratio numbers are benchmark results tied to named corpora and encodings, not universal facts.
- **Direction**: canonical forward runs always; reverse runs are declared synchronously maintained materializations enabled by default and may be disabled per edge type only with the registered reverse-scan fallback. Every present/required reverse family must equal the transpose of authorized forward incidence at each snapshot; disabling it changes performance, never semantics.
- **Partitioning**: runs are segmented by stable source partition and snapshot-ordinal ranges—the unit of compaction, buffering, statistics, checksums, and parallel scans. Labels use separate membership bitmaps and derived Beacon projections. Source-range ownership is an edge-cut/vertex-owner layout; a future hub-splitting vertex-cut mode is a different protocol and is named separately in §14.6.

### 6.2 Tier D internals

1. **Sorted edge blocks** (Sortledton lesson): the durable unit is immutable `DeltaBlockVersion {format,partition_id,descriptor_key,stripe_range,sorted_entries[],visibility_intervals[],property_patch_refs[],predecessor:ConditionalCoordinateRef<DeltaBlockVersion>?,canonical_logical_digest}`. A block is about 4 KiB and holds at most 256 `(dst_VId,EId,user_key_ref?,prop_row_ref,flags)` entries sorted by stable identity; binary search and SIMD lower-bound use canonical stable-key encoding. `DeltaPartitionRoot {partition_id,generation,descriptor_map_ref,sorted_block_head_refs[],overflow_state:Empty|Drained{through_commit_seq},canonical_partition_digest}` and immutable skip-list nodes represent a vertex's zero, one, or hub-sized two-level block family. Every reference is typed and every published root is content-addressed.
2. **Per-block MVCC**: a published block head reaches an immutable predecessor chain; no durable bump-arena index or process pointer appears in canonical bytes. Readers continue down the chain until the first version satisfying **all** sequence, branch-ancestry, schema, retirement, and own-write visibility predicates; a newer sibling-branch version is skipped rather than terminating the search. The current-line fast path may collapse this to one compare only under a verified lineage token. Process-local `VersionArena`/`prev_idx` layouts are discardable decoded caches for those immutable objects, never the authoritative chain.
3. **Concurrency, staging, and visibility**: eager block locks, latch-free transaction-private nodes, bump arenas, and EBR are strictly volatile staging machinery. A writer may build a candidate from those nodes, but before any logical state/root/RootSlot can name the result it must canonicalize and seal complete `DeltaBlockVersion` and `DeltaPartitionRoot` objects, verify their logical digest against the committed effects/marker, and root the immutable partition generation atomically with the candidate state. Publication never stamps or mutates an old object or authoritative pointer. Abort drops only volatile staging; crash recovery discards every unrooted arena/overflow node and deterministically reconstructs from the Chronicle command/effect suffix. Readers merge committed immutable roots plus their own private overlay; another transaction's staging is unobservable. Giant hubs stripe the neighbor-ID space into independently locked/versioned candidate ranges, and witness granularity follows the durable stripe identity.
4. **Hot-burst overflow**: a bounded per-partition append log may absorb spikes only as volatile, transaction-tagged staging. The drain actor preserves commit order and verifies the canonical logical digest while producing immutable blocks; the same root-publication barrier applies. The log is neither a durable source of truth nor recoverable state, and admission backpressures before memory is exhausted. A future durable overflow representation would require a separately registered immutable object and state transition; none exists in v1.
5. **Property deltas** live beside adjacency deltas as row-patches; sealed property data is columnar (§6.4).

### 6.3 Tier R internals (sealed runs)

- **Layout per run segment**: header (fenceposts, stats, checksum, seq-range, `source_ordinal_map_id`, `destination_map_table[]`) · Elias–Fano offsets for O(1) list location · per-list `NeighborCodec` chosen from `EliasFano`, `StreamVByte { skip_table }`, or `DenseIntervals` · stable EIds/`OriginBirthOrder`s and replaceable property locators · versioned marker-aware hole/retire metadata. A source ordinal is meaningful only under the source map. Each encoded destination is either stable VId or `(destination_map_slot, dst_ordinal)`, where the slot names an explicit `{ destination_partition, OrdinalMapId }`; no ordinal crosses a map boundary untagged. Codec/map choice is covered by the logical-digest validator over stable IDs.
- **Compressed intersections with an honest contract**: Elias–Fano neighbor lists support rank/select directly. StreamVByte lists use skip/fence metadata and bounded blockwise decode; dense intervals use interval arithmetic. Loom intersects without **full-list** decompression where the codec permits it—there is no claim that Elias–Fano offsets provide rank/select over a separate varint stream.
- **Runs are generational**: seal (Tier D → R₀ run), then merge R₀…R_k per partition. A snapshot pins run generations via epochs; compaction publishes a new segment set atomically in the manifest and retires the old under lease — readers never block, never see mixed generations.
- **The merge policy is a governed family, not a constant**: per `(partition, edge_type, direction)`, a bounded leveled↔tiered family is evaluated in shadow and deployed as a pinned deterministic table; static size-tiering is the permanent fallback. Birth–death and stability analyses are named configuration models with sensitivity bounds, while dwell/hysteresis and measured churn are runtime guards. They do not prove universal absence of oscillation.

### 6.4 Property storage

Vertex property chunks are grouped by `(stable partition, property/storage family)`, not mutable label. Label scans apply versioned membership bitmaps before reading rows. Edge chunks are grouped by `(edge_type, property, run generation)` and sequential by replaceable run row, with a stable EId sidecar. Published Tier-D patches are immutable objects and obey the same MVCC/branch visibility rules; mutable row-patch buffers are staging only. Embedding matrices are generation-pinned inputs to vector indexes; “zero-copy” is used only when requested dtype, alignment, authorization, and snapshot generation actually match.

### 6.5 Vertex directory

Per stable partition and generation, a packed array maps snapshot-local dense ordinal to `{ stable VId, label-set ref, property locator, small active-descriptor vector, sparse descriptor-table ref }`; a reverse map resolves VId to that generation's ordinal. IDs are never recycled (§4.5). Degree is O(1) per **authorized** descriptor only after Warden masking; unauthorized edge types do not contribute. Directory and label-membership segments are versioned immutable objects.

### 6.6 Write amplification & space discipline

Write amplification is `all physical bytes written / canonical logical input bytes` and includes canonical forward plus any configured reverse-incidence materializations, properties, constraint and optimizer indexes, checkpoints, FEC, staging waste, and every merge level; reports publish the component breakdown. Space amplification names the logical baseline and includes key wraps, repair symbols, and retained history. Numerical targets in §17 are benchmark gates, not format truths. Every representation migration emits a decision card with state, candidates, cost interval, minimum dwell, uncertainty, and pinned deterministic fallback.

Under Sextant (the calibration discipline within B5, §15.0), the card machinery adds statistical evidence without changing safety semantics:

- **Migration evidence is sequential, while dwell remains a hard guard.** An SPRT may evaluate promote/demote evidence under an explicit observation model and loss matrix; its reported error rates are conditional on those assumptions. Minimum dwell and benefit-greater-than-conversion-cost-plus-uncertainty remain deterministic anti-thrash rules even when the model is invalid.
- **Policies remain on trial.** An e-process may compare a policy with its pinned fallback on a declared outcome stream. Promotion evidence is `FG-CAL-01`; failure of assumptions or evidence reverts to the fallback through a stream-sequenced `PolicyEpoch`. It is not a production safety-invariant checker.
