Hidden descriptors and rows may affect neither enumeration order, empty/nonempty, degree, pagination, routing, plan/certificate fields, errors, timing class, statistics, nor cache identity. A mandatory differential oracle compares a database containing hidden descriptors with the same visible subgraph after physically removing them and requires byte-identical visible results, plans exposed to the caller, padded error classes, and observable metadata.

### 12.4 Derived state, caches, and errors

One canonical type keys every persisted or reusable derived object:

`DerivedIdentity { database_security_namespace_id, cluster_incarnation, kind, definition_oid, source_coverage: sorted Vec<DerivedSourceCoverage { input_role_id, source_relation_id, base_binding: CoordinateSchemaBinding, tracking_mode: Fixed|Advancing, lineage_digest }>, global_batch_frontier?, authority_digest, policy_semantics_oid, policy_epoch, revocation_index, topology_epoch, language_contract_oid?, semantic_profile_oid, scalar_profile_oid, collation_profile_oid?, redaction_profile_oid, build_profile_oid }`.

Fields irrelevant to a kind are explicit canonical `None`, never ambient defaults. View, index, statistics, subscription, plan/result cache, `DerivedGenerationRegistry`, certificate, and replay schemas embed this exact identity or its digest plus a strong reference to the identity object. A lookup must match all fields before applying an explicitly registered tail/rebuild rule; no singular graph/head/schema key may stand in for a coordinate set. Derived objects carry an `AuthorityReuseLaw`, not a bare subset slogan. Row-complete raw caches may derive a narrower domain only through an authorization-preserving projection that also masks metadata. Aggregates, cardinalities, sketches, BM25 statistics, DP results, and constraint outcomes require exact-domain state or a proved sufficient decomposition; HNSW/graph-routing topology requires exact authorized topology or a separately proved filter-aware construction. Definer views pin definer authority plus result-exposure policy; invoker state is authority-partitioned. Revocation or incarnation advance removes reachability even if bytes remain cached. Hardened errors use bounded capability-safe classes; plans, abort reports, witnesses, timing padding, and telemetry are redacted before crossing the boundary.

### 12.5 Encryption and key lifecycle

Logical, ciphertext, FEC-encoding, and placement identities are defined separately in §5.1. One random object DEK encrypts one `CiphertextId`; that ciphertext may have several `EncodingId` FEC realizations. Sharing adds recipient/database/branch/replica/backup wraps rather than re-encrypting the object. Branch sharing and handoff use only §5.6/Appendix A's typed envelope DAG: fork atomically closes and rotates both parent envelope/write epochs, every object-DEK wrap binds its source epoch and creation boundary, and a recipient grant opens one exact rooted/cut closure. A bare KEK, ambiguous branch DEK, or inherited still-active parent epoch is invalid. `CryptoCx` obtains production entropy independently of deterministic replay seeds, and secret entropy is never exported in incident bundles. Local data-key states are `Generated -> Active -> Retiring -> RetainedDecryptOnly -> DestroyPending{quarantine_generation,target_set_digest} -> DestroyedPendingCertificate -> Destroyed`; token/signing revocation is separate. RetainedDecryptOnly forbids new encryption/wrap grants but opens every reachable object. `KeyDestroyProposal` proves an exact typed root/configuration/backup/legal-hold scan and its applied command atomically installs DestroyPending as a no-new-reference quarantine plus one durable idempotent requested operation for every and only planned KMS/HSM/storage target before any physical call. Every encoder, prepared owner, backup, grant, configuration proposal, and root publisher rejects a new retaining use of the quarantined key. Recovery queries/retries each same operation ID; process death never invents another request or treats timeout as success. `KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec` recomputes the complete generated inventory against the exact current payload/root slots/configuration and consumes an authenticated one-to-one target/receipt set; it creates a compact result and `DestroyedPendingCertificate`. After that result and its audit mirror exist, a quorum may sign a certificate, and a distinct ordered certificate-publication command alone selects final `Destroyed`. Heavy scan/proposal/finalize closure retires only after certificate publication, both required audit mirrors, and an activated cut, while the compact result/receipt commitment/certificate remains. No pre-order object names its future result or certificate. The crypto contract also pins algorithm agility, nonce/SIV mode, AAD digest, passphrase KDF parameters, KMS/HSM mode, rotation, zeroization, replica provisioning, backup escrow, signing-key rotation, and crypto-erasure limits.

Cryptographic primitives require published vectors, constant-time/side-channel testing, misuse tests, independent expert review, and a release-blocking external audit. Where an audited foundation primitive exists, it is preferred. “Built in-house” never means unaudited cryptography is accepted merely because functional vectors pass.

### 12.6 Leakage and redaction

Timing/cardinality/error leakage is acknowledged. Padding, quantization, pools, and bounded errors are mitigations. Any mutual-information or channel-capacity result is a deployment-specific `StatisticalClaim` naming secret distribution, attacker observations, concurrency assumptions, padding schedule, sampling design, confidence bound, and identity-level cumulative budget; adversarial CI fixtures do not prove universal noninterference or a global bits/query ceiling.

### 12.7 Differential privacy

DP authority binds `PrivacyPrincipalId`, an explicit vertex- or edge-neighboring relation, contribution bounds, mechanism/query fingerprint, and an identity-level ledger spanning tokens and aliases. Each population/accounting trust domain has a stable `PrivacyAccountingDomainId` that normally survives cluster incarnations, same-identity restores, branches, and backups. Canonical `DpRequestKey` binds that domain, principal/authority, database security namespace, request nonce/idempotency identity, logical root and exact `GraphReferenceBinding[]`, normalized bound query and parameters, neighboring relation, clipping/contribution bounds, mechanism/version/parameters, policy/revocation epochs, and output encoding; cluster incarnation is recorded as provenance but does not create a fresh accounting domain or erase an existing request tombstone.

Privacy accounting has an external monotonic authority analogous to ID continuity but specialized to irreversible composition. Before any sensitive data access, a threshold-authenticated CAS registry atomically advances `PrivacyContinuityRecord { privacy_accounting_domain_id, privacy_epoch, cumulative_renyi_state_commitment, request_tombstone_root, predecessor_digest, external_registry_id, cas_version, status, issued_at, signer_set_epoch, threshold_signatures }`, records the exact request key and debit, and returns an `ExternalPrivacyChargeReceipt`. The debit cannot be rolled back or refunded. Chronicle then orders a typed DP charge command containing that receipt and mirrors the exact external head in `PrivacyLedgerState`/`LogicalStateRoot`; only after both the external CAS and local/consensus charge transition are durable may execution observe data, data-dependent timing, or a query-specific error. A crash after external CAS but before local mirroring leaves a charged orphan that recovery must import/reconcile—it never restores the budget. The database disables DP and fails closed whenever the external head is unavailable, behind, forked, or inconsistent.

The uniqueness-serialized durable machine is `Prepared{no_sensitive_access,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq} -> Charged{budget_debit,external_charge_receipt_ref,encrypted_seed_ref,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq} -> Computing{same_charge_and_seed,attempt_generation,no_output=true,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq} -> ResultCommitted{same_charge_and_seed,encrypted_result_ref,result_digest,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq} -> Delivered{same_charge_seed_result_refs,result_digest,delivery_receipt_digest,delivery_channel_class,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq}`; only `Prepared` may transition to `Abandoned{stable_reason,applied_command_ref,applied_logical_command_seq}`. Each input `DpTransitionSpec` is sequence-neutral and each result names the already identified `ControlCommand`, never its future `LogicalCommandRecord`. Every transition advances logical-command time. Cancellation/crash after charge consumes the budget and recovery/retry resumes with the same protected seed; if retained seed/result state cannot be reconciled after restore, the old request fails `DpStateUnavailable` and cannot draw new noise under that key. Result, seed, receipts, and necessary key wraps are strong through the privacy/retry floor; no output or data-dependent completion signal precedes `ResultCommitted`. Concurrent retries wait on the same key or return its committed result. No independent hedge, stale-follower budget, or duplicate execution may draw another sample.

A same-identity restore must reconcile to the latest external privacy head and import every post-backup debit/tombstone before DP is enabled; advancing `cluster_incarnation` is not sufficient. A clone gets a new privacy domain only when an approved policy proves the protected populations and identities are disjoint; otherwise it remains in the source domain and inherits its cumulative state. Rényi composition, reservation recovery/retention, collusion boundary, branch/snapshot/clone composition, and allowed aggregate catalog are normative. Motifs or arbitrary queries remain unavailable until sensitivity and clipping are proved. Budget refusal is structured and never silently changes epsilon or mechanism.

### 12.8 Audit

Compliance audit is a separately retained, signed append-only chain—not “whatever commit history remains.” Signatures, sequence continuity, and anchoring prove **append integrity and post-ticket gap/truncation detection**, not that a buggy or compromised ingress could never omit an event before logging. Each same-identity lineage has a stable `AuditDomainId`. An external monotonic authority CAS-publishes `AuditContinuityRecord { database_security_namespace_id, audit_domain_id, audit_epoch, highest_ticket_sequence, ticket_index_commitment, unresolved_ticket_commitment, audit_chain_head_digest, predecessor_digest, external_registry_id, cas_version, status:Complete{profile_oid}|PermanentGap{latest_transition_ref,current_profile_oid}, last_transition:TicketIssued{ticket_digest}|TicketResolved{ticket_digest,resolution_digest,event_digest,candidate_root_digest:WeakDigest}|CompletenessChanged{transition_ref}, signer_set_epoch, threshold_signatures }`, while retaining authenticated ticket/event/resolution/CAS-receipt bytes or authenticated resolver references—not commitments alone.

An `AuditCompletenessProfile` names which operations require an externally reserved `AuditTicket` before protected processing. Ticket issuance first CAS-adds a pending ticket externally, then orders its local mirror through exact `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec { ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>, expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>, expected_prior_cas_version, returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>, external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt> }`. Admission verifies that the returned record and receipt are the direct `TicketIssued` CAS successor, advance the expected ticket sequence by one, add exactly this ticket to the ticket-index and unresolved commitments, and change no unrelated continuity field; orphan-ticket recovery uses the same relation. Protected processing begins only after that local mirror is visible.

Protected construction has four explicit, noninterchangeable orders. **Local admitted transaction:** ticket admission/claim -> authorization/final rebase/outcome preparation -> ordered final-certification reservation plus coordinate/obligation holds -> sequence-neutral audit event/resolution bodies and immutable semantic plan -> replaceable event attempt/locks/shares/event -> replaceable resolution attempt/locks/shares/resolution -> triple-bearing `TerminalAuditGate` -> stable capsule/template/semantic prepared closure -> repeatable `LocalOrderAttemptInput` plus availability certificate -> command/order/candidate. **Local control or pre-effect terminal:** ticket/claim -> authorization -> `AuditTerminalFreezeSpec::Arm` plus generated control-basis hold -> the same body/semantic-plan/replaceable-attempt triple -> stable typed control base -> repeatable Local order supplement -> command/order/candidate. **W12 admitted write:** ticket/registration claim -> union authorization/resources/gate-free outcome preparation -> published admission -> shard fragments/prepares/constraints/serialization -> ordered Global final-certification reservation/holds -> audit semantic plan and replaceable event/resolution attempts -> gate -> stable Meta command base -> repeatable `MetaOrderAttemptInput` -> Global command/candidate. **Read in either posture:** ticket/claim -> read admission -> authorized traversal/buffered result -> release decision -> freeze/hold where state-changing publication requires it -> audit bodies/attempts/gate -> stable publication/read-close base -> role order supplement -> candidate -> mirror -> output. Thus Local outcome preparation carries its eventual gate, W12 preparation never does, a read-release decision cannot authorize the traversal that produced it, and neither HLC nor assigned order appears in signed audit bodies.

The event binds the exact ticket request, namespace/domain/profile/principal, authorization decision, and one tagged outcome commitment: `TransactionMutation { final_effect_digest, transaction_effect_basis_commitment }`, `ControlMutation { control_kind, spec_body_digest, expected_state_conditions_digest, semantic_transition_basis_commitment }`, canonical read result, denial, or stable failure/no-effect proof. `transaction_effect_basis_commitment` hashes only the sequence-neutral final effect, role-free coordinate/head expectations, schema/constraint/resource/authorization inputs, intent semantics, and transaction token; it explicitly excludes capsule/command/certificate identities, `TerminalAuditGate`, assigned sequence/HLC/marker identity, and chain hash. `spec_body_digest` hashes only canonical `SequenceNeutralSpec.spec_body`, excluding its terminal gate; `semantic_transition_basis_commitment` hashes the deterministic pre-order before/after relation expressed by that body and expected conditions, never an applied record/root identity. Event and resolution attestation times are pre-order signer observations, not the apply-assigned `logical_command_hlc`; expected sequence/state conditions make a stale prebuilt terminal fail closed. `AuditTicketResolution` is a tagged terminal in which `Completed`, `Denied`, and `Failed` each strongly name that exact event; `Abandoned` carries a signed typed no-effect reason and proof. There is no optional unbound `event_digest`.

State-changing apply verifies the complete staged signing chain and gate byte-for-byte and proves the later full spec/capsule/command/marker/result is the unique deterministic extension of those sequence-neutral commitments. `AuditVisibilityFence` is the closed posture union `Local{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,blocked_after_order:Local{logical_command_seq},candidate_state_root_ref:StrongRef<LogicalStateRoot>,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>}|Meta{ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,blocked_after_order:Meta{global_logical_command_seq},candidate_state_root_ref:StrongRef<GlobalStateRoot>,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>}`. Apply constructs only that unpublished candidate/fence and leaves the visible root/closed-read prefix before the protected command. While the one role-global prefix fence is active, the coordinator admits only its exact audit mirror/recovery commands and Raft maintenance; unrelated mutations cannot accumulate behind it.

The external sequencer CAS-resolves exactly that pending ticket and returns an authenticated direct-successor continuity record plus `AuditExternalCasReceipt`. The only command that can clear either posture's fence is `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec {active_fence_digest:WeakDigest,ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>,candidate:AuditCandidateRef,terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution>,expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,expected_prior_cas_version,returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>,external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt>}`. Apply byte-matches the active fence selected by the candidate's Local/Meta tag and verifies role/group, namespace/domain/profile/principal/request/outcome/final-effect equality; the returned continuity record must be the direct CAS successor of the expected head, remove exactly this ticket from unresolved state, and commit the exact resolution, event, candidate root, and receipt. Only then does the matching local or meta mirror command produce and publish the final root containing both candidate effects and the mirrored continuity head. A valid but stale, unrelated, wrong-role, or merely signed head cannot clear anything. No leader/follower snapshot, result frame or error, changefeed, observable system-graph/metric detail, or acknowledgement may cross the fence earlier. Read-only protected work similarly buffers output until terminal CAS plus the matching mirror. Recovery replays the same idempotent relation before lifting a fence.

Audit lifecycle commands cannot recurse through their own gate. `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec`, `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec`, and narrowly scoped `AuditRecoverySpec`/`AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec` have `TerminalAuditGate::StructurallyInapplicable{AuditSystemAuthority}` in their sole sequence-neutral wrapper; `AuditTerminalSpec { ticket_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicket>, expected_pending_ticket_digest:WeakDigest, event_ref:StrongRef<AuditEventRecord>, terminal_resolution_ref:StrongRef<AuditTicketResolution> }` consumes exactly that already-pending ticket and may not request another. `AuditTerminalSpec` is for non-mutating and pre-effect terminal paths, not a second mutation terminal. Every transaction command carries its one terminal gate in its transaction input, while every control command obtains its one Required, validated NotRequired, or StructurallyInapplicable gate only through its referenced spec wrapper; no command-level duplicate exists. If required external evidence is unavailable, gated work remains disabled. Resumption first builds and threshold-signs an immutable pre-CAS `AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord { audit_domain_id, prior_continuity_ref, exact_missing_ticket_or_event_interval, missing_commitment, evidence_or_reason, old_profile_oid, new_profile_oid, permanent_effective_audit_epoch, authorization, signer_set_epoch, threshold_signatures }`; the external authority CAS-installs a direct-successor continuity record that commits it, then emits a separate `AuditExternalCasReceipt`, and finally `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec { transition_ref:StrongRef<AuditCompletenessTransitionRecord>, expected_prior_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>, expected_prior_cas_version, returned_continuity_ref:StrongRef<AuditContinuityRecord>, external_cas_receipt_ref:StrongRef<AuditExternalCasReceipt> }` mirrors that exact pair locally. This order is acyclic. The continuity status and future profile validator permanently exclude the recorded gap; no later operator, restore, or profile change may reassert completeness across it. `LogicalStatePayload`, checkpoints, configuration/GC/key floors, and backups strongly retain the active continuity/transition chain and authenticated external locators. Same-identity restore reconciles the complete externally available history and every permanent-gap record before ticket-gated operations resume. Only events admitted through this gate receive a source-completeness claim within the trusted-process threat model. Unticketed/sampled read telemetry is labeled non-complete. The chain records successful and denied authentication/authorization, queries at the configured detail, mutations, DDL, token/key/policy changes, backup/export/restore, and replication administration, with explicit redaction and access rules.

---

## 13. Fabric: Server, Protocols, and the Embedded API

1. **Embedded**: `fgdb::Database::open(path | :memory:)` returns an incarnation/service-epoch-guarded handle only from an Operational root backed by the current service-promotion receipt; hidden restore and `RetiredLocal` reject ordinary open. Authorized sessions expose prepared statements and explicit transactions with begin idempotency, statement sequence/key/class, pinned error policy, and certified workspace generation. Execution returns only an audit-visible `PublishedResultStream`; `finish`/ACK and Drop/cancellation drive the same typed delivery acknowledgement or release transition as FGP. `commit()` returns `WriteCommitted|ReadClosed|Aborted|Unknown`, never a marker-shaped read close, and `status(TxnOutcomeCapability)` resolves BeginStaging, detailed/compacted NeverRegistered, in-progress, terminal-pending, and detailed/compacted terminal-ready outcomes identically. Rust-native typed accessors and capability-gated procedures obey the same authorization and epoch boundary. `fgdb-python` consumes the allowed `fnx-python` binding boundary rather than adding PyO3 directly to engine crates; ABI3/NumPy support remains isolated from durable/runtime layers. A claimed NumPy view is zero-copy only for matching contiguous authorized buffers and otherwise returns an explicit copy.
2. **`fgdbd` server**: multi-database, multi-tenant by capability; connection admission via semaphore + rate-limit combinators; graceful drain on shutdown (region close = no dropped in-flight commits, structurally).
3. **FGP (native wire protocol)** uses Appendix D's sole connection machine: protocol-only HELLO, principal authentication, protected database selection, then a posture/incarnation/service-receipt-bound Ready state. Every role-sensitive identity and dispatch is an exact `Local|Sharded` union. BEGIN, autocommit, subscription creation, export, replay, result resume/ACK, unsubscribe, and E-to-E2 cursor migration are durably idempotent. Every protected result, baseline, delta, proof, replay/export byte, cancellation explanation, and data-dependent error is buffered until its exact authorization and `NotRequired|RequiredMirrored` audit-release evidence exists, then consumes a fresh linear `OutputSendGuard` immediately before each frame write. Transaction-bound statements are serialized in v1; unsupported savepoint, partial-rollback, or concurrent-statement profiles are rejected. Draining admits no new children and completes mirrors, typed delivery releases, cancellation, admitted-decision recovery, and terminal records before close. Appendix D's state, frame, retry, privacy, and posture rules are normative; adapters cannot weaken them.

   Ephemeral `stmt_id`, `stream_id`, delivery cursor, open-query, active-transaction, and transient-reservation handles are server-minted random or MACed capabilities scoped to protocol version, database security namespace, **cluster incarnation, service visibility epoch**, tenant, principal, non-widenable authority digest, session, and creation policy/revocation epochs. Prepared statements bind the `PreparedQueryTemplate` digest, language/catalog/schema compatibility contracts, and authority ceiling; each execution resolves a fresh `BoundQuery` and reauthorizes it. Exactly four durable authority-bearing capabilities deliberately survive connection loss: §9.5's `ResumeCapability`, §5.6's `MergeOutcomeCapability`, §14.3's `ReadYourWritesCapability`, and `TxnOutcomeCapability`.

   All four use the exact `DurableCapabilityHeader { capability_format_version,capability_kind,issuer_id,mac_key_id,mac_key_epoch,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,service_visibility_epoch,tenant,principal,non_widenable_authority_digest,issuance_policy_epoch,issuance_revocation_index,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,nonce }`; a capability is `{header,kind_specific_body,mac}`, and the domain-separated MAC covers the complete canonical header—including the time profile and both closed-open bounds—and body. The Txn body is exactly `{request_kind:ExplicitBegin|AutocommitExecute,scoped_request_idempotency_key_digest,txn_token,outcome_capability_key}` and is the body embedded by `TxnOutcomeCapabilityFields`; Resume, Merge, and ReadYourWrites bodies are exact below. The active transaction remains session-bound, but the outcome capability permits idempotent BEGIN recovery/status from a newly authenticated same-or-narrower session; the other three retain only their named surfaces. None can mutate an unrelated transaction, merge, stream, or restored incarnation. Rotation and expiry respect their promised outcome/cursor/prefix floors. Verifier-key records, accepted time profiles, and old decoders remain rooted through maximum live expiry/floor. Presentation first validates a fresh subject/action-bound `TimeValidationEvidence::Usable` and consumes its `TimeUseGuard`; expiry classification requires `Expired` evidence before protected lookup. `AUTH_REFRESH` affects only new work and cannot widen an open child; narrowing/revocation fences unsent output, while admitted commit still finishes through current terminal rules. A MAC-valid capability with the correct namespace/incarnation/service/principal binding but an expired header returns `TokenExpired` before outcome lookup, revealing nothing about record existence; bad MAC, unauthorized principal/authority, wrong profile/epoch/incarnation/service binding, or deliberately privacy-collapsed lookup returns uniform `NotVisibleOrUnknown`. A valid unexpired capability returns the exact posture-supported in-progress or terminal state.

   `TxnOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord` is the immutable compact replay object `{fields:TxnOutcomeCapabilityFields,canonical_capability_bytes,capability_commitment,canonical_request_digest,request_kind,scoped_request_idempotency_key_digest,txn_token,outcome_capability_key,issuer_and_verifier_key_epoch,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,minimum_begin_retry_floor,body_digest:BodyDigest<TxnOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord>}`. Its registered body transcript includes every field except `body_digest` and requires the stored bytes to decode to `fields` and reproduce every repeated value, MAC, and commitment. It is built before a begin/autocommit reservation and never points to reservation, attempt, outcome, summary, or root. Detailed and compacted begin lineages strongly retain it so a lost acceptance response reproduces byte-identical capability bytes across restart and key/profile rotation. Only an evidence-bound expiry transition may replace that edge with a permanent nonreuse tombstone; after that a valid old capability returns TokenExpired rather than being reissued.

   `ResumeCapabilityReplayRecord` is the immutable union-backed replay object `{fields:{header:DurableCapabilityHeader{capability_kind=Resume},body:ResumeCapabilityBody},canonical_capability_bytes,capability_commitment,subject_basis:SubscriptionCursor{cursor_creation_request_digest,resume_cursor_id,cursor_state_version,public_state_commitment}|BufferedResult{posture,owner_basis:ResultDeliveryLeaseOwnerBasis,result_delivery_id,lease_generation,delivery_state_version,canonical_result_digest},capability_generation,lineage,issuer_id,mac_key_id,mac_key_epoch,issuance_policy_epoch,issuance_revocation_index,verifier_key_ref:StrongRef<DurableCapabilityVerifierKey>,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,minimum_resume_or_result_floor,body_digest:BodyDigest<ResumeCapabilityReplayRecord>}`. The stored bytes must decode to the repeated fields, body arm, MAC, and commitment. Cursor/result creation and every rotate/ACK/release transition prebuild the exact successor record without pointing to its future state transition, then atomically install that record. Current and immediate-predecessor lineage retains the necessary replay records; evidence-bound expiry/consumption alone replaces them with permanent tombstones.

   `MergeOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord` is `{fields:{header:DurableCapabilityHeader{capability_kind=MergeOutcome},body:{merge_prepare_id,merge_request_idempotency_key_digest,target_graph_branch_binding_digest,capability_generation,outcome_capability_key}},canonical_capability_bytes,capability_commitment,canonical_merge_request_digest,issuer_id,mac_key_id,mac_key_epoch,issuance_policy_epoch,issuance_revocation_index,verifier_key_ref:StrongRef<DurableCapabilityVerifierKey>,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,minimum_merge_outcome_lookup_floor,body_digest:BodyDigest<MergeOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord>}`. `MergePrepareSpec` strongly names this prebuilt record; prepare/detail/compacted/tombstone states retain or retire it by the same exact rules as transaction outcomes. It replaces every partial generation/nonce/key-epoch/expiry tuple elsewhere in this plan.

   `ReadYourWritesCapabilityReplayRecord` is `{fields:{header:DurableCapabilityHeader{capability_kind=ReadYourWrites},body:{posture:Local|Sharded,txn_outcome_capability_commitment,registration_identity,terminal_marker_identity:WeakMarkerIdentity,minimum_visible_logical_position:PostureLogicalPosition,committed_branch_head_commitment,read_authority_ceiling_digest,capability_generation}},canonical_capability_bytes,capability_commitment,issuer_id,mac_key_id,mac_key_epoch,issuance_policy_epoch,issuance_revocation_index,verifier_key_ref:StrongRef<DurableCapabilityVerifierKey>,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,minimum_visibility_and_lookup_floor,body_digest:BodyDigest<ReadYourWritesCapabilityReplayRecord>}`. It is prebuilt in terminal completion, issued only with `TerminalReady`, and retained by the outcome/replay floor until evidence-bound expiry. It authorizes waiting/reading at the exact committed visibility floor under the same-or-narrower authority; it is not a mutation or broader snapshot capability. For all four durable capability kinds, restart, compaction, verifier-key/profile rotation, lost response, current/immediate-predecessor retry, expiry, and unauthorized substitution tests compare exact canonical bytes.

   `FrameLimits` bounds encoded and uncompressed bytes, compression ratio, nesting, columns, parameters, FEC symbols, streams, in-flight bytes, result rows/bytes, and idle time. The decoder validates declared sizes and reserves resources before allocating or FEC decoding. Authentication follows protected transport and transcript-bound negotiation. Compression is disabled for mixed attacker-controlled/secret frames unless a reviewed profile permits it. Factorized frames carry canonical authorized values, never run references. Session types enforce order; runtime validators enforce values, epochs, authorization, and resource bounds. Appendix D is normative, not a sketch.
4. **HTTP/2 + gRPC + WebSocket** (asupersync http): query endpoint, subscription streams, health/metrics, bulk import/export endpoints (multipart or ATP bonded pull).
5. **Bolt-compat subset** (`fgdb-bolt`): enough of Bolt v5 + Neo4j type mapping to let standard Neo4j drivers and visualization tools connect for read/query workloads — the adoption wedge. Documented divergence table; not the native path.
6. **QoS and admission** separates ephemeral runtime reservations from durable quota state. A hierarchical `ResourceVector { cpu_ns, resident_bytes, temp_bytes, durable_bytes, read_iops, write_iops, egress_bytes, output_bytes, output_rows, snapshot_age, branch/index/view/subscription counts, subscription_backlog }` is reserved before transient work and released by obligation. Durable bytes/branches/indexes/views/subscriptions/history are enforced by an authoritative Chronicle-sequenced `ResourceLedgerState`; every create/grow/delete/expiry carries `ResourceReservationId` plus canonical `ResourceChargeEffect`/release in the same final capsule as the durable object change (§5.2). Concurrent sessions therefore serialize quota validation with publication, and crash recovery replays charge and object atomically. Maintenance has protected emergency reserves. Hedging is allowed only within ephemeral reservations and never chooses strict logical order by wall-clock race; DP work forbids independent hedges.
7. **Formats and migration** (`fgdb-formats`) import the declared fnx/CSV/JSONL/Parquet-lite profiles under explicit size, recursion, schema, and decompression limits. A `.fgdb` archive is a signed `BackupManifest` plus exact root/head, object inventory, base dependencies, key wraps, format/profile epochs, and transparency checkpoint. Decode proofs alone do not establish backup completeness or semantic validity (§16).
8. **Deterministic extensibility:** replicated/apply/merge logic is limited to validated Datalog or the fuel/memory/stack-bounded deterministic bytecode VM with mediated authority and pinned arithmetic. Native Rust procedures remain embedded-host extensions and are categorically barred from replicated logical effects, merge/apply, constraints, and replay-guaranteed queries; a conformance test cannot prove arbitrary native code deterministic. Native read procedures receive authorized views and are labeled external nondeterminism unless their outputs are excluded from strict replay.
9. **CDC export** sends canonical committed logical deltas with stable idempotency tokens and at-least-once delivery. Raw global feeds may attach contiguous-range proofs; filtered feeds label membership versus completeness exactly as §5.8 requires. External sinks provide their own transactional/idempotent boundary.

---

## 14. Aegis: Replication, HA, and the Distribution Doctrine

**Doctrine:** single-node correctness is the base product; replication adds crash-fault durability, availability, and read scale. Canonical logical effects/digests agree across replicas, but repair ESIs, ciphertext encodings, cache state, and physical placement need not be byte-identical. Horizontal sharding is a post-1.0 protocol workstream, not a configuration toggle.

1. **One commit state machine with durable Raft state.** §5.2 remains authoritative in one-member and multi-member configurations. Transactions advance through `Draft -> Validated -> FinalPrepared -> PreparedRootDurable -> PayloadAvailable -> Proposed(term,index) -> CommandCommitted -> Applied(logical_command_ref,marker_ref) -> Acknowledged`. Consensus commits the normative strongly referenced `CommitCommand`; the standalone `CommitMarker`, `LogicalStatePayload`, `LogicalCommandRecord`, and outer state root are deterministically created in that acyclic order after `LogicalCommandSeq`/`CommitSeq`/HLC assignment. Before proposal, each donor has root-published its `PreparedCommitRecord`, and the leader collects signed/MACed `PayloadReceipt`s binding stable `PreparedOwnershipId`, base-closure digest, and exact `EncodingId`/`PlacementId` coverage in named failure domains. The canonical `PayloadAvailabilityCertificate` proves the configured recoverability predicate—including quorum one—and is a strong command edge.

   Raft persistence obeys the no-extra-mutable-file doctrine. Appendix A's exact role-tagged `RaftLogSegment`, `RaftHardState`, `RaftSnapshot`, `RaftStateRoot`, configuration, certificate, prepared-root, and audit-fence formats all carry the database/security-namespace/incarnation/role/group domain; no abbreviated ambient schema is normative here. A node syncs the new closure before vote/append/receipt/durability replies. Recovery reconciles log ownership, validates exact command/payload closure, and idempotently applies committed work. The generated log-to-state verifier proves the exact role-specific root/config/prefix at a cut; no later root pairs with an earlier cut. Truncation stops at visible audit-safe state and waits for the generated-complete floor, including prepared transfers, cursors, replay, external continuities, remote trust/retention, backup, keys, and current/prospective configs. Local Raft publication may advance RootSlot without semantic change. Leader loss yields capability-scoped `Unknown`, never a guess.
2. **Membership and payload authority.** SWIM+Lifeguard supplies suspicion/routing/donor evidence only; it cannot change membership. Appendix A's exact `ConfigurationState` includes database/security-namespace/incarnation, role/group, epoch, stable-or-joint voters/storage sets, member key epochs/failure domains, quorum/recoverability/GC rules, weak predecessor, and transition nonce; it has no self ID. Joint requires independent old/new consensus quorums and the payload predicate over both sets. One-member is the ordinary stable specialization. Every local signed object uses the exact certificate header; every imported leaf uses the embedded canonical configuration evidence. Numeric epoch or equal member list is never authority.

   A pre-order `ConfigurationTransitionSpec` carries a nonretaining basis identity, current/prospective configuration refs, the candidate closure proof, and expected prefix. Its applied `ConfigPayloadFloor` **does not retain the spec, basis root, checkpoint, or checkpoint vector**: it stores weak state/checkpoint identities plus basis/closed-through logical-command, commit, and Raft positions; strong current/prospective configuration refs; retained suffix endpoints; a self-contained typed mandatory-inventory root; prepared-root generations/stable ownership IDs; and per-domain receipts/acknowledgements. Inventory entries are explicitly `RetainedStrong` for independently mandatory objects or `CurrentCheckpointObservation { checkpoint:WeakCheckpointIdentity, vector_digest:WeakDigest, availability_receipt_refs }`; neither the observation nor its receipts become a logical reachability edge to checkpoint/vector/prior-floor bytes. The separately strong `LogicalStatePayload.recovery_checkpoint_ref` owns the current checkpoint/vector, and floor validation requires the weak observation to equal and cover that exact current checkpoint. Every operational checkpoint install atomically supplies the paired refreshed floor through §5.4, whose projection excludes the prior floor. Thus replacing `F_n` cannot create either a direct or indirect `F_n -> Q_n -> F_(n-1)` retention chain. If the authoritative prefix or current checkpoint advances during transfer, the candidate floor is extended/recomputed before installation; a stale floor cannot authorize retirement.

   Reconfiguration is `ProposeJoint -> CatchUpLog -> TransferMandatoryClosure -> VerifyFloorAtBasis -> CommitJoint -> CommitNew -> RefreshFloorThroughCommitNew -> CommitRetirementFloor -> RetireOld`. `CommitJoint`, `CommitNew`, and `CommitRetirementFloor` are the typed Raft `ConfigurationTransitionSpec` entries themselves, so each semantic configuration transition increments `LogicalCommandSeq`; heartbeats/no-ops do not. The final retirement floor proves that the prospective durability set can recover through the committed `CommitNew` transition and every mandatory retained suffix/object and protected retry/accounting/idempotency closure under the new failure-domain policy. Old members cannot leave, discard payload, or advance GC until that final floor command is committed and acknowledged. Statistical suspicion may tune alerts but never authorizes membership, payload retirement, or GC.
3. **Read contracts and revocation/audit fences.** `LeaderRead` and `ReadIndexRead` provide linearizable data paths. The sole `AuthorizationLease` schema is the signed `{consensus_domain:ConsensusDomain,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,service_visibility_epoch,issuer_id,authority_leader_member_id,authority_raft_term,security_leader_epoch,lease_generation,source_token_or_capability_commitment,token_id,tenant,principal,non_widenable_authority_ceiling_digest,effective_authority_digest,policy_semantics_oid,policy_epoch,revocation_index,permitted_operation_class:ReadOnly,permitted_snapshot_interval,exact_role_bearing_read_bindings,allowed_query_operator_disclosure_scope,result_answer_contract_ceiling,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expires_at,signer_id,signing_key_id,signer_epoch,signature}`. The signature transcript includes every preceding field and the complete closed-open profiled window; authority term/leader drift, policy-root or revocation-root mismatch, token substitution, a wider ceiling, or a non-read operation invalidates it. `FollowerLeaseRead` is the separately signed `{consensus_domain:ConsensusDomain,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,service_visibility_epoch,follower_member_id,configuration_identity,term,lease_epoch,closed_logical_command_seq,closed_commit_seq,audit_visible_logical_command_seq,applied_logical_command_seq,applied_commit_seq,retention_lease_identity,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expiry,authorization_lease_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationLease>,signer_id,signing_key_id,signer_epoch,signature}`. It is legal only when both canonical prefixes are fenced at or below the audit-visible publication prefix, the requested snapshot/control state is closed and applied, all referenced objects/keys are retained, and the named retention lease is live. Its signature transcript includes every preceding field. Fresh `TimeValidationEvidence::Usable` and a linear `TimeUseGuard` must match the follower-read action and independently validate both profiled windows; mixed-profile comparison is invalid. The follower validates both complete domains/service epochs, configuration/term/signers, the requested snapshot range, policy semantics/root/epoch, and revocation root/index. Otherwise it contacts the authority leader or fails closed; data staleness never grants security staleness, and unpublished ticket-gated effects never leak through a follower. Open streams discard unsent buffered frames and reauthorize within the configured maximum lease TTL. `bounded_staleness` returns effective transaction sequence/lag, logical-command/audit-visible prefixes, and security index/lease expiry. Historical reads retain the same applied, retention, key, branch, audit, and authority predicates. The sole cross-session body is §13's exact `ReadYourWritesCapabilityReplayRecord.fields.body`; no second wire/MAC schema exists here. Its `minimum_visible_logical_position:PostureLogicalPosition` encodes the role-appropriate Raft/logical/commit/audit wait floor, and `committed_branch_head_commitment` binds the authorized committed heads without exposing raw marker identities. Presentation requires same-or-narrower live authority, current revocation checks, and a fresh profiled time-use guard, and only asks the server to route or wait until that already-committed visibility position is locally available; it grants no mutation, independent read, retention, or existence-disclosure authority. Until expiry, its exact replay record, verifier key, accepted time profile, and capability-safe prefix/tombstone metadata remain retained, while graph history remains governed by the separately advertised read/retention contract. Same-identity restore or role cutover changes `service_visibility_epoch`, invalidating every old capability and authorization lease before observation.
4. **Writer-anywhere preparation.** Followers may prepare `TxnProposal`s and candidate physical work, but only the leader/global Raft order validates final effects, builds or approves the final capsule, and publishes. Preparation can scale; ordered commitment remains bounded by validation, payload distribution, and Raft. No near-linear committed-write claim ships without a benchmark separating preparation from ordered publication.
5. **Transfer, anti-entropy, and safe GC.** ATP may fetch compatible symbols from multiple donors. Every symbol is authenticated against the exact logical/encoding identity and §5.1 MAC transcript; donor agreement alone creates no authority. Merkle anti-entropy locates missing encodings and logical-digest divergence. Applied/durable positions may gossip through a CRDT cache, but branch heads derive only from committed head CAS records and GC is `CollectTypedRoots(stable_membership_epoch,config_payload_floor) -> ResolveMarkedPhysicalRealizations -> ProposeSafePoint -> ValidateAllTypedRootsAndCuts(prepared,commands,leases,pins,merge,privacy,replay,keys,backups,audit,transparency) -> CommitGcEpochThroughRaft -> Reclaim`. Uncertain membership, incomplete new-configuration payload closure, partition, missing root/prepared-owner acknowledgement, external privacy-continuity mismatch, or unavailable key wrap stops reclamation. Backup/restore follows §16, not a decode-proof shortcut.
6. **Post-1.0 sharding workstream W12.** Sharding preserves B1's single version universe through one database-wide meta-Raft order. It is not a federation of independently committed shard histories and does not switch Chronicle to vector time.

   - **One scalar semantic clock.** In sharded posture, `LogicalCommandSeq`, transaction-only `CommitSeq`, and logical HLC are Meta-issued global aliases, not vector clocks. Every canonical mutation passes through Meta; shard Raft indices order durability/apply only and never move time or heads. Meta computes HLC from the previous value and normalized proposal observations. I/O/group-commit batching of already sequentially certified entries is allowed; speculative shared-basis semantic certification and shard-local visible commit are not.

   - **Snapshot and prepare.** When the audit profile requires it, Meta first mirrors one pending operation ticket; only then may it order the `ReadOnly|ReadWrite` registration with the matching read/mutation permit and `OperationAuditAdmission`. The registration's own control gate is a validated lifecycle-scaffolding `NotRequired` proof and cannot consume the operation ticket. The registered ReadIndex-fenced global snapshot follows; no shard read precedes ticket visibility or registration. A shard read also proves its active Meta topology/policy/revocation/key/audit projection covers the registration prefix and binds the operation-audit commitment. Read-only closes through its separate routing/witness and meta aggregate authorization records, then resolves that same ticket before releasing output. For writes, post-rebase shard effect bases lead to the deterministic routing/cascade/constraint-owner fixed point, aggregate effect digest, one union authorization decision whose ticket-only gate names the already-admitted operation ticket, then resources/outcome compare state. Meta orders the unique `GlobalPrepareAdmission` with immutable participant/reservation set and admission generation; its lifecycle gate is likewise a validated nonterminal scaffolding proof. Only after that record is visible may shards build fragments and order prepares keyed `(global_txn_id,registration_generation,admission_generation)`, after first applying every Meta command through admission. Prepared owners keep local fence epochs outside canonical commands. Certificates bind admission prefix, active projection, config/topology, heads/key material, witnesses/constraints/resources/auth and pending-operation-audit commitment. Commit/abort event and terminal gate are built only after certification chooses the outcome. Any drift requires admitted abort/release plus a new registration generation; digest substitution never recertifies stale work.

   - **Global certification and decision.** Commit requires the unique admission/routing/participant set, current distributed-serialization and constraint certificates, exact prefix/heads/key epochs, one aggregate authorization/resource/outcome basis, and one valid prepare per admitted shard. The final effect digest excludes wrapper/audit objects. Once certification chooses Commit or Abort, Meta builds the concrete matching audit event/resolution/gate. The pre-command availability certificate covers only already-built inputs and excludes itself/future command; a stable prepared-owner successor adds the completed command. Apply assigns sequences/HLC and builds marker (commit only), heads, outcome/conflict/constraint state, payload, record, and root—never future shard batches. After terminal audit mirror publication, the quorum creates and Meta publishes the unique decision certificate. Shards can then install decision N, apply its exact audit mirror, and only afterward export final visible acknowledgements. Abort is constructible even with no prepare and adopts no effect; shard acks are post-decision cleanup gates, never command inputs. The Meta record alone decides outcome.

   - **Distributed serializability, not “local SSI plus hope.”** Meta-Raft canonically owns `GlobalConflictIndex`. For every registered active or recently completed overlapping serializable transaction—including read-only work—it retains snapshot/start/terminal prefixes, participant set, witness frontier, conservative per-shard read/write summaries, and all `wr`, `ww`, and `rw` edges with proof references until no live transaction can add one. Before commitment, the deterministic certifier replays exact `may_affect` in both directions against every overlapping prepared/committed/closed transaction and rejects FCW/uniqueness conflicts or any cycle. V1 forbids speculative semantic multi-command certification: every commit or read-close certificate is built against the fully applied immediately prior global prefix/conflict/constraint/head state. Group commit may batch fsync/network transport of already sequentially certified entries, but two candidates cannot share a basis or omit cross-candidate edges. Missing/stale support, partition, or resource exhaustion waits or aborts conservatively; monotone coarsening may add false positives only. Read-only results return only after ordered `ReadClose`. An independent SCC/history oracle checks every history, including same-I/O-batch two-writer and rw-cycle cases.

   - **Global constraints and branch authority.** Each cross-partition unique/referential/cardinality domain has a canonical `ConstraintOwner = H(topology_epoch, constraint_id, canonical_domain_key)` shard or an explicitly meta-owned aggregate. The routing certificate lists every owner. Reservations are acquired in canonical `(owner_shard, constraint_id, canonical_key)` order with meta registration order as the deterministic loser/abort priority; participant prepare durably reserves exact keys/ranges and reports before/after contributions, and only an explicit meta decision releases them. Meta certification compares all reservations and aggregate state at the same global prefix and installs them atomically with the decision. Cross-shard path/predicate constraints run over the same registered witness algebra and complete participant closure; an unsupported or incomplete exact evaluator rejects the schema/transaction rather than approximating. Meta state alone owns branch heads/manifests/key-envelope and grant epochs, schema/topology/security epochs, merge/import idempotency, ID-range fences, global capability-verifier roots, and resource/privacy/audit outcomes/continuity. A shard cache is never authority. Every participant uses §12.3's exact `AuthorizedSnapshot`/`AuthorizedMutation` types, and hidden data cannot enter routing, witness, constraint, statistics, or error surfaces.

   - **Apply, visibility, and Ripple.** Participant state is keyed by `(global_txn_id,registration_generation,admission_generation)`. A published decision certificate installs decision N in order (or a no-prepare abort tombstone) but does not bypass later Meta controls. The shard then applies the exact audit mirror so visibility reaches N; only the post-mirror root can produce `ShardAppliedAck`. Irrelevant ranges require exhaustive proofs, while topology/policy/revocation/key/audit/remote effects use typed projections and visibility never decreases. Queries choose one global prefix and wait/fail until every routed shard has applied/proved it and retained that history. Meta builds `GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch` only from the complete post-mirror ack/fragment set and publishes it through one Meta control, which alone advances the global Ripple frontier. Delivery/CDC names that Global batch, never a shard fragment. Client acknowledgement waits for delta publication, participant durability/apply, audit visibility, and durable outcome; loss returns scoped Unknown.

   - **Recovery and nonblocking impossibility.** Prepared closures remain pinned through terminal decision, post-mirror participant acks, overlap/retention floors, and staged GC. No prepared participant times out or guesses; it recovers Meta's decision. `NeverRegisteredFloor` removes only proved staging, while `ClosedAttemptCompactionFloor` replaces detailed terminal history only after decision/publication/all admitted acks/overlap close and retains capability-safe summary proofs; neither decides Prepared work. Meta/Shard reconfiguration uses explicit prepared-ownership transfer and remote-config trust/adoption before old retirement. Distributed GC uses certified preflight -> Meta authorization -> per-shard durable apply/ack -> Meta completion, with remote targets released only through the six-stage handshake. Partitions may block; they cannot reverse decisions or reclaim uncertain state.

   - **Topology and repartitioning.** Source-range partitioning is the base edge-cut/vertex-owner scheme; optional hub vertex-cut uses separately versioned replicated-vertex metadata and a single canonical edge owner. Movement uses three separately ordered, evidence-complete commands: `TopologyCopyBegin` fixes copy basis `F`, source checkpoint/suffix inventory, joint configurations, and transfer plan while the old owner remains sole write authority; `TopologyCutover` names canonical transfer/catch-up certificates plus the exact active-attempt closure at prefix `S`, stops old-epoch admission, and switches ownership only at `S+1`; `TopologyRetireOld` names every new-owner/meta/backup/key/retention acknowledgement and the final retirement floor. Apply records only evidence already named by its command. No transaction straddles topology epochs, and old bytes/keys cannot retire before the third command. Allocation ranges are meta-fenced before use.

   - **Scope and exit.** These choices are normative now; only their implementation is post-1.0. W12 cannot ship until the dedicated gate in §19 proves meta/shard reconfiguration, every crash/partition point, distributed SCC/constraint histories, cross-shard branch/merge/key/audit behavior, Ripple frontier atomicity, and topology moves. Until that gate passes, a database advertises `sharding=false` and rejects a topology with more than one data shard rather than weakening any 1.0 guarantee.


---

## 15. Determinism, Calibration & Verification Doctrine (Bet B5)

This is not a QA appendix; it is a design pillar with its own budget. It opens with the runtime stratum (§15.0 — the calibration plane that governs the live system), then the verification stack from cheapest to strongest.

### 15.0 Sextant: the calibration discipline within B5

Sextant supplies e-processes, conformal predictors, sequential tests, robust estimators, regime/change detectors, and propensity/OPE tooling as deterministic transformations of logged inputs. It governs performance and operational choices; it never upgrades assumption-bearing evidence into exact correctness.

Every evidence envelope carries `ClaimClass`:

- `SafetyInvariant`: must hold on every execution; failure is a correctness defect.
- `FormalModelClaim`: theorem or model-check result with abstraction, bounds, and refinement status.
- `StatisticalClaim`: population, sampling/selection rule, alpha, power/effective sample size, and assumptions.
- `ConfigurationModelClaim`: model version, fitted inputs, sensitivity, and validity domain.
- `EmpiricalGate`: fixture, machine/profile, sample count, variance budget, and comparison rule.

`invariants.toml` contains only exact safety/liveness obligations. `evidence.toml` contains `FG-CAL-*` and `FG-EVID-*`; `slo.toml` contains `FG-CFG-*`, performance, durability-model, and controller targets. E-processes may be anytime-valid under their named filtration/null assumptions; conformal coverage is marginal under its named exchangeability or online-validity conditions; drift alarms do not retroactively preserve a broken assumption; OPE requires positivity/overlap and sufficient effective sample size. A monitor that drives no named decision is dead code, but binding it to a decision does not make it an invariant.

Every adaptive policy retains a deterministic fallback valid without the statistical model. Answer-affecting execution policies are bound to the `AnswerRequirement`, plan, result contract, and replay closure; canonical-state-affecting promotions are logical-command-sequenced and replay-pinned; only proved answer-preserving physical policies may remain local. Calibration windows, selection policy, strata, propensity support, regime epochs, fallback, and failure behavior are immutable evidence identities. This is how B5 makes adaptation inspectable without confusing “well measured” with “proved safe.”

### 15.1 Simulation-first development (`fgdb-sim`)

The entire database runs under asupersync's lab runtime with virtual time/network/disk, seeded scheduling, chaos, and deterministic pressure models. DPOR is exhaustive only within the declared bounded scenario/state model and the soundness of its independence relation; broader campaigns remain falsification, not proof of bug absence. Every failure still becomes a replayable seed/crashpack, which is the practical value.

Five force multipliers on the same substrate:

- **Targeted falsification (LDFI).** Random chaos asks “what if something fails?”; lineage-driven fault injection derives minimal fault hypotheses from successful-run dependencies. It targets every file/directory action in D1/D2 and every ordered, certificate, external-CAS, or physical side-effect boundary in dual-root publication; attempt generation/ticket claim/statement-workspace publication and delivery; checkpoint install/provisional-cut activation; prepared ownership and Raft; remote release; key stage/activate/zero/destroy/physical completion; GC preflight/authorization/quarantine/member completion; backup pin/copy/reopen/publish/release; restore reservation/transform/reconciliation/hidden activation/visibility/service preparation/continuity-plus-catalog receipt/finalize/open/reopen/completion; and Local-to-W12 seal/activation/authority-transfer/retirement. It is a high-yield falsification tool, while residual random chaos guards lineage blind spots.
- **A model-qualified stopping heuristic.** Novelty estimates and coverage maximization prioritize finite CI time under a named sampling model. They may stop a campaign according to policy; they never certify that no unexplored bug remains. Deterministic bounded-state completion is reported separately from statistical/heuristic stopping.
- **Failing runs shrink themselves.** Hierarchical delta debugging + replay minimization reduce every failing seed (schedule + workload trace) to a minimal reproducer before filing, and divergence diagnostics explain exactly where a replay departed from its recording. Crashpacks arrive pre-shrunk; the bug report writes itself.
- **Lab-vs-live dual runs.** The same scenario, same seed, runs under the lab and against the live build, and the traces are diffed — closing the classic simulation-testing loophole ("we verified the simulator, not the system"). This is the runtime-behavior counterpart of the `fgdb-reference` semantics differential.
- **Production incident replay is graded.** Production retains bounded mediated nondeterminism records under a fail-closed redaction contract. Each bundle carries the explicit `ReplayCompleteness` grade `Replayable | StructuralReplay{reproduced_classes[],omitted_classes[]} | VerifiableIfArtifactsSupplied{missing_classes[]} | AuditOnly{missing_or_redacted_classes[]}`. Crypto entropy is never recorded. Full internal forensic bundles may be exact when policy permits; customer-safe bundles never overclaim byte identity.

Every failing sim, live differential, integration, or E2E run emits one secret-redacted structured artifact containing `{seed,schedule,crashpoint,role,group,configuration,topology,incarnation,service_visibility_epoch,logical/commit/Raft/applied/visible/audit-visible positions,attempt/generation/statement/workspace/backup/restore/GC/key identifiers,object/spec/result/certificate/grant/floor identities,expected,actual,replay_command}`. Contract tests require every applicable field and execute the replay command; human prose is supplemental. Coverage includes lost `BEGIN_ACCEPTED`, duplicate/conflicting begin keys, denial/abandonment before registration, workspace-zero recovery, successor Registered-outcome rooting, cancel with prior results/workspace/grants, terminal/autocommit ACK/release races, every TerminalPending missing-postcondition combination, and status before/during/after compaction and detail reclamation.

### 15.2 Consistency oracles

In-sim checkers include snapshot/branch visibility, an SSI dependency oracle, obligation/quiescence, root/capsule closure, authorization noninterference, and Elle-class histories. The SSI oracle uses a deliberately independent small Tarjan/SCC implementation over trace-derived logical dependencies; production graph algorithms may be a secondary differential, never the sole checker of their own transaction graph. Every invariant has at least one checker outside the optimized component it checks where practical.

Independent protocol oracles continuously cross-check atomic begin/family/token/attempt/outcome transitions; ticket ownership; statement index, terminal/autocommit delivery frontier, workspace generation and cumulative witness/effect roots; terminal-postcondition bitmaps; decision publication/post-mirror acknowledgements/global-delta frontier; provisional versus activated cut authority; remote release; staged key and GC phases; backup manifest/pin release; restore hidden/service/reopen state; and Local-to-W12 retirement. Security negatives cover raw cross-group references and wrong role/domain/incarnation/configuration/grant/permit projection/claim owner/workspace/service epoch, plus observation or acknowledgement before the required mirror/open state. Detailed and compacted status paths must return byte-identical public outcome bytes.

Production assertions and complete audits can enforce exact invariants; sampled e-processes are statistical sentinels in `evidence.toml`, not the enforcement column of `invariants.toml`. Replay uses the complete `ReplayManifest` in §8.6. Security verification additionally covers cross-capability differential results/plans/errors/timing classes, revocation during streams, cache/view/index isolation, hidden-state constraints/cascades, donor poisoning, key rotation, restore authorization, parser/resource exhaustion, and audit-chain completeness.

### 15.3 Fault & recovery torture

Crash matrices kill at every D1/D2 filesystem barrier, both root slots, combined inode/incarnation takeover check, post-rebase capsule, marker/root publication, prepared ownership transfer, payload receipt/Raft/apply, audit ticket claim/signer-lock/candidate/external-CAS/mirror, statement workspace/result/delivery transition, and checkpoint install/provisional-cut/activation step. W12 campaigns cover begin reservation and Attempt First/Successor/idempotent/burn races; shard prepare through decision publication, audit projection, post-mirror acknowledgement and global-delta publication; every TerminalPending bit combination; six-stage remote release; key plan/stage/certify/manifest/activate/zero/durable destroy/member-or-KMS completion; and GC preflight/global authorization/current-root quarantine/no-resurrection/member/aggregate completion. Backup/restore campaigns cover exact Local and Sharded barriers, independent archive and target reopen, every release acknowledgement, continuity split-brain, leaves-first readdress/re-encryption, hidden activation/visibility/service preparation, continuity-then-catalog CAS, hidden roll-forward, Meta finalize, shard open/acks, completion and source-lease release. Activation campaigns stop at every Local freeze/seal/certificate/projection/first-entry/authority-transfer/RetiredLocal/finalize/reclamation point. Every scenario declares its filesystem, failure, placement, quorum, external-authority, and fairness model. Additional campaigns cover partial marker tails, full-digest locator collisions, mixed EncodingId symbols, erasures within and beyond every source-block budget, stale writers, uncertain membership, donor poisoning, key loss, and idempotent Unknown/status recovery through scoped capabilities.

### 15.4 Differential & conformance testing

- **Semantics oracles**: an executable **reference engine** (`fgdb-reference`) — a deliberately simple, single-threaded, obviously-correct implementation of the full logical semantics (values, visibility, path modes, intents, temporal selectors, branches, multi-statement transaction-error policy, workspace generations/read-your-own-writes, statement publication/delivery, and terminal attempt semantics) over canonical maps, compiled for tests/fuzzing/model-checking only, never shipped, never optimized, so "what should this return" is a program rather than a debate; openCypher TCK; a GQL feature-conformance corpus keyed to ISO feature IDs (published as a matrix); differential vs. Neo4j & Memgraph on a curated corpus (behavior parity where standards align, documented divergence elsewhere); Prism results differential vs. standalone fnx (which is itself NetworkX-parity-locked — a two-hop oracle chain to ground truth). Model-generated histories run against both engines and compare snapshots, results, certificates, and permitted abort outcomes.
- **Storage oracles**: model-based testing of Strata against an in-memory reference graph (arbitrary op interleavings, equality after every op under every open snapshot); metamorphic suites in the house style (e.g., pattern-match results invariant under compaction, seal, branch-fork, encode/decode round-trips).
- **Fuzzing**: parser (GQL/Cypher grammars), FGP frames, every fgdb-formats reader (extending fnx's 8-fuzzer precedent), SymbolRecord decoder.
- **Protocol-state oracles**: simple canonical-map reference machines for exact begin/attempt/audit/statement/workspace/delivery/status, provisional/activated cut, local and distributed key, GC, Local/Sharded backup/restore/service/reopen, and activation/retirement/reclamation transitions. Generated traces run against optimized state machines and compare every state, result, refusal, resource release, and log field.

### 15.5 Formal anchors (scoped, honest — the asupersync posture)

Lean targets the full visibility relation—publication, branch ancestry, create/retire, own writes, and reclamation—not merely three local MVCC facts. SSI work separates: dangerous-structure theorem, lifetime of dependency metadata, soundness of each witness constructor's concretization, refinement preservation of positive/negative/gap/path observations, optimizer transport of witness obligations, and statement-workspace transport plus cumulative-witness preservation. Merge proofs cover the registered algebra in its constraint context. Ripple proofs cover only the explicitly registered operator/annotation subset.

TLA+/TLC models the dual-slot root and generated-complete checkpoint authority transfer, exact writer-lease/takeover/fence-enable sequence, final-capsule commit, marker/global-branch links, fork-time envelope/write-key double rotation, delivery ACK/resume, audit candidate visibility fencing/external reconciliation, stable prepared ownership plus payload availability/Raft, membership reconfiguration floors, branch merge/token/range idempotency, and closed-sequence leases. Separate bounded W12 models cover (a) begin reservation, attempt generation, ticket claim, statement/workspace publication, terminal/autocommit delivery, status, cancellation, and read close; (b) admission, shard prepare, signer-locked terminal candidate, external CAS/mirror, decision publication, shard audit projection/post-mirror acknowledgement and global-delta publication; (c) provisional-cut replacement with inherited absent bytes and later activation; (d) closed-attempt build/attest/publish and detailed/compacted status equivalence; (e) six-stage remote release; (f) staged distributed key activation and physical destruction; (g) GC quarantine/no-resurrection and physical completion; (h) exact backup publication/release; (i) restore reservation, transformation, hidden activation/visibility/service preparation, receipt-first finalize/open/reopen/completion; and (j) Local-to-W12 activation, authority transfer, RetiredLocal finalization, and reclamation. Models include partitions, Meta/shard reconfiguration, conflict-index lifetime, constraint reservations, and topology moves. The generated durable-reference checker separately enforces per-field PriorObject construction annotations and rejects cycles in reachable object instances; recursive persistent-tree types remain legal because every concrete parent points only to already identified children. Neither method is mislabeled as the other. Every model run states bounds. Trace export demonstrates that captured executions are allowed by a spec; it is trace conformance, not an implementation-refinement proof. Runtime monitors detect selected violations but do not inherit model-check completeness. Proof-lane manifests name abstraction, assumptions, bounds, refinement bridge, and exactly what remains unproved.

Appendix F has exactly twenty top-level invariant IDs. G0 materializes each as stable subordinate clauses in `invariants.toml`; every clause records its exact statement, role/posture/format/feature activation predicate, dependency clauses, resolvable checker entrypoints, negative-test IDs, proof/model scope and bounds or liveness fairness assumptions, owner, first required gate, status, and `waiver=forbidden`. CI verifies the twenty-ID set and table hash, acyclic dependencies, checker/test symbol existence, and the compiled-plus-negotiated activation closure. Every reachable clause must be live; an unimplemented or dormant clause forces its feature off and cannot count as covered. The plan does not falsely claim the currently absent file already exists.

### 15.6 Performance regression apparatus

Criterion-style in-house microbench harness + macro suites (§17) with baselines committed, variance-aware gating (the asupersync/fnx baseline artifact discipline), and complexity-witness regression locks: an algorithm or operator whose instrumented operation count exceeds its registered bound on an in-domain fixture fails CI. Correctness, security, durable-format, recovery, authorization, invariant-checker, and required conformance gates are **nonwaivable**. A public, expiring waiver may cover only a named empirical performance threshold, statistical-evidence threshold, or non-safety coverage budget; it records owner, evidence, reduced claim, expiry, and fallback and cannot weaken an invariant or enable a feature whose safety checker failed.

### 15.7 Publish the design

Sortledton/Teseo/Kùzu earned trust by publishing. Target six papers/tech-reports from this work: (1) Strata: temperature-tiered transactional adjacency; (2) One Version Universe: unifying MVCC, temporal, branching, and replication over a fountain-coded commit stream; (3) Refinable predicate witnesses: graph serializability with near-zero false conflicts and no per-edge read tracking; (4) Plan certificates & decision cards: deterministic, auditable query execution; (5) The externally verifiable graph database: transparency checkpoints, inclusion-proof changefeeds, and computed durability certificates over a fountain-coded commit stream; (6) Calibrated adaptivity: anytime-valid statistical governance of a self-tuning DBMS. Ambition includes the receipts.

---

## 16. Observability & Operations

1. **Process tree** (Spork supervision, restart topologies declared):
```
FgdbRootRegion
 ├── ChronicleRegion      (WriteCoordinator · scrubber · checkpointer)
 ├── StrataRegion         (sealers · compactors per partition-group · GC/demotion)
 ├── RippleRegion         (view circuits · subscription fan-out · stats maintainers · index feeders)
 ├── BeaconRegion         (index builders · HNSW mergers · path-index manager)
 ├── PrismRegion          (analytics bulkhead)
 ├── WardenRegion         (policy/revocation authority · lease issuer · DP coordinator · audit anchor)
 ├── AegisRegion          (raft · replication streams · donor service)
 ├── FabricRegion         (listeners · sessions · admission)
 └── ObservatoryRegion    (metrics export · task inspector · spectral health · deadline monitor)
```
2. **Telemetry**: asupersync metrics + OTel export, authorized/redacted trace context, `EXPLAIN`, and `SHOW` surfaces cover transactions, compaction debt, Ripple/index watermarks, buffer residency, resource reservations, obligations, GC membership epoch, key epochs, and commit phases. Little's-law checks and shadow prices are diagnostics under stationarity/model assumptions and live in evidence/SLO registries, not the safety-invariant registry.
3. **Early warning**: wait-graph, futurelock, autocorrelation/variance, and coupled-controller monitors provide model-qualified alerts. `FG-CFG-02` rejects defaults predicted unstable by a versioned fluid model with sensitivity analysis; it does not claim every real workload lies in that model. Hard safety comes from bounded queues, resource reservations, cancellation checkpoints, and deterministic fallback controls.
4. **Ops verbs**: online `COMPACT/SCRUB/REBUILD INDEX/ANALYZE`; `fgdb doctor` verifies root slots, closure, full digests/encodings, marker/branch continuity, constraint state, key wraps, payload availability, GC epoch, and model-qualified configuration reports. Support bundles carry replay-completeness/redaction grades. Cancellation exposes phase and deterministic drain progress; any probabilistic remaining-work/stall estimate names its model and is not a quiescence proof. Quiescence is asserted only when obligations and resource ledgers reach their exact terminal state.
5. **The system graph**: the database's own runtime — sessions, transactions, queries, plans, operators, snapshots + leases, obligations, segments, compaction jobs, subscriptions, replication streams, repairs, decision cards — is exposed as a read-only, access-controlled *temporal property graph*, queryable in GQL like any other graph (`MATCH (q:Query)-[:WAITS_FOR]->(x) WHERE q.elapsed_ms > 250 RETURN q, x`). The wait-for graph is literally a graph: deadlock and contention analysis run Prism's own cycle detection and centrality over it, and incidents become subgraphs you can diff across time. The database dogfoods its data model as its control plane — bounded cardinality, sampled under load, redacted per capability (§12.6).
6. **Admission, backup, and upgrade**: ephemeral hierarchical ledgers reserve/charge/release the transient portion of §13's `ResourceVector`; Chronicle's canonical durable ledger atomically accounts for persistent branches/indexes/views/subscriptions/history/durable bytes through `ResourceChargeEffect`s. Startup/recovery reconciles ephemeral reservations by obligation generation and verifies durable ledger state against committed effects—neither local session counters nor telemetry are quota authority. Maintenance and recovery retain protected emergency capacity. Optimization models may advise allocations, but hard caps and shedding order govern ENOSPC, quorum loss, key unavailability, output backpressure, and tenant isolation.

   Backup uses ordered **source pins**, not a manifest that permanently retains the live database. Local lifecycle is `Absent -> Pinned -> ClosureCertified -> Sealed -> (PublicationReceiptedPendingTransparency ->)? Published -> ArtifactVerified -> ReleasedPendingArchiveHoldCompletion -> Released`; Sharded Meta lifecycle adds exact shard pin/certify and release-authorize/ack phases around the same publication and hold-completion states. Appendix A defines the exact commands, certificates, and registry states. A Local barrier fixes one published root/checkpoint/vector/configuration/floor/prepared/certificate/remote/history closure. A Sharded barrier fixes one Meta-issued global prefix `P`, exact Meta closure/topology/configurations, and one closure from every and only required shard. A shard supplies either its exact current state at `P` or an authenticated historical state/cut at `P`; `latest >= P` is not a legal proof. Every pin is a durable strong root until an independently reopened **published artifact**, signed manifest publication, valid required transparency inclusion, archive retention grant, source release, external hold-completion CAS, and ordered completion mirror all finish.

   `BackupManifestBody -> BackupManifestSignatureSet -> BackupManifest -> BackupPublicationReceipt -> BackupTransparencyInclusion? -> ArchiveRetentionGrant -> BackupArtifactReopenProof` is the acyclic publication order. The content archive inventory is fixed before the body and explicitly excludes the publication envelope; the later publication receipt durably locates and authenticates the body/signature-set/manifest tuple, and the grant enumerates that tuple, the content inventory, the receipt, and the required inclusion without including itself. A manifest body may name the prior transparency checkpoint but never its own future inclusion proof, receipt, grant, or reopen proof. Released manifests contain only typed `BackupSourceIdentity<T>` plus `BackupArchiveRef<T>`, not live `StrongRef<T>` or `CertifiedRemoteStrongRef<T>`. They pin database/security namespace/incarnation, exact posture and barrier, logical/commit/base/anti-rollback ranges, branch/checkpoint/history/prepared/certificate/key/derived/trust/continuity/cursor/delivery/replay/format inventories, recipient/escrow policy, canonical semantic digest, and signer/configuration chain. Legacy Local backups remain Local after W12 activation. Verification reopens the actually published envelope and content inventory independently, reconstructs every physical realization and logical digest, and recomputes the posture-specific semantic digest before release.

   Restore acquires a new archive-owned `RestoreSourceLease`; it cannot reuse the source-database backup pin released after publication. `RecoverSameIdentity` first advances the external `ClusterIncarnationContinuityRecord` through `Operational(I) -> RestoreFencePending -> RestoreReserved(J)`, where all old incarnation leases are revoked/expired and `J > max(external retired floor, current live incarnation, backup incarnation)`. Only one CAS contender can reserve `J`. A member-bound `ClusterIncarnationLease(scope=RecoveryOnly|OrdinaryWrite)` is checked together with the inode lease/fence immediately before every irreversible seal, prepared publication, receipt, Raft proposal/ack, certificate, and RootSlot publication.
