Confined temporary references also require durable allocation **before** their permanent values enter a capsule or shard effect basis; “assign in commit order” is not an ambient counter operation. `FinalizationAllocationPlan<Role>` is the sequence-neutral pre-order object `{role,registration_identity,admission_generation,finalization_generation,expected_allocation_binding_root_ref:StrongRef<TxnAllocationBindingRoot>,allocator_basis:WeakStateIdentity,topology_and_owner_basis,sorted_mappings[{slot_key,value_kind,permanent_value,lease_ref,lease_offset,source_intent_ordinal}],sorted_lease_use_evidence_refs[StrongRef<TimeValidationEvidence>],exact_before_lease_cursor_and_high_water_values,exact_after_lease_cursor_and_high_water_values,permanent_spent_extension_commitment,complete_confined_tmp_ref_bijection,exhaustion_and_checked_overflow_proof,body_digest}`. It excludes every previously escaped slot, has no future command/result/root, and must map every and only remaining create/generated-key reference in the normalized effect set.

Local `LocalFinalCertificationReserveSpec` names that plan, and its apply atomically updates `IdAllocatorState`, installs `FinalizationAllocationReservationRecord<Local> {plan_ref,registration_identity,finalization_generation,sorted_mappings,permanent_spent_extension_commitment,applied_control_ref,state:Active}`, and installs the Active final-certification/constraint/resource/escrow holds. Only afterward are final effects, terminal result preparation, capsule, and terminal audit bytes constructed, and each strongly names the reservation record. Commit atomically replaces it with `Consumed{terminal_input_identity,marker_identity}`. Cancel or abort replaces it with `AbandonedSpent{terminal_or_cancel_identity,tombstone_summary_ref}`; because durable plan/effect candidates may already name the values, capacity is never returned.

In Sharded posture, each allocation-owner shard orders `ShardFinalizationAllocationReserveSpec` before constructing `ShardEffectBasis`, consumes exact offsets in its authoritative leased-range ledger, and exports `ShardFinalizationAllocationEvidence {SameGroupCertificateHeader,reservation_record_ref:StrongRef<FinalizationAllocationReservationRecord<Shard>>,sorted_mappings,permanent_spent_extension_commitment,topology_and_configuration_basis,one_digest_signer_lock_ref,quorum_signatures}`. The effect basis and routing certificate bind the exact certified evidence. `GlobalFinalCertificationReserveSpec` requires a canonical bijection over all such evidence and every remaining temporary reference, holds those reservations, and cannot remap them. Global commit/abort disposition is projected back to every shard; participant loss retains the spent reservation until recovery applies that disposition. Meta never guesses a shard's next slot and a shard never uses an uncertified Meta mapping.

`FinalizationAllocationTombstoneSummary` is the compact cumulative `{role_and_owner,allocation_epoch,sorted_spent_ranges_or_offsets,attempt_and_finalization_generation,terminal_disposition_commitment,predecessor_summary_digest:WeakDigest,body_digest}`. Checkpoint, configuration, backup/restore, role transition, topology movement, prepared/final-certification, and GC inventories retain every Active reservation and cumulative consumed/abandoned spend. Tests race two candidates on the same allocator basis, crash before/after reservation/capsule/audit/order, cancel and abort, force rebase/partition movement, expire leases, restore an old allocator root, and exhaust every high-water counter; exactly one mapping wins, overflow fail-closes, and no permanent value is ever reused.

**CommittedEffectCapsule**: `{ read_snapshot_basis, validated_apply_basis, intent_semantics_oid, read_graph_reference_bindings[], validated_write_coordinate_bindings[], validated_write_key_epoch_bindings[{graph,branch,envelope_epoch,write_key_epoch}], coordinate_schema_transitions[], topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index, effect_directory_root, committed_effect_refs[ConditionalCoordinateRef], constraint_evidence, authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>, authorization_decision_digest:WeakDigest, authorized_permit_scope_digest, resource_transition_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>], resource_charge_effects, txn_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<TxnOutcomePreparationRecord>, final_read_witnesses, final_write_summary, birth_ordinals, merge_record_ref:StrongRef<MergeRecord>?, logical_delta_template_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaTemplate>, logical_delta_template_digest:WeakDigest, optional_physical_accelerators[{apply_basis,digest,payload_ref:ConditionalCoordinateRef,answer_equivalence_proof_ref:StrongRef}], txn_token, final_effect_digest }`. Prepared traversal follows every conditional effect/accelerator strongly; after commit the marker supplies the coordinate and a matching effect cut may stop old optional accelerators/effects, while active derived generations independently retain bytes still used. Repeated digests cross-check typed refs. The template, effects, bindings, key epochs, and final digest must agree. The capsule contains no future command/result or writer fence; the applied marker becomes resulting coordinate heads without entering this prebuilt object.

**CommitCommand / ControlCommand / LogicalCommandRecord / PreparedCommitRecord.** A transaction order unit is `{command_version,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,txn_token,final_certification_reservation_ref:StrongRef<LocalFinalCertificationReservation>,required_reservation_state:Active,order_attempt_input_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptInput>,order_attempt_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptAvailabilityCertificate>,capsule_ref:StrongRef<CommittedEffectCapsule>,logical_delta_template_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaTemplate>,authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>,resource_transition_refs[StrongRef<ResourceLedgerTransition>],txn_outcome_preparation_ref:StrongRef<TxnOutcomePreparationRecord>,payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_branch_heads[WeakMarkerIdentity],expected_branch_key_epochs[{graph,branch,envelope_epoch,write_key_epoch}],topology_epoch,policy_epoch,revocation_index,final_effect_digest}`. A `ControlCommand` is `{command_version,kind,schema_version,typed_payload_ref:StrongRef<SequenceNeutralSpec>,payload_availability_certificate_ref:None|Some{certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>},order_attempt_input_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptInput>,order_attempt_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<LocalOrderAttemptAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_state_conditions[WeakStateIdentity|WeakMarkerIdentity|ExpectedEpoch|ExpectedIndex],authorization_decision_ref:StrongRef<AuthorizationDecisionRecord>}`; CAS expectations are comparison-only and never retain a prior root. The command's `LocalOrderSubject` must exactly match transaction reservation or control spec/conditions/audit freeze. The spec wrapper named by `typed_payload_ref` contains the one terminal audit gate. The generated `PayloadBearingControlKind` table requires `Some` for branch fork/grant bundles, remote-retention/config-anchor evidence publication, backup/restore, and any other spec whose stable closure adds payload bytes; that certificate excludes the future command and order supplement. Non-payload kinds require `None`; every semantic Local command separately carries order/HLC evidence through its replaceable order-attempt input/certificate.

Every typed sequence-neutral spec is canonically encoded once as `SequenceNeutralSpec<Tag> {wire_tag:u16,schema_version,body:Body<Tag>,terminal_audit_freeze:AuditFreezeField<Tag>,terminal_audit_gate:TerminalAuditGate}`; `GlobalSequenceNeutralSpec<Tag>` uses the identical wrapper with the separate Global tag registry. `AuditFreezeField<Tag>` is the generated closed associated type `Required{freeze_ref:the exact registered AuditTerminalFreezeRef arm}|Forbidden{compatibility_row_id}`. Every final protected terminal tag has exactly one Required arm; admitted Local/Meta writes require their admission-fence arm, protected Local/Meta controls require their scope-specific freeze arm, and nonterminal/scaffolding/audit-recovery tags can encode only Forbidden. Appendix prose flattens `body` fields into the surrounding braces for readability: shown audit fields are wrapper fields, not fields inside `Body<Tag>`; when a compact rendering omits them, `wire_types.toml` and `durable_fields.toml` still supply exactly one tag/version/freeze/gate row. No `ControlCommand` or `GlobalControlCommand` contains either audit field. `spec_body_digest` hashes exactly canonical `Body<Tag>` bytes; the domain-separated wrapper transcript and ObjectId include tag, version, body, freeze, and gate, while D1 and the command retain that complete wrapper. Apply revalidates and consumes the required armed freeze atomically with the protected terminal output. Golden encodings and negative fixtures prove that changing, removing, or substituting the freeze/gate leaves `spec_body_digest` unchanged but changes the wrapper ObjectId and is rejected by the tag-associated arm matrix.

The generated local `SequenceNeutralSpec` table is exhaustive. Its v1 envelope rows are exactly `RecoveryBridgeSpec`, `TxnSubmissionSpec`, `TxnAbortSpec`, `CheckpointInstallSpec`, `InitialConfigFloorInstallSpec`, `HistoryCutActivationSpec`, `RemoteRetentionControlSpec`, `AdvanceRemoteConfigurationEvidenceSpec`, `ValidateRemoteConfigurationAnchorSpec`, `IdRangeGrantSpec`, `BranchForkSpec`, `BranchGrantSpec`, `MergePrepareSpec`, `MergeRejectSpec`, `DpTransitionSpec`, `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec`, `AuditTicketAdmissionSpec`, `AuditTerminalSpec`, `AuditContinuityMirrorSpec`, `AuditRecoverySpec`, `AuditCompletenessTransitionSpec`, `CatalogMutationSpec`, `SchemaMutationSpec`, `IndexDefinitionSpec`, `IndexActivationSpec`, `PolicyTransitionSpec`, `ResourceLedgerTransitionSpec`, `RevocationTransitionSpec`, `PrivacyContinuityMirrorSpec`, `KeyDestroyProposal`, `KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec`, `GcProposal`, `ConfigurationTransitionSpec`, `LocalBackupBarrierSpec`, `LocalBackupClosurePublishSpec`, `LocalBackupSealSpec`, `LocalBackupPublishCompletionSpec`, `LocalBackupReleaseSpec`, `LocalRestoreActivationSpec`, `LocalRestoreServicePrepareSpec`, `LocalRestoreServicePromotionSpec`, `LocalRestoreServiceCompletionSpec`, `ShardingFreezeSpec`, `ShardingUnfreezeSpec`, and `BeginRoleTransitionSpec`. Registered inner tags are exactly `RemoteRetentionControlSpec::{AcquireGrant,RegisterConsumerGrant,RequestConsumerRelease,PublishConsumerReleaseEvidence,ApplyAuthorityRelease,PublishAuthorityReleaseAck,ConsumeReleaseAck,AdoptLegacyAuthorityTransfer}`, `DpTransitionSpec::{Prepare,AbandonBeforeCharge,RecordCharge,StartComputing,CommitResult,RecordDelivery}`, `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec::{CreateCursorAndBaselineLease,AckBaselineComplete,CreateLease,RotateCapability,AckComplete,PostActivationCursorTransition,ResetOrExpire}`, and `ConfigurationTransitionSpec::{ProposeJoint,CommitJoint,CommitNew,CommitRetirementFloor}`. There is no generic schema/catalog/security/key/backup/restore/configuration arm and no unregistered phase. `RecoveryBridgeSpec` has fixed `TerminalAuditGate::StructurallyInapplicable{RecoverySystemAuthority}` and is accepted only by `PendingRestoreCreationGuard`; the four audit-system wrappers retain their fixed AuditSystemAuthority gate. Every other state-changing control wrapper carries exactly its registered Required, validated NotRequired, or StructurallyInapplicable gate; apply rejects a control-mutation event whose tag/body/expected-condition/transition commitments do not match. Actual committed merge effects use the ordinary transaction path. No spec may point to its applied result or resulting root. Every transaction or control command deterministically advances `logical_hlc_state`; a transaction additionally advances `CommitSeq`. Apply constructs result objects, then `LogicalStatePayload`, then `LogicalCommandRecord {logical_command_seq,origin:LocalCommandOrigin,command:StrongRef<CommitCommand|ControlCommand>,transaction_marker:StrongMarkerRef?,logical_command_hlc,resulting_state_payload_digest:WeakDigest}`, then `LogicalStateRoot {payload_ref:StrongRef,logical_command_head:StrongCommandRef?}`; fresh genesis alone uses no head.

Exact local `ConfigurationTransitionSpec` is `{phase:ProposeJoint|CommitJoint|CommitNew|CommitRetirementFloor,basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,prospective_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,candidate_closure_proof_ref:StrongRef,paired_checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>?,paired_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,required_prepared/certificate/remote/key/audit/backup_obligation_floor,terminal_audit_gate}`; every phase is a separate command and final retirement proves the new configuration owns every obligation. Exact local `GcProposal` is `{basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,retention_map_digest,complete_typed_root_inventory_digest,sorted_reclaim_objects_and_realizations,availability_and_retirement_ack_refs[StrongRef],excluded_live_prepared/certificate/remote/key/backup/legal_hold/replay/audit/capability obligations,terminal_audit_gate}`; follower recomputation must derive the identical set and only its applied `GcDecisionRecord` authorizes retirement.

A replica-local `PreparedCommitRecord` is `{prepared_ownership_id,prepare_id,record_generation,predecessor_ref:StrongRef<PreparedCommitRecord>?,database_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,group_role:Local,group_id,configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,payload_predicate_digest,local_writer_fence_epoch,txn_token,capsule_ref:StrongRef,command_ref:StrongRef?,base_closure_inventory_digest,current_closure_inventory_digest,strong_logical_refs[StrongRef],exact_realizations[{object_or_subobject_id,encoding_id,placement_id,key_opener_ref:StrongRef}],status:Preparing|Receipted|Ordered{raft_index}|Applied{logical_command_seq,commit_seq}|Abandoned{fence_proof_digest},receipt_nonce}`. Recomputing its ownership ID and every receipt transcript includes the exact database/incarnation/Local group/configuration OID and predicate digest. `LocalPreparedPayloadRoot` maps the stable ownership ID to the latest immutable successor through the role-specific entry type above. Every successor repeats the same domain/config/predicate/base inventory and has an identical or superset current closure; a receipt commitment is retained. `Receipted`/`Ordered` ownership cannot be removed by timeout or crash; only the fenced terminal rules in §5.2 and a committed GC decision may release it. On apply, ownership transfers to the command record/marker/logical state/outcome index before the prepared entry becomes terminal.

**LogicalDeltaTemplate / LogicalDeltaBatch.** A template is `{format,intent_semantics_ref:StrongRef<IntentSemantics>,final_effect_digest,source_intent_root_digest,coordinate_entries[]}`, where entries are canonically sorted and each is `{graph,branch,relation_id,validated_schema_binding,schema_transition:None|Some{transition_ref:StrongRef<SchemaTransition>},delta_payload_ref:ConditionalCoordinateRef,delta_payload_digest}`. The payload is a canonical exact Z-set over `CanonicalRow`; duplicate coordinates/relations, zero weights, noncanonical order, a transition inconsistent with its binding, or a payload not equal to the capsule's before/after effects are invalid. Prepared traversal follows every conditional edge as strong; committed traversal supplies the enclosing marker sequence and may apply only a matching `EffectCut`.

`LogicalDeltaBatch<Role>` has a generated common body `{format,role,coordinate_entries[{source_binding,resulting_binding,relation_id,delta_payload_ref:RegisteredStrongRef<DeltaPayload>}],batch_digest}` and exactly two role schemas. `LogicalDeltaBatch<LocalCommitted>` adds `{source_template_digest:WeakDigest,commit_marker_identity:WeakMarkerIdentity,commit_seq,frontier:Local{commit_seq}}`. `LogicalDeltaBatch<ShardFragment>` adds `{source_fragment_basis_digest:WeakDigest,decision_identity:WeakGlobalCommandIdentity,shard_id,global_logical_command_seq,global_commit_seq,frontier:ShardFragment{global_commit_seq}}`. `batch_digest` covers every preceding canonical field and is the batch idempotency key; the object's full ObjectId is `LogicalDeltaBatchId<Role>`. Local apply/rematerialization and shard decision apply must reproduce the same role-specific object. A retained batch owns payloads directly but does not retain template/fragment, marker/decision, capsule, or predecessor history. Only `LocalCommitted` may inhabit `CommittedDeltaSourceRef::Local`; shard fragments are internal inputs to a `GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch` and are never a public CDC source.

Delta indexes are bounded authenticated windows, not append-only strong maps. `LocalDeltaBatchIndex {format,retained_after_commit_seq,frontier,entries[every commit_seq in (retained_after_commit_seq,frontier] -> StrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch<LocalCommitted>>],retired_prefix_commitment,active_cut_ref:StrongRef<ActivatedDeltaRetentionCut<Local>>?}` and `GlobalDeltaBatchIndex {format,retained_after_global_commit_seq,frontier,entries[every global_commit_seq in (retained_after_global_commit_seq,frontier] -> StrongRef<GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch>],retired_prefix_commitment,active_cut_ref:StrongRef<ActivatedDeltaRetentionCut<Meta>>?}` require a gap-free exact map in their retained interval. `ShardFragmentDeltaBatchIndex {format,shard_id,retained_after_global_commit_seq,observed_through_global_prefix,entries[participating committed global_txn_id/global_commit_seq -> StrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch<ShardFragment>>],nonparticipant_or_noncommit_coverage_commitment,retired_prefix_commitment,active_cut_ref:StrongRef<ActivatedDeltaRetentionCut<Shard>>?}` requires an exact bijection with every locally applied committed participant decision in its retained interval; it does not invent fragments for unrelated global commits.

`DeltaRetentionObligationRef<Role>` is the generated closed union of role-valid cursor/delivery, derived-generation, replay, backup/export, CDC, shard-ack/global-publication, and explicit administrative history promises. `DeltaRetentionCutEvidence<Role> {role_and_group,basis_index_digest,cut_through_position,exact_sorted_obligation_refs[],transferred_batch_owner_refs[],released_or_gap_transition_refs[],authoritative_rematerialization_availability_or_retirement_proof,complete_obligation_bijection,checker_version}` proves that every promise at or below the cut has either moved to an independent strong owner, completed/released, or taken an explicit `GAP`/new-baseline transition. `ProvisionalDeltaRetentionCut<Role>` may authenticate inherited absence but authorizes no new edge removal. The role-specific ordered `LocalDeltaBatchRetentionCutSpec`, `GlobalDeltaBatchRetentionCutSpec`, or `ShardFragmentDeltaRetentionCutSpec` may install `ActivatedDeltaRetentionCut<Role>` and advance `retained_after_*` only after the paired checkpoint/floor and ordinary activated retention cut cover the same position. Apply replaces old strong entries with the prefix commitment in the same state transition; a missing retained entry is corruption, while a query below a proved cut returns `HistoryUnavailable` or the already-recorded gap contract. Checkpoint/configuration floors and backup/restore inventories retain the current index, active cut, and every still-live independent owner. Crash, lease-transfer, concurrent cursor, cut replacement, and rematerialization tests cover every boundary; no checkpoint cut silently invalidates a promised resume range.

**DeliveredBaselinePayload / DeliveredDeltaPayload / DeltaDeliveryEnvelope / resume cursor and lease registry.** `DeliveredBaselinePayload` is `{format,baseline_id:OpaquePublicNonce,derived_identity_digest,source_coverage,baseline_frontier,authorized_cursor_position,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_row_segment_refs[StrongRef],canonical_payload_len,internal_baseline_digest,public_baseline_digest}`. `InternalBaselineDigest` is exactly `BLAKE3("fgdb:internal-baseline:v1" || canonical(format,baseline_id,derived_identity_digest,source_coverage,baseline_frontier,authorized_cursor_position,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_payload_len,exact_concatenated_canonical_result_bytes))`; it is never a default wire value. `PublicBaselineDigest` is exactly `BLAKE3("fgdb:public-baseline:v1" || canonical(format,baseline_id,authorized_cursor_position,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_payload_len,exact_concatenated_canonical_result_bytes))`. Both transcripts exclude storage-only keyed segment refs and their digest fields; only the public transcript excludes the derived identity, source coverage, and raw frontier. `DeliveredDeltaPayload` is `{format,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_zset_segment_refs[StrongRef],canonical_payload_len,output_payload_digest}` with exact transcript `BLAKE3("fgdb:delivered-zset:v1" || canonical(format,output_schema,result_answer_contract,canonical_encoding_version,canonical_payload_len,exact_canonical_zset_bytes))`, likewise excluding segment refs and itself. Mutation/golden tests independently change every included and excluded field and include low-entropy coverage/frontier dictionary attacks against the public digest.

`CommittedDeltaSourceRef` is exactly `Local{batch_ref:StrongRef<LogicalDeltaBatch>,commit_seq}|Global{batch_ref:StrongRef<GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch>,global_commit_seq}`. `DeltaDeliveryEnvelope` is `{format,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,service_visibility_epoch,tenant_principal_authority_digest,derived_identity_digest,baseline_id,start_frontier,resulting_frontier,delivery_id:OpaquePublicNonce,delivery_sequence,authorized_cursor_position,output_payload_ref:StrongRef<DeliveredDeltaPayload>,output_payload_digest,provenance:Atomic{source:CommittedDeltaSourceRef,source_batch_digest}|Coalesced{source_role:Local|Global,first_batch_id,last_batch_id,ordered_source_commitment,source_count},internal_delivery_digest}`. Local and Global frontiers/source IDs have distinct internal tags; W12 emits only Meta-published Global sources, never shard `LogicalDeltaBatch` fragments, while migrated outstanding leases preserve Local but cannot be delivered after a service-epoch change without the explicit posture-transition baseline. `InternalDeliveryDigest` hashes every canonical envelope field except itself, so it commits service epoch, role, output, and full provenance. `AuthorizedDeltaPublicProvenance` and `PublicDeliveryDigest` are separately constructed exactly as §9.5 and Appendix D specify; neither can acquire a hidden envelope field except through the Declassified arm's explicit authorization and audit release. `DeliveryId` is the pre-minted opaque public nonce, not an ObjectId or digest of the internal envelope. `delivery_id`, `baseline_id`, `delivery_lease_id`, `resume_cursor_id`, and every successor capability nonce are pre-minted in the input transition spec.

`DeliveryFrontier = Local{commit_seq,batch_frontier}|Global{global_commit_seq,batch_frontier}`. `ResumeCursorRecord` and `DeliveryLeaseRecord` use the exact namespace/incarnation/service-epoch and tagged-state schemas in §9.5; the Appendix rendering adds only posture-tagged `DeliveryFrontier` fields and `applied Local|Global command seq`. `DeliveryLeaseTransitionSpec` is `CreateCursorAndBaselineLease|AckBaselineComplete|CreateLease|RotateCapability|AckComplete|PostActivationCursorTransition{expected Local cursor version,proved no outstanding Local lease,projected Local frontier,new service_visibility_epoch,new Global baseline payload/lease and pre-minted successor capability}|ResetOrExpire`. ACK transitions atomically remove exact leases and retain the immediate predecessor/request lineage for lost-response replay. The posture transition sets `Global` only with a pending Global baseline under the newly promoted service epoch; no Global delta exists before its ACK, no old-epoch token resumes it, and no coalesced/atomic range crosses roles. A capability authorizes lookup but never retains bytes.

**CommitMarker and physical batching.** A canonical marker is independently hashed:

```text
CommitMarker {
  logical_command_seq:u64, commit_seq:u64,
  effect_source:
    Local { capsule_ref:StrongRef<CommittedEffectCapsule>,
            logical_delta_template_digest:WeakDigest }
    | Global { global_txn_input_ref:ConditionalGlobalTxnInputRef,
               routing_and_participant_commitment:WeakDigest,
               final_effect_digest:WeakDigest,
               aggregate_template_digest:WeakDigest },
  prev_global:ConditionalMarkerRef{axis=Global}?,
  head_updates[{graph,branch,
                expected_previous:ConditionalMarkerRef{axis=Branch(graph,branch)}?}],
  merge_record_oid?, coordinate_schema_transition_digest,
  topology_epoch, policy_epoch, revocation_index,
  txn_token, commit_hlc,
  final_effect_digest,
  authorization_decision_digest, resource_effect_digest,
  payload_availability_certificate_oid?, flags, chain_hash
}
```

The marker itself is the implicit new head for each update. Its effect-source tag is fixed by posture: local apply uses the already-built capsule/template pair; W12 meta apply uses `ConditionalGlobalTxnInputRef {command_oid,assigned_global_logical_command_seq}` to the already-built transaction input plus routing/participant/effect/template commitments. The later global record at that exact sequence must name the same command. Before a matching global command cut, traversal follows the conditional input into the full prepared closure; afterward the head marker remains valid without permanently resurrecting remote prepare grants or effect bytes. A reader that does not know the required W12 tag rejects it. The marker deliberately does not name the terminal outcome or any future record/fragment/global batch; apply constructs the marker first and later objects may name it, avoiding outcome/distributed-batch cycles. `chain_hash` hashes the prior chain value plus marker bytes excluding `chain_hash`. `MarkerBatch {first_seq,last_seq,previous_batch_digest,entry_directory[{marker_oid,offset,length}],canonical_marker_bytes,mmr_update,checksum}` is only a physical pack; object locations resolve each marker independently.

**RecoveryCheckpoint / CheckpointStateVector / RetentionMap.** A checkpoint is `{basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,command_basis:Genesis{command_chain_genesis_seed}|Ordered{covered_basis_logical_command:WeakCommandIdentity,covered_command_chain_hash},marker_basis:NoCommittedTransactionAtBasis{marker_chain_genesis_seed,proof_ref:StrongRef<NoCommittedTransactionAtBasis>}|Committed{covered_global_marker:StrongMarkerRef,covered_marker_chain_hash},basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest,basis_projection_digest,logical_hlc_state,checkpoint_state_vector_ref:StrongRef<CheckpointStateVector>,nonretaining_predecessor_checkpoint_digest}`. `command_basis=Genesis` is legal iff `basis_logical_command_seq=0`; otherwise Ordered is required. `marker_basis=NoCommittedTransactionAtBasis` is legal iff `basis_commit_seq=0`; otherwise Committed is required. Thus a control-only operational database can checkpoint without inventing a marker, while any positive transaction prefix must name the exact marker. The weak command identity and chain/payload/projection commitments authenticate the cut without retaining prior command/spec/checkpoint chains. The vector is generated from the exact versioned payload schema and has one typed entry per field: `CopiedStrong`, `ProjectedSnapshot`, `ResetByCheckpointInstall`, `SelfExcluded`, or the single constrained `InstallProvisionalCut{field_tag=retention_map_root,retention_cut_body_ref,checkpoint_binding=InstallThisCheckpoint,install_input_kind,assigned_order_literal}`. That fifth tag is required exactly once for an operational basis and forbidden for Genesis; it commits the already-built checkpoint-free body and deterministic applied-result recipe without a future checkpoint/result OID. `recovery_checkpoint_ref` always uses `InstallThisCheckpoint`; operational `config_payload_floor_ref` uses `InstallPairedConfigFloor`, while Genesis copies absence. `basis_projection_digest = BLAKE3("fgdb:checkpoint-projection:v1" ‖ canonical(vector reconstruction with exact literals))`; it never hashes a future checkpoint/floor/cut OID. A missing, duplicate, illegally self-excluded, or otherwise unclassified field is invalid. Control-only checkpoint/cut/recovery fixtures cover every `(logical_seq>0,commit_seq=0)` crash point.

`CheckpointInstallSpec` is `{basis:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_payload_digest:WeakDigest,basis_projection_digest,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,paired_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>?,retention_cut_body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>?,reset_field_tags[]}`. It must be the first retained record at `basis_logical_command_seq+1`; apply verifies the exact current basis/vector, installs its own already-known checkpoint ref, and, for every operational basis, atomically installs the required paired floor and deterministic provisional cut whose checkpoint/vector/prefix and weak observations match. `retention_cut_body_ref=None` is legal only for Genesis, where no prior absence needs re-attestation. Genesis advances to `CheckpointInstalled`; later installs preserve `Operational`, apply only declared resets, and otherwise preserve every field. `InitialConfigFloorInstallSpec {checkpoint_installed_state:WeakStateIdentity,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,checkpoint_state_vector_digest,initial_config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,initial_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,expected_logical_command_seq,terminal_audit_gate}` is the sole local `CheckpointInstalled -> Operational` transition.

The checkpoint-free pre-order cut-recipe union is `CommandCutRecipe {axis:Logical,stop_at:WeakCommandIdentity} | GlobalCommandCutRecipe {axis:GlobalLogical,stop_at:WeakGlobalCommandIdentity,exact_covered_global_prefix} | ShardCommandCutRecipe {axis:ShardRaft,stop_at:WeakShardCommandIdentity,exact_covered_shard_raft_index,exact_covered_global_prefix} | MarkerCutRecipe {axis,stop_at:WeakMarkerIdentity} | EffectCutRecipe {graph,branch,through_seq,effect_payload_digest_range}`. `RetentionCutBody` is `{role:Local|Meta|Shard{shard_id},basis_state_identity:WeakStateIdentity,command_cut_recipe,sorted_marker_cut_recipes[],sorted_effect_cut_recipes[],covered_policy_epoch,covered_coordinate_set_commitment,verified_first_retained_order,completeness_digest}` and must contain the role's one command recipe plus every marker/effect recipe to be superseded. It contains **no checkpoint identity or reference** and therefore exists before the vector/checkpoint that will consume it. Construction is strictly `RetentionCutBody -> CheckpointStateVector -> RecoveryCheckpoint -> checkpoint-install input`. The vector's `InstallProvisionalCut` entry means “attach this body to `InstallThisCheckpoint` at the assigned install order”; it never points backward from the body to that checkpoint.

Apply deterministically constructs `ProvisionalRetentionCutSet {body_ref:StrongRef<RetentionCutBody>,checkpoint_ref:Local{StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>}|Meta{StrongRef<GlobalRecoveryCheckpoint>}|Shard{StrongRef<ShardRecoveryCheckpoint>},install_input_ref:Local{StrongRef<ControlCommand>,assigned_logical_command_seq}|Meta{StrongRef<GlobalControlCommand>,assigned_global_logical_command_seq}|Shard{StrongRef<ShardControlCommand>,assigned_shard_raft_index},basis_projection_digest:WeakDigest}` before constructing the payload. Role, basis, recipe, checkpoint/vector, assigned order, and install-input fields must match exactly. The checkpoint and input are already known at apply time; the future result root/record is not named. The outer state root and command head then prove the corresponding applied record.

`HistoryCutActivationSpec {provisional_cut_ref:StrongRef<ProvisionalRetentionCutSet>,checkpoint_install_record_ref:StrongCommandRef,expected_retention_map_basis:WeakStateIdentity,verified_contiguous_suffix_start,terminal_audit_gate}` is the sole local strengthening path; Global/Shard use the matching global/shard record tags. Apply creates `ActivatedRetentionCutSet {provisional_cut_ref:StrongRef<ProvisionalRetentionCutSet>,checkpoint_install_record_ref:StrongCommandRef|StrongGlobalCommandRef|StrongShardCommandRef,activation_applied_ref:AuthorityAppliedRef}` and atomically replaces that provisional map entry. `RetentionMap` contains policy epochs and exactly one `Provisional|Activated` entry for each retained cut body. Operational checkpoint reset atomically drops superseded entries and installs the new provisional set; at every crash point, either the old activated authority or the new provisional authority authenticates already-missing bytes. Traversal may stop only when axis/group/checkpoint/body completeness and the provisional input+assigned-order or activated record proof all validate. Strong roots always win. A cut transfers authority to checkpoint+install+suffix; it does not assert that pruned capsules or old delta ranges remain individually recoverable. Recovery/crash tests begin with bytes already reclaimed under the prior cut and interrupt every install/activation step for all three roles.

**ConstraintState / ResourceLedger / Local transaction cross-reference.** `ConstraintStateRoot` is keyed by a full `CoordinateSchemaBinding` and contains canonical constraint maps plus base-state digest. `ResourceLedgerState` maps tenant/scope to limits, committed charges, and `ResourceReservationId`; `ResourceChargeEffect` atomically creates/releases named durable charges. The sole Local schemas for `TxnOutcomePreparationRecord`, `TxnAbortSpec`, `TxnOutcomeRecord`, and `TxnOutcomeIndex` are the exact BeginStaging/Registered/PrepareAdmitted/TerminalPending definitions in **Local 1.0 durable transaction formats** above. There is no `TxnSubmissionSpec`, `Submitted`, or `Absent -> terminal` alternate schema. W12 uses separately named `GlobalTxnOutcomePreparationRecord`, `GlobalTxnOutcomeRecord`, and global indexes. G0 rejects duplicate logical-schema names or a second body hash for any ObjectKind. A `TxnOutcomeCapability` authenticates lookup/retry of the posture-tagged record and never grants mutation authority.

**BranchManifest / branch key-envelope DAG.** A branch manifest is `{graph,branch_id,origin:Genesis{creation_checkpoint_or_genesis_basis:GenesisBranchBasis}|Fork{parent_branch,parent_head:StrongMarkerRef,fork_boundary_logical_command_seq,boundary_reservation_identity},base_checkpoint_ref?,key_envelope_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,current_envelope_epoch,current_write_key_epoch,policy}`. The Genesis tag forbids parent/head/boundary fields; Fork requires all four and verifies parent ancestry/head/epochs at the exact already assigned `BranchEpochBoundaryReservation` boundary. The later install command sequence is deliberately absent. Both wire tags are registered and cross-tag bytes are noncanonical.

Expensive key closures never depend on a future install sequence. `BranchEpochBoundaryReserveSpec {reservation_id,operation:Fork|SnapshotGrant|StartOrContinueAdvancingGrant|RevokeAdvancingGrant|Rotate,graph,branch,parent_or_target_scope,expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_envelope_epoch,expected_write_epoch,transition_nonce,complete_affected_coordinate_set,expected_boundary_index_absence,terminal_audit_gate}` is ordered first. Apply validates current state and creates immutable `BranchEpochBoundaryReservation {source_spec_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReserveSpec>,reservation_id,operation,graph_branch_scope,frozen_head_and_epoch_commitment,boundary_logical_command_seq,transition_nonce,exclusive_branch_head_and_epoch_hold_root_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryHoldRoot>,state:Active}`. Every branch mutation/key transition consults the hold root; conflicting work waits or rejects, while disjoint commands may proceed. `ObjectCreationBoundary` is the exact tag `CommittedExisting{creation_marker_identity,creation_commit_seq}|TransactionReserved{final_certification_reservation_identity,permanent_object_ordinal}|BranchEpochReserved{boundary_reservation_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReservation>,permanent_object_ordinal}`. It supplies stable AAD identity before ordering; actual applied sequence remains in the command/result and is not part of pre-order object identity.

`WeakEpochIdentity` is `{graph,branch,kind,epoch,record_oid,rotation_chain_digest}` and is nonretaining. `BranchKeyEpochRecord` is pre-order-buildable only after the boundary reservation and is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,kind:Envelope|Write,epoch,key_id,predecessor:Genesis|SameEpochLifecycle{ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>}|PriorEpoch{identity:WeakEpochIdentity},transition_nonce,boundary_reservation_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReservation>,state:Active{opened_at_boundary}|Closed{opened_at_boundary,closed_through_boundary,close_reason}}`; both boundary fields are the already-assigned reservation identity/sequence, never the later install order. Closing an epoch uses the strong same-epoch predecessor; opening a successor uses only the weak prior-epoch identity/rotation-chain commitment. Command history, transparency, and the epoch registry authenticate rotation without making the current epoch retain every old key forever. The record points to no future install command. Apply installs it only while the exact reservation/hold is Active and byte-matches the frozen head/epochs. Old envelope roots/nodes/grants/backups—not a permanent epoch chain—are the strong owners that keep an old key decryptable; when they disappear, two-stage destruction can prove zero references. Genesis/no-fake-parent, cross-branch/head, boundary-substitution, unrelated-command interleaving, and reproposal tests are mandatory.

`KeyEnvelopeNode` is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,owning_graph,owning_branch,envelope_epoch,node_kind,coverage_cut:{through_logical_command_seq,through_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity?},children[{range,child_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeNode>,child_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,wrapped_child_dek,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}],inherited_roots[{source_graph,source_branch,source_envelope_epoch,source_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,source_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,maximum_logical_command_seq,maximum_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity?,wrapped_source_envelope_key,wrapped_source_root_dek,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}],write_epochs[{write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,allowed_creation_range,wrapped_write_epoch_key,wrap_profile,aad_bytes,aad_digest}]}`. `KeyEnvelopeRoot` is `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,envelope_epoch,envelope_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,current_write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,root_node_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeNode>,root_node_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,coverage_cut,profile_oid}`. Nodes are canonically sorted persistent-tree objects; inherited/source roots, their selected ciphertext realizations, and epoch records are constructed first. The four exact AAD domains are:

```text
H("fgdb:key-envelope-child:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  graph, branch, envelope_epoch, parent_node_kind, child_range,
  child_oid, canonical(child_ciphertext_ref), wrap_profile, envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:key-envelope-inherit:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  target_graph, target_branch, target_envelope_epoch,
  source_graph, source_branch, source_envelope_epoch, source_root_oid,
  canonical(source_root_ciphertext_ref),
  maximum_logical_command_seq, maximum_marker, wrap_profile, target_envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:key-envelope-write:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  graph, branch, envelope_epoch, write_epoch_record_oid,
  allowed_creation_range, wrap_profile, envelope_key_id)
H("fgdb:branch-object-dek-wrap:v1", namespace, incarnation,
  logical_oid, ciphertext_id, dek_id, graph, branch, write_epoch,
  canonical(object_creation_boundary), wrap_profile, write_key_id)
```

The stored AAD bytes must equal the canonical transcript; a digest alone is not usable AAD. `KeyEnvelopeGrant` is built after its root and selected root ciphertext and binds `{grant_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,graph,branch,envelope_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,envelope_epoch,write_epoch?,coverage_cut,mode:SnapshotAtHead|AdvancingBranch,recipient_id,recipient_public_key_id,wrapped_root_object_dek,wrapped_envelope_key,wrap_profile,grant_aad,issuer,policy_epoch,revocation_index,issued_at,expiry?,signature}`. Its AAD is `canonical("fgdb:key-envelope-recipient:v1", every preceding scope/identity/coverage/mode/StrongCiphertextRef field except wrapped bytes/signature)`. A snapshot grant can name only a frozen closed root. An advancing grant intentionally covers new wraps under the named active epoch until rotation; a later epoch requires a new ordered grant. A live grant/edge pins its exact named ciphertext even if compaction creates another realization of the same logical root/node.

After the ordered boundary reservation, the entire physical/logical key closure is finalized before the later install order. `BranchForkBundle` is `{boundary_reservation_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReservation>,transition_nonce,parent,parent_expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,parent_expected_envelope_epoch,parent_expected_write_epoch,child_branch_id,child_policy,closed_parent_envelope_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,closed_parent_write_epoch_record_ref:StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>,frozen_parent_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,frozen_parent_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef,parent_successor_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],parent_successor_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,parent_successor_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,child_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],child_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,child_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,grant_refs[StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeGrant>],complete_object_wrap_ciphertext_realization_inventory,closure_digest}`. `BranchGrantBundle` is `{boundary_reservation_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReservation>,transition_nonce,operation:SnapshotAtHead|StartOrContinueAdvancing|RevokeAdvancing,branch,expected_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_envelope_epoch,expected_write_epoch,closed_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],frozen_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>?,frozen_root_ciphertext_ref:StrongCiphertextRef?,successor_epoch_record_refs[StrongRef<BranchKeyEpochRecord>],successor_root_ref:StrongRef<KeyEnvelopeRoot>,successor_manifest_ref:StrongRef<BranchManifest>,grant_or_revocation_record_refs[StrongRef],complete_object_wrap_ciphertext_realization_inventory,closure_digest}`. Every epoch/wrap/grant/manifest field byte-matches the same Active reservation and uses `ObjectCreationBoundary::BranchEpochReserved`. The bundle is built bottom-up under a stable prepared owner: epoch records → ciphertexts/encodings/placements/openers → `StrongCiphertextRef` availability certificates → envelope nodes/roots → grants/manifests → bundle. Its payload-availability certificate covers that exact closed inventory and excludes only the future install control/order supplement.

`BranchForkSpec` is `{boundary_reservation_ref:StrongRef<BranchEpochBoundaryReservation>,required_reservation_state:Active,bundle_ref:StrongRef<BranchForkBundle>,bundle_payload_availability_certificate_ref:StrongRef<PayloadAvailabilityCertificate>,expected_parent_head:WeakMarkerIdentity,expected_parent_envelope_epoch,expected_parent_write_epoch,transition_nonce,terminal_audit_gate}`. `BranchGrantSpec` is the analogous `{boundary_reservation_ref,required_reservation_state:Active,bundle_ref,certificate_ref,expected_head,expected_envelope_epoch,expected_write_epoch,transition_nonce,terminal_audit_gate}`. Apply creates no key material/ciphertext/placement/envelope/epoch/grant/manifest and performs no ambient physical selection: it validates the complete bundle/certificate/reservation/held basis, closure disjointness, and grant subset laws, installs the known manifests/registries, consumes the reservation, and releases its holds atomically. The actual install sequence is assigned by the ordinary order supplement and recorded only in applied lifecycle/provenance. Snapshot issue and revocation encode close→frozen root→double rotation; advancing issue may bind the exact active root/epoch without rotation. `BranchEpochBoundaryCancelSpec` is legal before any bundle/prepared owner/certificate/wrap exists and requires `NoBoundaryClosureProof`; `BranchEpochBoundaryAbandonSpec` is legal after construction only with complete signer/prepared closure, no install order/candidate/external grant publication, and typed cleanup/zeroization evidence. Once a grant or revocation is externally published, recovery must complete the matching install; timeout cannot release the hold. Expiry without ordered revocation/rotation does not claim cryptographic cutoff. Envelope reachability is part of GC/key-destruction/backup inventory. Fork/handoff/rotation tests cover sibling, post-fork-parent, post-snapshot, post-revocation, expired-grant, stale-prepared-wrap, unrelated command interleaving, reproposal, cancel/abandon, merge overbreadth, restore, every reserve/build/order/apply crash boundary, and collected-key decryption.

**MergeRecord / BranchMergeLedger.** A squash `MergeRecord` retains `{merge_token,merge_request_commitment,target,target_basis:StrongMarkerRef,source_heads[StrongMarkerRef],merge_bases[StrongMarkerRef],imported_range_tokens[{branch,first:WeakMarkerIdentity,last:WeakMarkerIdentity,base:WeakMarkerIdentity,chain_digest}],imported_range_keys[],resolution_policy_oid,resolution_digest,final_effect_digest}` and is linked from capsule/marker. Range tokens are weak provenance, not target ancestry or implicit retention. Pre-order `MergePrepareSpec` is `{client_request_nonce,request_commitment,candidate_merge_token,capability_replay_ref:StrongRef<MergeOutcomeCapabilityReplayRecord>,expected_merge_index_absence_or_matching_retry,terminal_audit_gate}`; the coordinator mints token and every capability byte before ordering, and apply uses no entropy. The replay record's body is the sole exact `MergeOutcomeCapability` body and the common header supplies the complete namespace/incarnation/service/tenant/principal/authority/policy/revocation/key/profile/window domain. The ledger first maps `{tenant,principal,target,client_request_nonce}` to the chosen token plus replay ref before evaluation; a same-request retry returns identical canonical bytes, a different proposed candidate is ignored after success, and conflicting commitment reuse is rejected. `ImportedRangeKey` hashes `{database namespace,target graph/branch,source branch/range/chain digest,merge semantics,resolution policy}` and excludes the mutable target basis. `BranchMergeLedgerRoot` contains `outcomes[merge_token -> {original_request,capability_replay_ref,basis:WeakMarkerIdentity,state:InFlight|Committed{target_marker:WeakMarkerIdentity,final_effect_digest}|Rejected{stable_reason_digest}|Compacted{summary_ref}|ExpiredTombstone{token_digest,capability_commitment,expiry_evidence_digest}}]` plus `coverage_domains[H(namespace,target,source_branch,source_chain_domain,merge_semantics,resolution_policy) -> normalized_nonoverlapping_ranges[{first:WeakMarkerIdentity,last:WeakMarkerIdentity,chain_digest,imported_range_key}]]`. Transaction apply validates the prepared token/request/range-key set and installs the terminal outcome, normalized coverage, and merge marker atomically. Token retries return the original outcome; interval lookup detects exact and partial overlap, which rejects `AlreadyImported` or applies only a declared canonical uncovered remainder. Both maps are non-forgetting idempotency state preserved across checkpoint/history cuts, backup/restore, reconfiguration, and GC; replay ref retirement requires the separate profiled expiry transition.

**PayloadReceipt / PayloadAvailabilityCertificate / ConfigPayloadFloor / GcEpoch.** `RemotePreparedIdentity { storage_member,prepared_ownership_id,base_closure_inventory_digest,latest_record_observation:NonRetainingRemoteObservation{record_digest:WeakDigest,observed_prepared_payload_root_generation} ? }` names the stable signed ownership promise; the optional diagnostic is neither a local ObjectId nor a reachability edge. A receipt binds `{database_id,database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,configuration_state_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,payload_predicate_digest,storage_member,failure_domain,local_writer_fence_epoch,prepared_owner:RemotePreparedIdentity,encoding_and_placement_requirements[],symbol/source-block coverage,fsync_generation,proposal_valid_through?,nonce}` and a domain-separated member signature/MAC. The signer must still hold the matching `WriterLeaseGuard/FenceToken`; a receiver verifies the epoch against the member's current fenced identity/configuration before using the receipt. Successor records preserve that ownership/base closure and may only strengthen current closure. `proposal_valid_through` limits freshness for forming a new proposal; it is never a storage lease, retention horizon, or deletion permission. A certificate repeats namespace/incarnation, the exact configuration ref/predicate digest, canonically lists receipt refs, exact base logical-object plus encoding/placement requirements, FEC recoverability calculation, verifier version, and threshold signature.

Installed local `ConfigPayloadFloor` is the exact schema `{schema_version,payload_schema_oid,protocol_registry_epoch,basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,closed_through_raft_index,closed_through_logical_command_seq,current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,prospective_joint_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>?,prospective_final_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,failure_domain_policy_ref:StrongRef,current_checkpoint:WeakCheckpointIdentity,checkpoint_state_vector_digest:WeakDigest,retained_command_suffix_endpoints,retained_marker_suffix_endpoints,mandatory_inventory_root:StrongRef<MandatoryInventory>,prepared_owner_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalPreparedOwnerFloor>,receipt_certificate_signer_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalReceiptCertificateSignerFloor>,audit_ticket_fence_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalAuditTicketFenceFloor>,retention_cut_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalRetentionCutFloor>,branch_key_allocator_merge_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalBranchKeyAllocatorMergeFloor>,outcome_conflict_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalOutcomeConflictFloor>,delivery_replay_derived_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalDeliveryReplayDerivedFloor>,continuity_service_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalContinuityServiceFloor>,remote_trust_release_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalRemoteTrustReleaseFloor>,gc_key_destruction_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalGcKeyDestructionFloor>,backup_restore_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalBackupRestoreFloor>,migration_transition_floor_ref:StrongRef<LocalMigrationTransitionFloor>,coverage_bitmap,nonretaining_predecessor_floor_digest:WeakDigest}`; its ObjectId is its floor identity. It has no strong edge to its basis root, checkpoint/vector, predecessor floor, transition spec, or applied command.

`MandatoryInventory` is `{schema_version,payload_schema_oid,protocol_registry_epoch,role:Local|Meta|Shard{shard_id},ordered_entries[MandatoryInventoryEntry],coverage_bitmap,body_digest:BodyDigest<MandatoryInventory>}`. `MandatoryInventoryEntry` is `{class_tag,source_slot_tag,activation_predicate_id,value:RetainedStrong{typed_ref:RegisteredStrongRef}|CurrentCheckpointObservation{checkpoint:WeakCheckpointIdentity,checkpoint_state_vector_digest:WeakDigest,logical_inventory_digest,availability_receipt_refs[StrongRef]}}`. `RegisteredStrongRef` is the closed generated union of role-legal typed strong-reference encodings, never a raw ObjectId. `MandatoryInventoryClassRegistry` maps each stable class tag to one exact target kind, reference encoding, payload field or protocol-state slot, live predicate, cut/release predicate, and owning floor field. Entries are canonical by class tag and the bitmap equals every currently activated class exactly once. Unknown, duplicate, missing, wrong-role, or dormant-feature entries fail G0; deleting each class in turn is a generated negative fixture.

The Local inventory and named floors cover current/joint/final configurations; command and marker suffixes; prepared owners, receipts, certificates, signer locks, and an audit fence; provisional and activated cuts plus the retention map; branch/head/key-envelope/grant/merge and allocation state; transaction outcome and conflict state; cursor, delivery, replay, archive and derived state; identity, privacy, audit, and cluster-incarnation/service-catalog continuities; remote trust and every stage of the six-transition release; local GC and key destruction; every nonterminal Local backup pin, closure, publication and release; `RestoreSourceLease`, reconciliation, hidden activation/visibility, service promotion and catalog receipt; and sharding freeze, transition, migration authority transfer and retirement obligations until adoption/finalize. `RetiredLocal` has no `ConfigPayloadFloor`: its manifest owns only the compact certified transition/retirement/audit proof closure.

For every role, `CurrentCheckpointObservation` is the sole weak checkpoint exception and must byte-match the separately strong current payload checkpoint. An operational install creates a `ProvisionalRetentionCutSet`: it may authenticate bytes already absent under inherited activated coverage, but it cannot satisfy any new-reclamation, key-destruction, backup-pin-release, remote-release, topology-retirement, or ownership-discharge predicate. A replacement provisional must dominate every absorbed activated absence until its own activation; only an `ActivatedRetentionCutSet` can authorize a new physical release. Prefix, checkpoint, payload-schema, registry-epoch, or obligation drift requires recomputation before installation. Initial installation is the fresh `CheckpointInstalled -> Operational` command; configuration retirement requires a final floor committed after and covering through `CommitNew`.

`GcProposal` is the Local pre-order bounded-set authorization `{gc_id,basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,basis_logical_command_seq,basis_commit_seq,basis_raft_index,configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>,config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,activated_retention_cut_ref:StrongRef<ActivatedRetentionCutSet>,retention_map_digest,complete_typed_root_inventory_ref:StrongRef<GcRootInventory>,candidate_derivation_profile_oid,sorted_reclaim_objects_and_realizations,exact_reclaim_set_digest,required_storage_profile_and_member_set,completed_remote_release_refs[GcRemoteReleaseCompletionRef],excluded_live_prepared_certificate_remote_key_backup_legal_hold_replay_audit_capability_restore_result_workspace_and_delivery_obligation_commitment,terminal_audit_gate}`. It uses only weak basis identities and strong current floors/inventories. Every follower recomputes the candidate and either rejects the command or applies `GcDecisionRecord {proposal_ref:StrongRef<GcProposal>,applied_control_ref:AppliedControlRef,stable_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,config_payload_floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>,retention_map_digest,typed_root_validation_digest,decision:Rejected{stable_reason}|Accepted{gc_id,authorized_reclaim_set_digest,required_storage_member_set_digest,quarantine_generation}}`; the input never names this result.

An accepted decision does **not** authorize physical work by itself. `LocalGcApplyQuarantineSpec {decision_record_ref:StrongRef<GcDecisionRecord::Accepted>,expected_current_state:WeakStateIdentity,expected_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,expected_root_slot_generations,current_complete_typed_root_inventory_ref:StrongRef<GcRootInventory>,current_reachability_recomputation_ref:StrongRef<GcReachabilityProof>,newly_reachable_disjoint_proof_ref:StrongRef<GcDisjointnessProof>,exact_authorized_reclaim_set,sorted_member_operation_plans[{operation_id,idempotency_token_digest,storage_member_id,storage_profile_oid,target_inventory_digest,canonical_request_transcript_digest}],complete_member_and_target_bijection_digest,terminal_audit_gate}` requires `reclaim_set ⊆ authorized_set` and disjointness from every current root slot, candidate result, prepared/certificate/Raft owner, and independently retained obligation. Apply atomically installs `LocalGcReclaimAuthorizationRecord` plus `GcReclaimQuarantineRoot {gc_id,authorization_identity,object_and_realization_set,quarantine_generation,state:AuthorizedNotStarted,member_operation_root_ref:StrongRef<GcPhysicalOperationRoot>}`. The operation root contains exactly one immutable `GcPhysicalOperationRecord::Requested` per required storage member/target before any call. Every encoder, dedupe lookup, prepared receipt, command validator, compactor, and root publisher rejects a new retaining edge or realization selection to a quarantined identity.

Each member service has one linear idempotent operation state keyed by `(operation_id,idempotency_token_digest)`: `Requested -> Started{member_monotonic_counter,pre_operation_physical_root_digest} -> Completed{member_monotonic_counter,post_operation_physical_root_digest,receipt_digest}` or `Requested -> CancelledBeforeStart{counter,cancellation_receipt_digest}`. It cannot move from Started to Cancelled, and timeout changes no state. `GcPhysicalStartReceipt` and `GcPhysicalMemberReceipt` are the signed portable projections of those transitions and bind `{gc_id,authorization_identity,quarantine_generation,operation_id,idempotency_token_digest,storage_member_id,storage_profile_oid,target_inventory_digest,canonical_request_transcript_digest,pre_operation_physical_root_digest,member_monotonic_counter}`; completion additionally binds the exact deleted-or-crypto-erased inventory, post-operation physical root and probe digests, durability evidence, completion counter/time profile, signer key/epoch, and signature. `LocalGcCancelSpec` is legal only with an exact `GcCancellationBijectionProof` over one `CancelledBeforeStart` receipt for every required operation and no start/completion receipt; it removes the quarantine and records `CancelledBeforePhysicalStart`. If any operation reached Started, recovery must finish the same operation set.

`LocalGcPhysicalProgressSpec` may monotonically record a verified subset of start/completion receipts and the exact missing/failed set but releases nothing. `LocalGcPhysicalCompletionSpec {reclaim_authorization_record_ref:StrongRef<LocalGcReclaimAuthorizationRecord>,expected_quarantine_root_ref:StrongRef<GcReclaimQuarantineRoot>,sorted_member_receipt_refs[StrongRef<GcPhysicalMemberReceipt>],complete_member_and_target_bijection_proof_ref:StrongRef<GcPhysicalCompletionBijectionProof>,post_reclaim_inventory_ref:StrongRef<PhysicalInventory>,current_root_recheck_ref:StrongRef<GcReachabilityProof>,completed_two_sided_release_commitment,expected_state_conditions,terminal_audit_gate}` accepts every and only required terminal receipt, rechecks current logical reachability and unchanged quarantine, then moves the quarantine to `PhysicallyCompleted` and creates `LocalGcPhysicalCompletionRecord`. Only after that command's audit mirror and an activated cut covers the authorization/quarantine/completion chain may heavy GC evidence and reclaimed logical locators leave the GC floor. Missing, duplicate, wrong-operation, wrong-member, wrong-inventory, stale-root, or partial receipts reject completion; they never select a misleading terminal state.

**KeyWrap / KeyDestroyRecord / BackupManifest.** `KeyWrap` binds `{database_security_namespace_id,cluster_incarnation,logical_oid,ciphertext_id,dek_id,scope:Recipient|Database|BranchEpoch{graph,branch,write_epoch,object_creation_boundary:ObjectCreationBoundary}|Replica|Backup,wrap_algorithm,wrap_key_id,wrap_key_epoch,wrapped_dek,aad_bytes,aad_digest,issuer_signature}`; BranchEpoch AAD is exactly the branch-object transcript, while every other scope has its own registered transcript. Namespace-key escrow uses separately typed `ObjectIdKeyWrap` for `K_oid`. Rewrap creates only a new wrap; re-encryption creates a new CiphertextId and EncodingId realizations. `KeyDestroyFloorRef` is `Checkpoint{checkpoint_ref:StrongRef<RecoveryCheckpoint>}|Configuration{floor_ref:StrongRef<ConfigPayloadFloor>}` and `KeyDestroyExternalAckRef` is `Backup{ack_ref:StrongRef<BackupKeyReleaseAck>}|LegalHold{ack_ref:StrongRef<LegalHoldReleaseAck>}|RemoteConsumer{ack_ref:StrongRef<RemoteKeyConsumerReleaseAck>}`. `KeyDestructionTarget` is the closed union `KmsKeyVersion{kms_authority_id,key_uri,key_version}|HsmObject{hsm_cluster_id,slot_id,object_handle_digest}|StorageMemberReplica{consensus_domain,member_id,material_class,material_identity_digest}`; canonical target identity is `H(domain,canonical(target))`. `KeyDestructionOperationPlan` is `{operation_id,idempotency_token_digest,target:KeyDestructionTarget,canonical_request_transcript_digest,required_receipt_profile_oid}` and plans are sorted by target identity with no duplicate target or operation ID.

`KeyDestroyProposal` is the pre-order body `{key_identity,expected_key_state:RetainedDecryptOnly,basis_state:WeakStateIdentity,expected_current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,expected_prospective_configuration_set_digest,exact_root_slot_generations,checkpoint_and_configuration_floor_refs[KeyDestroyFloorRef],generated_scanned_root_inventory_ref:StrongRef<KeyReferenceInventory>,zero_reference_proof_ref:StrongRef<ZeroReferenceProof>,backup_legal_hold_and_external_consumer_ack_refs[KeyDestroyExternalAckRef],threshold_authorization_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestructionAuthorization>,sorted_destruction_operation_plans[KeyDestructionOperationPlan],complete_target_set_digest,expected_state_conditions,terminal_audit_gate}`. The generated inventory includes every branch epoch, envelope node/root/grant, advancing-grant obligation, reachable ciphertext/wrap/opener, prepared/certificate/audit/outcome/result/workspace/replay/DP/backup, current or prospective configuration, and signing/verifier dependency. Apply atomically installs `KeyReferenceQuarantine {key_identity,quarantine_generation,proposal_identity:WeakDigest,installed_at_logical_command_seq,target_set_digest,no_new_reference_rule_id}` and one `ExternalKeyDestructionOperationRecord {operation_id,key_identity,quarantine_ref:StrongRef<KeyReferenceQuarantine>,target:KeyDestructionTarget,idempotency_token_digest,canonical_request_transcript_digest,required_receipt_profile_oid,status:Requested,source_command_ref:StrongRef<ControlCommand>,assigned_logical_command_seq}` for every and only plan, then moves the key to `DestroyPending`. The canonical operation-root map is keyed by target identity and proves a plan/record bijection. No physical request precedes durable publication of all records; retry/status uses the same operation ID/transcript, and a timeout neither retries with a new ID nor implies destruction.

`AuthenticatedKeyDestructionReceipt` is `{operation_id,idempotency_token_digest,target:KeyDestructionTarget,canonical_request_transcript_digest,destruction_result:Destroyed{target_terminal_counter,provider_evidence_digest}|AlreadyDestroyed{matching_prior_operation_id,target_terminal_counter,provider_evidence_digest},completed_at,time_authority_profile_oid,provider_key_id,provider_key_epoch,signature}`. `AlreadyDestroyed` is accepted only when provider evidence cryptographically binds the same target and canonical request lineage. `TargetCompletionBijectionProof` binds the proposal target-set digest, canonical operation-root digest, sorted receipt identities, and proves exactly one valid terminal receipt per target/operation with no missing, extra, duplicate, substituted, or conflicting result.

`KeyDestroyFinalizeSpec` is `{proposal_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestroyProposal>,expected_quarantine_ref:StrongRef<KeyReferenceQuarantine>,sorted_operation_record_refs[StrongRef<ExternalKeyDestructionOperationRecord>],sorted_authenticated_destruction_receipt_refs[StrongRef<AuthenticatedKeyDestructionReceipt>],target_completion_bijection_proof_ref:StrongRef<TargetCompletionBijectionProof>,exact_current_role_payload_and_root_slot_identities,current_configuration_ref:StrongRef<ConfigurationState>,current_prospective_configuration_set_digest,current_complete_generated_root_inventory_ref:StrongRef<KeyReferenceInventory>,current_zero_reference_recomputation_ref:StrongRef<ZeroReferenceProof>,no_new_reference_since_quarantine_proof_ref:StrongRef<NoNewKeyReferenceProof>,expected_state_conditions,terminal_audit_gate}`. It requires current-root/configuration/slot equality, zero retaining references, and the exact proposal/operation/receipt bijection. Apply selects `DestroyedPendingCertificate` and creates compact `KeyDestroyRecord {key_identity,quarantine_generation,proposal_identity:WeakDigest,finalize_spec_identity:WeakDigest,complete_target_set_digest,operation_and_receipt_commitment,verified_current_inventory_digest,applied_finalize_identity:WeakAuthorityAppliedIdentity,terminal_audit_commitment}`; the record has no strong path to proposal, finalize, receipts, scanned inventories, old floors, or a future certificate.

Only after that record, its resulting durable root, and its required audit mirror exist may the current quorum create `KeyDestructionCertificate {SameGroupCertificateHeader,key_identity,quarantine_generation,key_destroy_record_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestroyRecord>,post_finalize_state_root_ref:StrongRef<LogicalStateRoot>,operation_and_receipt_commitment,verified_current_inventory_digest,finalize_audit_mirror_identity,certificate_attempt_ref:StrongRef<CertificateAttemptRecord>,canonical_signature_set}`. `KeyDestroyCertificatePublishSpec {key_destroy_record_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestroyRecord>,certificate_ref:StrongRef<KeyDestructionCertificate>,expected_key_state:DestroyedPendingCertificate,expected_quarantine_generation,expected_current_state:WeakStateIdentity,terminal_audit_gate}` is the sole transition to final `Destroyed` and installs a compact certificate-index edge. Heavy inputs remain owned by the key lifecycle and certificate ledgers until publication's audit mirror plus an activated cut; compact result/receipt commitment/certificate remain through the crypto-erasure evidence floor. No state reaches final `Destroyed` if any reachable or independently obligated object can still require the key, any target lacks a receipt, or the certificate is absent.

Backup and archive references are distinct identity classes. `BackupSourceIdentity<T> {source_authority_domain:ConsensusDomain,source_cluster_incarnation,object_kind,object_id,canonical_digest}` is nonretaining evidence and is never accepted by local or remote mark traversal. `BackupArchiveSubject<T>` is the closed union `SourceObject{expected_source:BackupSourceIdentity<T>}|PublicationEnvelope{backup_id,publication_bundle_id,artifact_kind:ManifestBody|ManifestSignatureSet|Manifest|PublicationReceipt|TransparencyInclusion,expected_canonical_digest}`; generated type/kind rows make, for example, `PublicationEnvelope::Manifest` legal only for `T=BackupManifest`. `BackupArchiveRef<T> {backup_id,archive_authority_id,content_archive_inventory_root_digest,publication_bundle_id?,inventory_key,subject:BackupArchiveSubject<T>,archived_byte_digest,archived_length,protection_profile,required_recovery_proof_class}` resolves only through a current matching archive-retention grant. Live source objects use `SourceObject`; the newly constructed publication envelope uses `PublicationEnvelope` and never fabricates a source-database identity.

`BackupManifestBody` is `{backup_id,database_id,database_security_namespace_id,source_cluster_incarnation,source_posture:Local|Sharded,barrier,backup_state:BackupState,exact_logical_commit_base_and_anti_rollback_ranges,content_archive_inventory_root_digest,content_archive_inventory_count,branch_checkpoint_history_prepared_certificate_key_derived_trust_continuity_cursor_delivery_replay_inventories,object_id_key_escrow_policy,recipient_policy,format_matrix,canonical_semantic_digest,trust_policy,transparency_policy:NotRequired{policy_digest}|Required{log_id,minimum_checkpoint_policy_oid},prior_transparency_checkpoint?}`. The content inventory and every `SourceObject` archive ref exist first and exclude every publication-envelope object. `BackupManifestSignatureSet` is `{body_ref:StrongRef<BackupManifestBody>,body_digest,signature_policy_oid,signer_set_epoch,configuration_chain_digest,canonical_sorted_signers[{signer_id,signing_key_id,key_epoch}],threshold,canonical_signing_transcript_digest,canonical_signature_set}`; the transcript binds the complete body bytes/digest and signer identities/keys/epochs. `BackupManifest` is exactly `{body_ref:StrongRef<BackupManifestBody>,signature_set_ref:StrongRef<BackupManifestSignatureSet>,body_digest,signature_set_digest,manifest_format_major,manifest_format_minor}` and contains no self digest, receipt, inclusion, grant, or reopen proof. Its canonical digest is computed only after encoding and becomes a later object's field.

`BackupPublicationReceipt` is the portable externally signed `{backup_id,publication_bundle_id,archive_authority_id,manifest_canonical_digest,manifest_body_digest,manifest_signature_set_digest,content_archive_inventory_root_digest,content_archive_inventory_count,publication_envelope_locations_and_byte_digests[{artifact_kind:ManifestBody|ManifestSignatureSet|Manifest,authenticated_locator,canonical_digest,length}],content_inventory_durability_commitment,publication_generation,archive_monotonic_counter,published_at,time_authority_profile_oid,signer_set_epoch,signature}`. It contains no local `StrongRef`; its transcript covers every field except `signature`, and exact retry returns the same generation/bytes. `BackupTransparencyInclusion` is the later portable `{backup_id,publication_bundle_id,publication_receipt_digest,manifest_canonical_digest,log_id,leaf_index,tree_size,root_hash,inclusion_path,checkpoint_bytes,checkpoint_signatures,cross_log_consistency_evidence?,included_at,time_authority_profile_oid}` and verifies the body-declared policy and prior checkpoint. A NotRequired body makes this object illegal; a Required body makes a valid inclusion mandatory before the grant below.

`ArchiveRetentionGrant` is the immutable successor record `{backup_id,publication_bundle_id,archive_authority_id,grant_id,generation,predecessor_grant_digest:WeakDigest?,subject_set:{content_archive_inventory_root_digest,content_archive_inventory_count,manifest_body_digest,manifest_signature_set_digest,manifest_canonical_digest,publication_receipt_digest,transparency:NotRequired{policy_digest}|Included{inclusion_digest,checkpoint_digest}},permitted_recovery_and_reader_authority_digest,minimum_retain_through,maximum_lease_through,renewal_policy_oid,time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expires_at,archive_monotonic_counter,status:Active|Revoked{authorized_reason,revocation_evidence_digest}|Expired{time_evidence_digest},signer_set_epoch,signature}`. The subject set excludes the grant itself. Generation one has no predecessor; renewal preserves every subject and increments generation/counter with checked arithmetic. Early revoke before `minimum_retain_through` requires the manifest-declared exceptional authority and cannot claim deletion; expiry/revocation only makes resolution fail closed. Source-pin release requires an `Active` grant whose usable window and minimum-retention promise cover the publication contract. Construction is exactly `content inventory -> BackupManifestBody -> BackupManifestSignatureSet -> BackupManifest -> BackupPublicationReceipt -> required BackupTransparencyInclusion -> Active ArchiveRetentionGrant -> BackupArtifactReopenProof`; no object contains its own digest or a future receipt/signature/inclusion/grant/proof. A released manifest contains only source identities and archive refs, never a live source `StrongRef` or CRSR.

Grant freshness is externally linearized. `ArchiveGrantAuthorityHead` is the archive authority's CAS chain `{archive_authority_id,grant_id,cas_version,current_generation,current_grant_digest,current_status:Active|Revoked|Expired,current_subject_set_digest,archive_monotonic_counter,active_source_release_hold:None|Prepared{hold_id,backup_id,release_generation,participant_set_digest,expires_at}|Activated{hold_id,backup_id,release_generation,participant_set_digest,activated_counter},predecessor_head_digest,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`. A successor generation, revoke, expire, hold prepare/activate, or hold complete must name the direct predecessor; no skip/fork is valid. While an Activated hold exists, the authority rejects revoke/expire/subject removal and retains the complete subject set. `ArchiveGrantAuthorityObservation` is the challenged signed `{archive_authority_id,grant_id,current_head_digest,current_cas_version,current_generation,current_grant_digest,current_status,current_subject_set_digest,archive_monotonic_counter,active_source_release_hold_projection,intended_action:ArtifactReopen|ArtifactVerify|LocalSourcePinRelease|GlobalSourceReleaseAuthorize|ShardSourcePinRelease{shard_id}|GlobalSourceReleaseFinalize,action_subject_digest,challenge_nonce,authority_tick,time_observation_ref:StrongRef<TimeAuthorityObservation>,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`. Presentation creates a linear `ArchiveGrantUseGuard` only from this exact current observation plus action-bound `TimeValidationEvidence::Usable`; a stale generation/head, different action/subject, non-Active status, absent/mismatched activated hold for a release action, or profile/window failure rejects.

`ArchiveSourceReleaseHold` is the portable `{archive_authority_id,grant_id,backup_id,hold_id,release_generation,participant_set_digest,state:Prepared{time_authority_profile_oid,not_before,expires_at}|Activated{activation_head_digest,activation_cas_version,activation_counter,no_time_based_release:true}|Completed{completion_receipt_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveSourceReleaseCompletionReceipt>,completion_head_digest,completion_counter},subject_set_digest,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}` projection of the matching head and release contract. Local release prepares and activates a hold for participant set `{Local}` before ordering its pin release. Meta does the same for the exact Meta-plus-shard set before `GlobalBackupReleaseAuthorizeSpec`; activation is externally durable before any shard can see authorization. Prepared holds may expire only before activation and before any pin release. Activated holds have no time-based escape hatch: they complete only after the exact Local source-release record or Global source-release record plus every shard acknowledgement is presented to the archive authority. Crash, timeout, or partial release therefore retains the artifact while recovery completes the same release generation.

`ArchiveSourceReleaseEvidence` is the closed portable union `Local{backup_id,release_generation,local_release_applied_identity,post_release_root_identity,no_source_pin_proof_digest,audit_release_evidence,role_signatures}|Sharded{backup_id,release_generation,meta_release_applied_identity,post_release_global_root_identity,meta_no_source_pin_proof_digest,exact_sorted_shard_release_acks[PortableShardBackupReleaseAck],complete_participant_bijection_digest,audit_release_evidence,meta_signatures}`. It contains no Local/Meta/Shard `StrongRef` or CRSR. The archive authority verifies the hold, subject, exact participant set, role/configuration signatures, audit release, and source-pin absence, CASes the direct Activated head to Completed, and emits `ArchiveSourceReleaseCompletionReceipt {archive_authority_id,grant_id,backup_id,hold_id,release_generation,activated_head_digest,completion_head_digest,completion_cas_version,completion_counter,source_release_evidence_digest,participant_set_digest,subject_set_digest,completed_at,time_authority_profile_oid,signer_set_epoch,threshold_signatures}`. Exact retry returns identical bytes; a different evidence set, partial participants, stale head, or competing generation fails.

`ArchiveSourceReleaseCompletionMirrorSpec {backup_id,expected_registry_state:ReleasedPendingArchiveHoldCompletion,activated_hold_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveSourceReleaseHold>,completion_receipt_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveSourceReleaseCompletionReceipt>,completed_hold_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveSourceReleaseHold>,expected_prior_grant_mirror_digest,current_completed_head_observation_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveGrantAuthorityObservation>,time_validation_evidence_ref:StrongRef<TimeValidationEvidence>,terminal_audit_gate}` is the only ordered transition to compact `Released`. It byte-matches the direct CAS successor and creates the completed `ArchiveGrantAuthorityMirror`. Until this command and its audit mirror exist, checkpoint/backup/GC floors retain the release evidence, all shard acknowledgements, Activated hold, observation, and artifact. Only a later activated cut may replace that heavy closure with the compact completed receipt/hold/grant identities.

`ArchiveGrantAuthorityMirror` is the immutable local `{archive_authority_id,grant_id,mirrored_head_digest,mirrored_cas_version,mirrored_generation,mirrored_grant_digest,mirrored_status,mirrored_subject_set_digest,mirrored_archive_counter,mirrored_release_hold_projection?,source_observation_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveGrantAuthorityObservation>,source_time_validation_evidence_ref:StrongRef<TimeValidationEvidence>,predecessor_mirror_digest:WeakDigest?,continuity_status:DirectSuccessor|PermanentGap}`. `ArchiveGrantAuthorityMirrorSpec {backup_id,expected_backup_registry_generation,expected_prior_mirror_digest:WeakDigest?,authority_observation_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveGrantAuthorityObservation>,time_validation_evidence_ref:StrongRef<TimeValidationEvidence>,expected_direct_successor_or_genesis,current_grant_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveRetentionGrant>,hold_ref:StrongRef<ArchiveSourceReleaseHold>?,terminal_audit_gate}` orders each relied-on head/observation/hold transition into the role-valid backup registry. Apply accepts genesis or the exact direct successor, rejects rollback/fork/skip unless the archive authority supplies a separately audited permanent-gap reconciliation, and creates the mirror; exact retry is idempotent. Artifact verification retains its observation/time evidence, while every pin-releasing order obtains a new current observation under the activated hold.

Backup proof and pin vocabularies are closed. `BackupPinnedClosureRef<Role>` is the generated tagged union of `RegisteredStrongRef` arms legal for the exact Local, Meta, or Shard source-payload schema; every value carries its `source_slot_tag`, and the associated coverage bitmap must equal every live mandatory-inventory class at the barrier exactly once.
