No frame or state row ships without its exact generated wire tag, authorization/release rule, size bound, retry rule, and negative transition fixture.

## Appendix E — Working Bibliography (anchors reviewed for this plan)

Storage: Sortledton (PVLDB 15(6), 2022) · Teseo (PVLDB 14(6), 2021) · LiveGraph (PVLDB 13(7), 2020) · Aspen (PLDI 2019) · GraphOne (FAST 2019) · GTX / Spruce / RapidStore (2024–25) · RadixGraph (2026) · "Revisiting In-Memory Dynamic Graph Storage" (2025) · Dostoevsky/Fluid LSM (Dayan & Idreos, SIGMOD 2018) · S3-FIFO (Yang et al., SOSP 2023) · SuRF (Zhang et al., SIGMOD 2018). Processing: Kùzu (CIDR 2023) + "Columnar Storage and List-based Processing" (PVLDB 14(11)) + A+ Indexes · NPRR/AGM & Leapfrog Triejoin · EmptyHeaded (SIGMOD 2016) · Free Join (SIGMOD 2023) · ADOPT (2023) · HoneyComb (2025) · Umbra (CIDR 2020) · LeanStore · morsel-driven parallelism (SIGMOD 2014) · SPJM converged optimization (2024). Incremental: DBSP (PVLDB 16 / VLDBJ 2025, Lean-formalized; Feldera) · Differential/Timely Dataflow · streaming-graph SGQ work. Temporal: AeonG (PVLDB 17(6), 2024; VLDBJ 2025) · SQL:2011 system time · T-GQL, Clock-G. Languages: ISO/IEC 39075:2024 (GQL) · ISO/IEC 9075-16:2023 (SQL/PGQ) · GQL/PGQ pattern-matching & expressive-power papers · path-multiset representations (Martens et al.) · openCypher TCK. Vector: HNSW (Malkov & Yashunin) · DiskANN/Vamana · 2025–26 fresh-ANN and disaggregated-HNSW literature. Verification: FoundationDB simulation testing · Elle (Kingsbury & Alvaro) · Cahill/Fekete SSI · Serial Safety Net (Wang et al.) · asupersync formal-semantics & proof-lane artifacts. Distributed alternatives (evaluated, not adopted — §3.4, §14): Weaver refinable timestamps · G-Tran RDMA MV-OCC. Calibration & sequential statistics (§15.0): conformal prediction (Vovk, Gammerman & Shafer) and conformal risk control · game-theoretic probability, e-processes & anytime-valid inference (Shafer & Vovk; Ramdas, Grünwald, Vovk & Shafer; Ville 1939) · Wald's SPRT (1945) · Shiryaev–Roberts change detection · Bayesian online changepoint detection (Adams & MacKay 2007) · empirical Bayes / James–Stein (Robbins; Efron & Morris) · Good–Turing (1953) · robust estimation (Huber; Catoni 2012) · off-policy evaluation (Dudík, Langford & Li 2011) · learning-augmented algorithms (Lykouris & Vassilvitskii 2018). Control & operations (§16.6): CVaR (Rockafellar & Uryasev 2000) · extreme value theory / POT-GPD (Pickands 1975) · network calculus (Le Boudec & Thiran 2001) · max-plus algebra (Baccelli et al.) · Kingman's bound; Little's law · submodular maximization (Nemhauser, Wolsey & Fisher 1978; Krause & Golovin) · critical slowing down / early-warning signals (Scheffer et al. 2009). Consistency & distribution (§7.4, §14): CALM (Hellerstein & Alvaro, CACM 2020) · Red–Blue consistency (Li et al., OSDI 2012) · escrow transactions (O'Neil 1986) · SWIM (Das, Gupta & Motivala 2002) + Lifeguard (Dadgar et al. 2018) · closed timestamps (CockroachDB) · hybrid logical clocks (Kulkarni et al. 2014) · Merkle anti-entropy (DeCandia et al., Dynamo 2007) · consistent hashing with bounded loads (Mirrokni et al. 2016) · optimal transport (Villani; Cuturi's Sinkhorn 2013). Verifiability (§5.8): Certificate Transparency (Laurie; RFC 6962) · Merkle Mountain Ranges (Todd/opentimestamps lineage) · authenticated data structures (Merkle; Miller et al.) · PDP (Ateniese et al. 2007) / PoR (Juels & Kaliski 2007) · MTTDL Markov reliability models (Patterson et al. RAID lineage) · misuse-resistant AEAD/SIV (Rogaway & Shrimpton 2006) · differential privacy (Dwork et al. 2006; Rényi accounting, Mironov 2017; smooth sensitivity, Nissim, Raskhodnikova & Smith 2007). Verification methodology (§15): lineage-driven fault injection (Alvaro, Rosen & Hellerstein, SIGMOD 2015) · delta debugging (Zeller & Hildebrandt 2002) · record/replay of nondeterminism boundaries (rr; Mozilla) · provenance semirings (Green, Karvounarakis & Tannen, PODS 2007) · persistent union-find (Conchon & Filliâtre 2007) and offline dynamic connectivity (segment-tree-over-time folklore). Executor engineering (§8.7): AMAC (Kocberber, Falsafi & Grot, PVLDB 2015) · radix hash joins (Balkesen et al., ICDE 2013) · tail at scale hedging (Dean & Barroso, CACM 2013). Benchmarks: LDBC SNB / Graphalytics / FinBench. Market context (2026): GQL adoption in Spanner Graph & Fabric; Kùzu wind-down and forks; GraphRAG/agent-memory adoption analyses and their governance/freshness gap findings.

## Appendix F — Invariant and Evidence Registries

This table contains exactly twenty top-level invariant IDs. G0 materializes each row as one or more stable subordinate clause records in `invariants.toml`; subordinate clause keys do not create additional invariant IDs. Every clause records its exact statement, activation predicate, dependencies, resolvable enforcement and negative-test entrypoints, model/proof scope or liveness fairness assumptions, owner, first gate, status, and `waiver=forbidden`. CI verifies the twenty-ID/table hash, dependency DAG, checker/test existence, and the compiled-plus-negotiated activation closure. Every reachable clause must be live; otherwise the corresponding capability is absent. Statistical, configuration-model, and empirical claims remain in their separate registries.

| ID | Invariant | Enforcement |
|---|---|---|
| FG-INV-01 | Within one database security namespace/incarnation and outcome-capability domain, a durable token maps to at most one immutable semantic terminal outcome and final-effect digest; matching retries return the recorded value, conflicting transitions fail, Commit has exactly one marker, and Abort or ReadClosed can never later Commit. Local submission/abort/commit uses the exact predecessor CAS. W12 first reserves the scoped begin key and outcome capability durably; the begin index moves exactly `Reserved -> Bound(registration)` or `NeverRegisteredDetailed -> NeverRegisteredCompacted`, and retries return that same lineage. `AttemptFamilyState` admits only generation-zero First, exact `prior+1` Successor after terminal-or-burn plus release/overlap proof, or byte-identical IdempotentRetry; at most one generation is Active or PrepareAdmitted and a token/begin key binds once. NeverRegistered is a durable capability outcome, not an attempt. Every registered attempt has one immutable semantic terminal, but client success/status becomes TerminalReady only after its typed postcondition bitmap is complete; detailed and compacted proof sources return byte-identical `TerminalPublicOutcome`. No shard creates or reverses the semantic outcome. | Local and Meta begin/family/token/attempt/outcome/completion-state CAS models; lost-BEGIN_ACCEPTED, concurrent reservation/first/successor/retry/burn/cancel/read-close/commit and TerminalPending-to-Ready tests; participant, leader-loss, crash, partition, compaction-summary, and capability-status oracle. |
| FG-INV-02 | For each exclusive block or constraint domain, at most one legal live owner exists; ownership and every successor/transfer are generation-fenced, so a stale, cancelled, or prior-configuration owner can neither mutate nor release the resource. | Lock/reservation/ownership-transfer model plus independent lock-table, fence-reuse, cancellation, takeover, and reconfiguration oracle. |
| FG-INV-03 | Every physical version chain is finite, acyclic, strictly newer-first by commit order, and every link remains within one owning object generation. | Lean chain model plus arena decode, generation-substitution, debug, property, and fuzz oracles. |
| FG-INV-04 | Visibility obeys snapshot high sequence, selected branch ancestry for each graph-reference role, create/retire and schema-coordinate rules, and own-write/workspace-overlay rules; two references to one branch at distinct heads never alias. Restored state remains unobservable while reconciliation, activation, visibility, or service preparation is hidden; only the role-valid receipt-first service finalize/open transition permits Operational access, and every session/request/forward/cursor/capability must match the current incarnation and service-visibility epoch. | Independent reference engine and Lean visibility model; historical-self-join, workspace read-your-writes, hidden-restore/direct-endpoint, stale-epoch, and Local/Meta/Shard visibility oracles. |
| FG-INV-05 | Every committed SERIALIZABLE history has an acyclic logical dependency graph, and dependency metadata remains until no overlapping attempt can add an edge. W12 Meta state contains every local, cross-shard, read-only, statement-workspace, positive/negative/gap/path `wr`, `ww`, and `rw` edge. Each statement publication atomically extends the cumulative witness/conflict state; ReadWrite admission and ReadOnly close name the exact statement/delivery/workspace frontier and independently recheck the complete graph; compaction removes detail only after overlap closure. | Independent local/global SCC and history oracle; statement-publication/admission/read-close/compaction interleavings; overlap-lifetime model and scoped Lean theorem. |
| FG-INV-06 | Every witness conservatively represents all logically relevant positive, negative, gap, early-stop, and path-cut observations, and refinement preserves them. W12 routing/coarsening, workspace overlays, shard transport, cumulative statement-witness union, and finalization preserve the same `concretization` and `may_affect` contracts; missing routing, prior-touched-shard overlay, support, or proof causes conservative failure, never a dropped edge. | Constructor/refinement/optimizer/partition/workspace transport proofs plus mutation-complete single-shard, multi-shard, and multi-statement small-model differential suites. |
| FG-INV-07 | The concrete durable strong/uncut-conditional graph is acyclic; every reference, registered transcript digest, and weak identity names already identified bytes, and every pre-order spec excludes its future result/root. Before receipt or order, D1 roots one exact closure under stable prepared ownership, whose successors preserve the base and strengthen current ownership. W12 read order is durable begin reservation -> atomic ticket claim and attempt/workspace-zero registration -> statement registration and distinct claim when applicable -> certified shard read/workspace bases -> fixed-point read routing and global read authorization/serialization -> buffered result and successor workspace -> Meta statement publication -> immediately succeeding Registered outcome rooting the latest workspace -> external CAS/mirror -> streaming, with terminal close naming the complete chain. W12 write order is registration/latest workspace -> effect bases and routing -> global authorization/resource/outcome/admission -> fragments and shard prepares -> constraint/serialization certificates -> signer-locked terminal audit bytes and Meta pre-command-base certificate -> global command/candidate -> external CAS/mirror -> decision certificate and publication -> shard decision apply -> audit-mirror projection -> post-mirror acknowledgements -> GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch and Meta publication -> TerminalReady public outcome. Cross-group ownership uses only certified remote wrappers; cancel/compaction closes result, workspace, and remote-grant obligations before release; timeout never releases prepared, certificate, audit, result, or retention ownership. | Generated kind/field/reference/DAG/transcript/role checker; D1/D2 and Local/Meta/Shard Raft models; begin/read/write DAG, signer-lock, audit-extension, cancellation, compaction, crash, reconfiguration, and remote-retention oracles. |
| FG-INV-08 | Logical-command predecessor order and the transaction-marker subsequence are contiguous at their respective sequences; every retained checkpoint suffix begins with its exact install command; every role-tagged Raft snapshot matches the exact root/configuration/sequences at its cut; every branch-head CAS and parent link is valid. An operational checkpoint installs a `ProvisionalRetentionCutSet` that may authenticate bytes already absent under inherited activated coverage but cannot authorize new physical reclamation or release; replacement provisional coverage dominates every absorbed activated absence until its own activation command, and only Activated supports new reclamation. Fresh sharded Genesis and Local activation use their registered first Meta/Shard entries and barriers without a mixed-role chain. W12 semantic sequence/HLC/heads come only from Meta and every shard advances or proves irrelevance through one contiguous prefix. Transparency grades remain distinct; non-equivocation requires the named fresh policy, valid distinct keys, durable witnesses, verified extensions, `2t > n+f`, and old-plus-new thresholds during rotation. | Two-sequence and exact-cut oracles; all-role checkpoint install/replace/activate tests beginning with old bytes absent; activation/barrier/global-prefix models; command/marker/MMR and witnessed-transparency split-view tests. |
| FG-INV-09 | Full ObjectId equals canonical plaintext; CiphertextId, EncodingId, and non-self-referential PlacementId equal their complete registered descriptors and bytes/inventory; root bootstrap reproduces them without indexes; metadata-child keys unwrap only under the exact reconstructible noncircular AAD transcript; every symbol MAC covers its complete transcript; collisions are resolved and incompatible encodings never combine. Every stored digest is a registered Target, Transcript, WeakIdentity, or BodyDigest; a body digest uses its declared domain/schema/tag set and excludes exactly its own registered field unless the row explicitly says otherwise. | Full-digest/descriptor/AAD/body-transcript/root-bootstrap oracle; generated digest-recipe and field-table checker; mutation/golden/cross-version/collision/mixed-symbol/FEC-wire fuzz campaigns. |
| FG-INV-10 | Under the accepted filesystem/crash profile, publication leaves a highest structurally credible slot with authentic role closure, exact writer and incarnation-continuity fencing, and complete durable/applied/visible/service positions. Before an ordinary token, only PendingFenceGuard may publish the state-preserving takeover root, PendingCreationGuard the exclusive fresh Genesis install, and PendingRestoreCreationGuard the one non-Genesis RecoveryReconciling bridge; none can express ordinary work or service. Every irreversible seal, prepared update, receipt, Raft action, certificate, and RootSlot publication rechecks both inode/fence authority and the current continuity lease/CAS. Fresh creation alone follows Genesis -> CheckpointInstalled -> Operational; restore remains hidden until receipt-first role finalize/open. Checkpoint vectors classify every role payload field without predecessor-floor cycles. `RootManifest::RetiredLocal` contains no semantic/prepared/Raft/fence/service roots and always rejects ordinary open, resurrection, receipt, Raft, or advertisement. Closure failure repairs or fails closed, never rolls back implicitly. | Filesystem/lease/takeover/creation/restore-guard type model; external-CAS split-brain and stale-service-epoch tests; all-role checkpoint/floor coverage; every-write/fsync-lie/path-replacement/rollback/hidden-open/RetiredLocal crash matrices. |
| FG-INV-11 | Externally monotonic allocation epochs and canonical allocator/range state prevent VId/EId alias, overlap, or reuse across crash, label change, branch, merge, clone, same-identity restore, topology movement, and role activation. Canonical forward incidence, stable IDs, origin/birth and branch-admission orders, membership, properties, ordinal maps, and branch-aware holes agree; every declared reverse materialization equals forward truth, and its absence invokes the exact fallback. | External-continuity CAS and allocator crash/restore/branch/merge/topology model; reference graph after every operation; forward/reverse-present/reverse-absent compaction/label/map metamorphics. |
| FG-INV-12 | Canonical scalar equality, hashing, ordering, and encoding are coherent. Every claimed answer-equivalent transition, including seal, compaction, codec switch, spill, factorize/flatten, workspace materialization, and safe replan, preserves logical value, multiplicity, order, visibility, and AnswerContract; exact rebuild preserves exact contents, while approximate topology/candidate changes create a new pinned semantic generation. | Scalar-law property/fuzz suite; digest/reference and workspace equivalence; answer-contract/type checker; exact-rebuild and approximate-generation metamorphic suites. |
| FG-INV-13 | Commits are immutable and branch heads move only by atomic expected-head updates. Fork closes the parent envelope/write epochs before opening independent parent/child successors; every envelope, object-DEK, grant, and wrap is bound to one authenticated root/cut/epoch. In W12, Meta first orders a certificate-free key distribution plan, each shard installs unusable Staged material and certifies it, Meta activates exactly one complete manifest, and only the matching typed shard projection makes material Active; Staged material cannot serve reads/effects/prepares or active backup. Distributed destruction requires current-root zero-reference certificates, durable shard authorization, physical member/KMS receipts and completion from every planned Meta target and shard/range, then Meta completion; any new root invalidates the zero proof. Merge tokens/nonces/capability generations are pre-minted, each has one terminal outcome, imported-range coverage prevents partial or repeated application across drift/cuts/restore/reconfiguration, and effects obey proved ACI algebra or their recorded total order. | Branch/fork/envelope/merge/imported-range and distributed-key phase models; cross-branch denial, wrong plan/manifest, stale-zero-basis, partial KMS, crash, retry, topology, and backup property tests. |
| FG-INV-14 | GC follows every registered strong and currently uncut conditional edge; only field-table weak/locator/observation tags are nonretaining, while provisional/activated cut strong references are followed. A live StrongCiphertextRef retains its exact ciphertext, opener, recoverable realizations, and certificate. A certified remote reference is nonlocal ownership and releases only through the six ordered two-sided transitions. No reachable or independently obligated object, effect, key, result, workspace, begin reservation/public-status proof, prepared/certificate/audit artifact, checkpoint/cut/floor, branch/envelope/grant, cursor/delivery/replay, backup/restore lease, continuity state, attempt/statement/conflict/compaction evidence, topology/migration, or retirement proof may be reclaimed or cryptographically destroyed. Provisional cuts never authorize new reclamation. W12 reclamation requires bounded preflight and global authorization, a current-root proof that the reclaim set is within authorized intersection and disjoint from reachability, a published no-resurrection quarantine, exact physical-member completion, and aggregate completion; missing participants remain PartialBlocking. Attempt compaction additionally requires every result ACK/release/independent-retention proof plus every local-overlay and remote-workspace-grant release; heavy evidence releases only after floor publication, audit mirror, and activated cut. Old Local closure releases only after authority transfer/adoption, retirement finalization, and the narrow RetiredLocal reclamation guard. | Generated reference/mandatory-inventory/remote-release/GC/key-destruction models; mark-then-resolve and quarantine/dedupe-resurrection oracles; provisional-cut, physical-partial, result/workspace, backup/restore, attempt-compaction, topology, and RetiredLocal storms. |
| FG-INV-15 | For every registered exact derivative, integrating ordered deltas equals batch evaluation. A retained local batch owns every payload and integrates each coordinate once. W12 transaction records never name future batches: after every exact post-mirror shard batch/ack, one acyclic GlobalLogicalDeltaBatch owns the complete certified set, and only its contiguous Meta publication advances Ripple. A result remains buffered until the owning GlobalStatementPublicationSpec or GlobalReadCloseSpec, exact audit CAS/mirror, and delivery lease. `ResultDeliveryOwner` is exactly TerminalRead, AutocommitWriteTerminal, or Statement; ACK and typed release are idempotent for all three, and autocommit uses the same transition. Prepare/read-close names the complete statement, delivery, workspace, and witness frontier. Public baseline/result/delta digests cover exact authorized schema/contract/canonical bytes and provenance, never keyed object IDs. Cursor generation and one tagged baseline-or-delta lease make create/ACK/rotate/lost-response/resume/reset/expiry idempotent, retain promised bytes, forbid delta before baseline ACK, and expose gaps. Derived reads respect coverage/contracts; hidden or future approximate nodes cannot affect authorized results. Detailed versus compacted status proof may change; public outcome bytes may not. | Derivative-vs-batch and post-decision-global-publish differential; statement/workspace/backpressure/mirror/terminal-and-statement-delivery tests; participant/frontier/DAG oracle; public-digest/cursor/lease/ACK-resume, status-equivalence, and answer-contract/index/ANN suites. |
| FG-INV-16 | No structured task, begin reservation, pin, scratch object, result/workspace/cursor/lease, prepared or receipted closure, privacy debit/tombstone/seed/result, audit ticket/claim/event/resolution/CAS/gap, resource charge, backup source pin, remote-retention transition, GC quarantine, restore-source lease, or TerminalPending postcondition is lost, duplicated, refunded, released, or exposed while obligated. Audit tickets move monotonically PendingUnclaimed -> Claimed(exact owner) -> Resolved; operation claim is atomic with registration, statement claims have distinct owners, and substitution/double claim is impossible. Once AuditTerminalAttemptRecord and AuditSignerLock reserve terminal bytes, crash, policy drift, timeout, or leader change cannot abandon or replace them. Candidate state/result remains hidden until the exact external successor and mirror. Result release uses only the closed ResultReleaseEvidence variants; generic session-death StrongRef is forbidden. Backup pins release only after independent reopen/publication/grant and ordered acknowledgements; restore source authority persists through target reopen, receipt-first service finalize/open, all operational acknowledgements, and completion. Under declared fairness/quorum/storage/network/continuity/resource assumptions, every obligation reaches one legal terminal or recoverable state. | asupersync leak/quiescence oracle; begin/ticket-claim/signer-lock/result-release race models; prepared/resource/delivery/DP/audit/backup/remote-release/GC/restore recovery tests; external-CAS conflict and bounded-liveness models. |
| FG-INV-17 | Rebase and branch merge execute under capability-stripped deterministic contexts pinned to IntentSemanticsOid; every semantic change regenerates final effects, workspace/read/write state, constraints, witnesses, logical deltas, and a new capsule before publication. | Type/capability boundaries; unavailable or wrong-semantics fail-closed tests; effect/workspace-digest oracle and forced-drift replay/property tests. |
| FG-INV-18 | Base graph semantics and constraints remain authoritative: canonical committed effects equal the logical before/after change, workspace finalization equals the ordered published statement effects, constraint writes cannot commit without synchronous enforcement, and rebuildable indexes/views/caches may be discarded without changing answers. | Reference-effect/workspace differential; synchronous-constraint oracle; degraded-recovery and derived-state rebuild drills. |
| FG-INV-19 | A registry-rooted replay manifest derives its structural maximum only from its versioned evidence-slot matrix, and its effective grade may only weaken as leases, resolution, trust, configuration, or authority change. Replayable requires every semantic slot, including answer requirement, realized contract, authority, external inputs, executable artifacts, decisions, workspace-affecting statements, and exact approximate generations, to resolve through exactly LocalStrong, live CertifiedRemote, or active Archived evidence and reproduce canonical logical output. Sharded replay is no stronger than its weakest required group; activation/legacy evidence uses certified transition wrappers, never raw old-group refs. Missing, redacted, revoked, expired, or untrusted evidence yields only the declared weaker grade. Answer-affecting and canonical-state policies are sequenced/pinned; proved physical equivalence cannot change strict output. | Cross-plan/target/artifact/workspace/approximation replay CI; generated slot-grade/local-remote-archive resolver and expiry/trust doctor; activation/posture-substitution tests and replica logical-digest oracle. |
| FG-INV-20 | Authorization precedes every observation or effect across storage, statistics, routing/scoring, workspace reads/writes, errors, constraints/witnesses/prepares, derived state, Prism/UDFs, streams, cross-session capabilities, replay/export/backup, audit, and observability. Local ticket-only gates precede their event. In W12, registration atomically claims the operation ticket and each statement registration claims a distinct statement ticket; shard reads carry certified execution scope, workspace generation, imported permit projection and ticket/claim identities only, never raw Meta refs. Effect-only bases feed exactly one current union-wide global authorization decision; it does not consume or fabricate the later terminal event. Fragments/prepares bind registration, admission, claim, permit, workspace, and authorization. After certification, one signer-locked terminal event/resolution gates the Meta candidate; only its external CAS/mirror permits visibility, followed by decision publication, shard audit projection, and post-mirror acks. Statement publication has its own exact gate/mirror before streaming. A valid same-principal outcome capability returns exact BeginStaging/NeverRegistered/InProgress/TerminalPending/TerminalReady state; unauthorized or wrong-epoch lookup is uniformly nonrevealing and status cannot expose another authority domain. Structural lifecycle exceptions are closed typed cases. Hidden-state constraints obey one explicit disclosure contract; only named, ticketed, audited declassification is legal. | Unforgeable secure-view/permit-projection/gate/capability/aggregate types; raw-cross-group and wrong domain/config/grant/owner golden negatives; double-claim, omitted-participant, workspace-substitution, status noninterference, pre-mirror observation/ack, declassification, and continuity matrices. |

### Statistical, evidence, and configuration gates (not invariants)

| ID | Qualified claim | Required disclosure/gate |
|---|---|---|
| FG-CAL-01 | Adaptive policy evidence versus pinned fallback | null/outcome filtration, alpha, support/overlap, effective sample size, loss and fallback; stream-sequenced promotion only |
| FG-CAL-02 | Cardinality/risk interval coverage | population, selection/window, exchangeability or nonexchangeability method, strata, marginal target, realized coverage and drift |
| FG-CAL-03 | ANN recall/drift evidence | authorized snapshot population, keyed sample, exact baseline, candidate policy, confidence interval and rebuild action |
| FG-EVID-01 | Decision-card/OPE completeness | state/actions/features, logged probabilities, zero-support exclusions, clipping/estimator, policy epoch and fallback |
| FG-EVID-02 | Scrub/corpus-health evidence | population, keyed stratified sampling, dependence assumptions, exhaustive-sweep position and observed corruption |
| FG-CFG-01 | Modeled durability target | CTMC/model version, fitted failure rates, failure domains, sensitivity bounds, repair/backup assumptions |
| FG-CFG-02 | Modeled controller stability | model/equilibrium, parameter uncertainty, predicted margin, deterministic hard guards and soak results |
| FG-CFG-03 | View/index staleness SLO feasibility | arrival/service assumptions, resource reservation, predicted envelope, actual watermark and fallback policy |

---

*Fin. The graph database the 2030s deserve, built from parts the 2020s already proved — ours.*
